Why: Cards expire and bank accounts change. A plan owner who cannot update their payment method is a plan owner whose next installment will return — a situation entirely preventable with a simple self-service update.

Agreement Change History. Every change to a payment plan agreement — balance adjustments, payment method changes, installment reschedules, plan cancellations, return events — must be recorded in a timestamped change history visible to the plan owner in the consumer portal and to institution admins in the admin portal. Each entry must show: what changed, the actor (student, AP, institution admin, system), and the date/time.

Why: When a student calls and says "my plan amount changed and I don't know why," the change history is the answer. Without it, every balance change generates a support escalation that requires manual investigation.

Agreement Terms & Conditions. The plan owner must be able to access the full terms and conditions of their active agreement from the consumer portal at any time — not just at enrollment. The Ts&Cs displayed must be the exact version accepted at enrollment, stored immutably. If an institution updates its plan Ts&Cs, enrolled students continue to operate under the version they accepted.

Why: Plan owners who need to reference their agreement terms must not have to call the bursar or search their email. On-demand access to the exact accepted version is a legal and trust requirement.

Consumer Plan Actions. Plan owners must be able to perform the following self-service actions directly from the portal: cancel their agreement (with confirmation and consequences disclosed), reschedule a single upcoming payment (within institution-configured rules), and initiate a request for NBS to refund or waive fees (routed as a service request to the appropriate institution or NBS contact). Payment Plan Invites (hidden plans, see Hidden Plans section) are initiated by the institution admin — not the student.

Why: Self-service for routine plan actions eliminates the most common support contacts (rescheduling a payment, understanding fees) and gives plan owners a sense of control that increases plan completion rates.

Institution Plan Servicing

Cancel a Plan. Institution admins (and NBS Support Managers) must be able to cancel any active payment plan agreement. Cancellation immediately stops all scheduled future installments, updates the SIS flag to reflect plan termination, and triggers a notification to the plan owner. All cancellations are logged in the Agreement Change History with the acting user's identity, timestamp, and reason code.

Why: Institutions encounter scenarios that require plan cancellation independent of student action: enrollment cancellation, institutional error, hardship waiver. Admin-initiated cancellation must be a first-class supported workflow.

Reschedule an Installment. Institution staff (all CSR levels and above) must be able to reschedule any upcoming installment on an active plan to a different date, within institution-configured date constraints. Rescheduling a payment must recalculate the payment schedule and log the change. This action is available to all support roles because it is a routine service request that should not require manager escalation.

Why: The most common plan-related support call is "can you move my payment date?" Restricting this to high-privilege roles would create an unnecessary bottleneck in the support queue and frustrate students with an easily resolvable request.

Duplicate a Plan Offer. Institution admins must be able to duplicate an existing plan offer configuration as the starting point for a new offer. The duplicated offer is saved as a draft and can be modified before publishing. This eliminates the need to reconfigure common settings (eligibility rules, installment count, return policy) from scratch when creating a similar plan for a new term.

Why: Institutions create similar plan configurations each term. A duplicate function reduces configuration time and the risk of misconfiguration from manual re-entry.

Past Due Arrangements — Additional Configuration. For past-due plan types, institution admins must be able to configure: weekly payment schedules (in addition to monthly), collection for institution-defined fee types (late fees, service fees specific to the institution's billing structure), balance amount type (how the past-due balance is calculated — outstanding balance only, or total account balance), and the ability to cancel a plan that has an invalid or expired payment method on file before the next payment attempt occurs.

Why: Past-due arrangements involve students in more precarious financial situations. Weekly schedules and more granular balance configuration give institutions the flexibility to structure arrangements that the student can realistically honor — increasing recovery rates vs. a one-size-fits-all monthly plan.

Pay Over Time

Standard Plans

Standard pay over time plans are the core pay over time product — auto-debit, term-based, offered to enrolled students with current-term balances. All other payment plan types (LTPP, International, Guarantee, Hidden, Custom) are variants that share this base or differ explicitly from it.

Term-Based Enrollment Window. Standard plans must be configured per term with an enrollment open date and enrollment close date. Students may only enroll during this window. The window is configured by the institution admin in the Horizon admin portal and may differ by term, campus, or student population segment.

Why: Institutions need control over when payment plans are available to prevent students from enrolling in plans after charges are nearly paid or too late in the term to spread meaningfully. The enrollment window is also tied to the institution's financial reporting cycles.

Auto-Debit Authorization. Enrollment in a standard plan requires the student to authorize automatic debits from a saved payment method (bank account or card) on the plan's scheduled due dates. The student must explicitly accept the auto-debit terms during plan enrollment. No manual payment step is required for each installment.

Why: Auto-debit is the core value proposition of Nelnet's payment plan product — it removes the burden of remembering to pay each installment and reduces non-payment rates vs. invoice-based plans. It also reduces institution administrative overhead compared to manually-managed plans.

Installment Schedule Options. Institutions must be able to configure the number of installments available for each term (e.g., 2-month, 3-month, 4-month, 5-month options). The plan amount is divided evenly across installments after any down payment. The student selects their preferred schedule at enrollment.

Why: Different institutions and students have different payment capacity. A student at a school with a $5,000/term balance may need 5 payments of $1,000; a student at a $2,000/term program may only need 2. Offering multiple schedule options increases plan adoption by letting students choose the installment size that fits their cash flow.

Down Payment Configuration. Institutions may optionally require a down payment at plan enrollment. The down payment amount or percentage must be configurable. The first installment may serve as the down payment, or the down payment may be collected separately at enrollment with subsequent installments beginning after.

Why: Down payments reduce the institution's exposure if a student defaults on the plan immediately after enrolling. Some institutions require them; others do not. Configurability is required to match institutional policy.

Balance Eligibility. The institution must be able to configure a minimum balance required to enroll in a payment plan (e.g., students with less than $100 outstanding may not enroll). The plan must be calculated on the student's unpaid balance at time of enrollment after financial aid has been applied.

Why: Payment plans with very small balances have higher overhead (transaction fees, customer service) relative to their value. A minimum balance threshold protects profitability and avoids confusion for students who effectively have no meaningful balance to spread.

One Plan Per Student Per Term. A student may only be on one active standard payment plan per term. The system must prevent duplicate standard plan enrollment for the same term. If a student's balance changes significantly after enrollment, the plan may be adjusted (see Institution Process Flow — Mid-Term Account Changes) but a second plan cannot be opened.

Why: Multiple simultaneous plans for the same term balance create reconciliation complexity, confuse the student, and create financial reporting problems for the institution. The constraint is intentional and enforced by the system.

Plan Modification After Enrollment. After a student enrolls in a standard plan, only the payment method and (if institution-enabled) pausing can be changed by the student. Plan schedule, installment count, and end date cannot be modified by the student post-enrollment. If balance changes require plan recalculation, the system adjusts the installment amount or end date according to the student's previously selected balance-change preference (see Balance Change Handling).

Why: Allowing arbitrary mid-plan changes creates reconciliation complexity and potential for abuse (e.g., reducing a payment right before it's due). Constraining changes to payment method and pausing keeps the plan predictable while still accommodating the most common legitimate need.

Institution-Initiated Plan Cancellation. Institution admins can cancel any active plan on behalf of a student. On cancellation: auto-debit is immediately stopped, the student is notified with the remaining balance now due, and the original receivable is restored to the institution's SIS. Cancellation reason is logged and visible in the plan record.

Why: Institutions occasionally need to cancel plans for non-payment-related reasons (enrollment cancellation, institutional error, hardship waiver). Admin-initiated cancellation must be available without requiring student action.

Plan Completion Confirmation. When the final installment on a plan is successfully processed, the student receives a "Plan complete" notification showing: all installments paid, total amount paid, and a confirmation that the balance covered by this plan has been satisfied. The student portal updates to show no active plan for that term.

Why: Completion is a moment worth acknowledging. Students who receive clear confirmation are less likely to contact support asking "is my account settled?" It also builds trust in the auto-debit process.

Pay Over Time

Past-Due Plans

Past-due plans cover balances that have aged beyond the standard term payment window but are not large enough or old enough to qualify for LTPP. They bridge the gap between a missed standard plan and full LTPP eligibility. Duration is typically 2–6 months.

Eligibility: Aged Balance Without Active Plan. A student is eligible for a past-due plan when they have an outstanding balance from a prior term, are not currently on a payment plan for that balance, and the balance falls within the institution's configured past-due plan threshold (e.g., less than $5,000 and less than 6 months overdue). Balances above the threshold route to LTPP eligibility.

Why: Past-due plans give institutions a middle option between the standard plan (for current students, term-based) and LTPP (for significant past-due balances, long duration). Without this tier, institutions have no structured offering for the student who missed a term payment but has a moderate balance that could be resolved in a few months.

Auto-Debit, Same Mechanic as Standard Plans. Past-due plans use the same auto-debit payment mechanic as standard plans. The student authorizes automatic debits at enrollment. This is distinct from LTPP only in duration and eligibility thresholds, not in payment mechanic.

Why: Consistency in payment mechanic across plan types reduces the student's learning curve and reduces engineering complexity. Past-due plans use the same infrastructure as standard plans; only configuration differs.

Late Fee Handling. The institution must be able to configure whether late fees pause while a student is on a past-due plan (same as LTPP behavior) or continue to accrue. Pausing late fees is a common incentive for the student to enroll in the plan rather than ignore the balance.

Why: If late fees continue to accrue during a past-due plan, the student's balance grows even as they make payments — this can undermine confidence in the plan and increase default rates. Pausing fees is a meaningful incentive that different institutions may choose to offer or not offer depending on their policy.

Sophie review needed Review the distinction between Past-Due Payment Plans and LTPP. The primary differentiators are duration (2–6 months vs. 12–36+ months) and balance threshold (lower vs. higher). Confirm whether these should be two separately configured plan types in the system or whether LTPP is a superset that handles both. If they are distinct, add requirements for: returned payment handling, plan termination, institution notification, and communications — following the same pattern as the LTPP section but with shorter-duration parameters.
Pay Over Time

Hidden Plans

Hidden plans are payment plan options that are not visible to the general student population. A student can only access a hidden plan if they receive a one-off invite from an institution admin. Used for special arrangements, exceptions, or plans offered to specific student cohorts.

Admin-Only Creation and Invitation. Hidden plans must not be visible in the standard plan enrollment flow. An institution admin must create the plan (with specific terms: schedule, amount, dates) and explicitly invite a specific student to it. The invitation is delivered to the student via email with a direct link to enroll in that specific hidden plan.

Why: Some students require individually negotiated payment arrangements that differ from the institution's standard plan options — different amounts, different timing, a specific exception granted by the bursar. These should not be visible to other students, should not require a separate agreement outside Horizon, and should be tracked in Horizon like any other plan.

Invitation Expiry. Hidden plan invitations must expire after a configurable number of days. If the student does not enroll before expiry, the invitation becomes invalid. The admin must be able to re-send or extend the invitation.

Why: An expired invitation that can still be accessed creates operational risk — the institution may have changed the student's status or terms after sending the invitation. Expiry ensures the admin remains in control of when the arrangement is still valid.

One-Time Use Invitation. Each hidden plan invitation is single-use. Once the student enrolls, the invitation link is consumed and cannot be reused. The plan can only be accessed through the student's active plan view after enrollment, not by re-clicking the invitation link.

Why: Prevents a student from sharing their invitation link with other students who then enroll in the same special arrangement. Also prevents accidental double-enrollment if the student clicks the link more than once.

Full Plan Mechanics Apply. Once enrolled, a hidden plan behaves like any other payment plan: auto-debit, plan status tracking, payment confirmation, returned payment handling, and plan termination follow standard plan rules. The "hidden" designation only affects discovery (student cannot find it without an invitation) — not plan behavior.

Why: Reusing standard plan mechanics for hidden plans minimizes the engineering surface area of the feature. The only unique behavior is the invitation and access control layer.

Sophie review needed Confirm the scope of hidden plans: Can they be term-based (like standard plans) or are they always custom schedule? Can an admin create a hidden plan for a student who already has an active standard plan? Can hidden plan terms differ from any institution-configured defaults (e.g., a zero-down-payment hidden plan at an institution that requires down payments)? Add any audit/reporting requirements for tracking which admin created each hidden plan invitation and when it was accepted.
Pay Over Time

Custom Plans

Custom plans give institution admins the ability to create a fully bespoke payment schedule for an individual student on the fly — specific payment dates, specific amounts, outside the standard installment templates. Used for highly individualized arrangements that standard and hidden plans cannot accommodate.

Admin-Created, Fully Bespoke Schedule. An institution admin must be able to create a custom plan by defining: the total plan amount, each individual payment date, and each individual payment amount. Payment amounts do not need to be equal. Payment dates do not need to follow a monthly schedule. The admin creates this directly in the Horizon admin portal for a specific student.

Why: Some student situations require payment arrangements that no templated schedule can accommodate — a student paying in large lump sums on employer reimbursement cycles, a student with an irregular income pattern, or a complex financial arrangement worked out with a financial aid advisor. Custom plans give the institution the flexibility to honor these arrangements within Horizon rather than managing them in a spreadsheet outside the system.

Student Notification and Enrollment Confirmation. When an admin creates a custom plan, the student must receive a notification with the plan details and must confirm/accept the plan before it becomes active. The student should be able to view the full schedule before accepting. After acceptance, the auto-debit authorization is established for each scheduled payment.

Why: The student must consent to the specific payment schedule and authorize each debit. A plan created entirely by the admin with no student confirmation would not satisfy the auto-debit authorization requirements and could create disputes if the student claims they didn't know about specific payment dates.

Partial Amount Custom Plans. A custom plan does not need to cover the student's entire outstanding balance. An admin may create a custom plan for a specific subset of the balance (e.g., a $2,000 custom plan for a student with a $5,000 balance, where the remaining $3,000 is being handled through financial aid or another process). The system must clearly show the student what balance is and is not covered by the custom plan.

Why: Complex financial situations often involve multiple sources of funds covering different portions of a balance. The custom plan may cover only the portion the student is personally responsible for while a scholarship, employer reimbursement, or pending appeal covers the rest.

Sophie review needed Clarify the relationship between custom plans and hidden plans — are they the same feature with different names, or are they distinct? The user described hidden plans as "one-off invite from admin" and custom plans as "create one-off plan for an individual student on the fly." If they are distinct: hidden plans may use standard installment amounts/dates but are invitation-only, while custom plans have fully bespoke amounts and dates. Confirm this distinction and add requirements for: plan modification after student acceptance, admin audit trail, reporting on custom plans (how are they included in institution reports?), and whether custom plans have the same returned payment and termination rules as standard plans.
Features · Account

Communication History

Every person interacting with a student account — the account holder, authorized parties, and institution staff — needs a clear, appropriately scoped view of communications. This section defines what each persona can see, what institution users can action, and the technical contract that governs message visibility and resendability across all outbound correspondence.

Consumer View — Student (Account Holder)

As a student

Full Account Communication History. The student must be able to view all communications associated with their account, including communications sent to authorized parties about their account. Each entry must display the communication type, recipient, sent timestamp, delivery status (delivered, failed, or pending), and a message preview when the communication is marked viewable.

Why: Students are the account holders of record and need full visibility into all outbound correspondence touching their account — including messages sent to parties acting on their behalf — so they can verify accuracy, follow up on failed deliveries, and maintain awareness of their account activity.

As a student

Rendered Message Preview. For any communication where isViewable is true, the student must be able to open a full preview rendering the message body as it was delivered, including any visible links or action buttons. For communications where isViewable is false, a placeholder reading "Content not viewable" must be shown in place of the message body; no partial body content may be exposed.

Why: Viewing the actual message body helps students confirm what was communicated on their behalf. Concealing sensitive one-time content (verification codes, invite tokens) prevents replay attacks and protects account security after those messages have served their purpose.

As a student

Communication History Filtering. The student must be able to filter their communication history by communication type (e.g., payment confirmation, invite, statement), date range, and delivery status. Filters must be combinable and must update the displayed list in real time without a full page reload.

Why: Students with long account histories or multiple authorized parties may have dozens of communications. Filtering by type, date, and status lets them quickly locate a specific message rather than scrolling through an unorganized list.

Consumer View — Authorized Party

As an authorized party

Scoped Communication History. An authorized party must only be able to view communications sent directly to their own email address. Communications sent to the student or to other APs about the student's account must not appear in the AP's communication history view. The same isViewable rendering rules that apply to students must apply to the AP's scoped view.

Why: APs may have limited or role-restricted access to account data. Surfacing communications addressed to other parties — including the student — could expose information the AP is not authorized to see, violating the access boundaries the student established when granting AP access.

As an authorized party

Delivery Status Visibility for AP Communications. The AP must be able to see the delivery status (delivered, failed, pending) for each communication in their scoped history. Where isViewable is true, the full rendered message body must be accessible. Failed delivery status must be displayed clearly so the AP understands that action may be needed.

Why: APs taking financial action on a student's account need confidence that time-sensitive communications they expected to receive were actually delivered. Failed delivery visibility helps them escalate to the institution or the student promptly.

Institution User View & Resend

As an institution user (CSR)

Full Communication History for Serviced Accounts. An institution user must be able to view the complete communication history for any student account they are servicing, including all communications sent to the student and to any authorized parties associated with that account. The same display format — type, recipient, timestamp, delivery status, and conditional message preview — must be present in the institution user view.

Why: CSRs handling support inquiries need to see the full communication record to answer questions like "Did we send the payment receipt?" or "Was the AP invite delivered?" Without a unified view across all recipients tied to the account, CSRs must piece together history from disconnected sources, increasing handle time and error risk.

As an institution user (CSR)

Resend Eligible Communications. For any communication where isResendable is true, the institution user must be presented with a resend action. Activating the resend action must deliver the communication to the original recipient's email address on file at the time of resend. Resending to a new or alternate email address is not supported. The system must log the resend event, including the institution user's identity and the timestamp of the resend action.

Why: Resend capability reduces the burden on students and APs who did not receive important but non-sensitive communications, such as payment confirmations. Restricting resend to the original address on file prevents misuse of the resend feature to redirect communications to unverified addresses.

Message Flags & Compliance

isViewable Flag Enforcement. Every communication record must carry an isViewable boolean flag set by the originating service at send time. When false, the system must substitute the message body with the placeholder "Content not viewable" for all roles — including institution users. No role may bypass this restriction. Communications subject to this rule include: verification codes, one-time passwords, time-sensitive authentication tokens, and registration invite links. The isViewable flag defaults to true if not explicitly set; it is the originating service's responsibility to set it to false for sensitive message types.

Why: Exposing one-time or time-sensitive security credentials after their use window creates a meaningful attack surface. Enforcing the flag at the display layer — regardless of role — ensures that even well-intentioned CSR access cannot inadvertently reveal credentials that could be replayed or misused.

isResendable Flag Enforcement. Every communication record must also carry an isResendable boolean flag. When false, no resend action may be surfaced in any UI role, and the resend API endpoint must reject requests for those records. Communications where isResendable must be false include: AP and guest payment invites (resend means create a new invite), password reset messages, recovery codes, and any communication containing an expiring link or token. The flag defaults to true; originating services set false for non-resendable types. This flag is not backfilled on prior emails — only new sends carry it.

Why: Resending an expired invite or a used password reset link would either fail silently or create user confusion. For invite-type communications, the correct workflow is to generate a new invite rather than resend an old one. Enforcing this at the system level prevents workarounds that could produce inconsistent behavior.

Technical Architecture

Required Identifiers on All Correspondence Events. Every service that sends email through the correspondence service must include the following identifiers with each send event: userId (the Passport user ID of the intended recipient), accountId (the account balance ID associated with the communication), and externalId (the institution's student ID). These identifiers are the keys the correspondence service uses to scope communication history records to the correct person and account. Incomplete events must be rejected and logged as errors in the originating service. Passport-related communications (password reset, account verification) are out of scope for the initial release and will be integrated in a subsequent phase.

Why: The student and AP communication history views depend entirely on the ability to scope records by recipient identity and account. Without consistent required identifiers on every event, the correspondence service cannot reliably attribute records to the correct person, making history retrieval inaccurate or incomplete.

Features · Account

Guest Payments

Guest payments allow authenticated account holders and institution staff to invite a third party — someone without a Horizon account — to make a one-time payment toward a student's balance. This section defines the invite workflow, the guest payer experience, validation boundaries, institution user capabilities, and the configuration and audit requirements that govern the feature.

Invite Workflow

As a student or authorized party

Guest Payment Invite Form. An authenticated student or authorized party must be able to initiate a guest payment invite by providing the recipient's email address and an optional personalized message. The invite form must display the invite's expiration date to the sender before submission so they understand the window within which the guest must act. The system must generate a unique, time-limited invite link and deliver it to the specified recipient email. The invite must appear in the student's communication history as isResendable=false — if a new invite is needed (e.g., after expiration), the student must create a new one rather than resending the old record.

Why: Students and APs often coordinate payments with family members or sponsors who are not account holders. Providing an invite form with clear expiration information ensures the sender can set appropriate expectations with the guest payer and take action if a new invite is needed after expiration.

As a guest payer

Guest Invite Email Content. The invite email must include: the optional custom message from the sender, institution branding consistent with the payment space configuration, the invite expiration date and time, and a prominent call-to-action link that routes the guest directly to the guest payment flow. No Horizon account creation prompt may appear in the invite email.

Why: Guest payers are typically unfamiliar with Horizon. A well-branded, clearly worded email with expiration context and a direct payment link reduces friction and drop-off, and sets accurate expectations about the payment window without creating confusion about account registration.

Guest Payment Experience

As a guest payer

Account-Free Payment Flow. A guest payer must be able to complete a payment by following the invite link without creating a Horizon account or authenticating. The guest payment flow must present: (1) entry of a payment amount within the allowed range; (2) entry of a new payment method — card or ACH only (Apple Pay and third-party wallets are not supported for guest payments); (3) a confirmation screen summarizing amount and payment method; and (4) a receipt delivered to the guest's email address after successful submission.

Why: Requiring account creation introduces significant friction for a one-time use case and drives payment abandonment. The guest flow must be optimized for a single session with no persistent identity, while the receipt provides proof of payment without needing account access.

As a student

Student Notification on Guest Payment Completion. When a guest payer successfully completes a payment, the student associated with the account must receive a notification confirming the guest payment, including the payment amount and date. Guest payer identity is tracked by the absence of a person ID in the transaction record — guests have no person ID, distinguishing them from student and AP payments in transaction history.

Why: The student is the account holder of record and needs to be aware of all payments applied to their balance — including those initiated by third parties — to maintain an accurate picture of their account status and detect any unexpected transactions.

Validation & Error Handling

As a guest payer

Payment Amount Validation. The guest payment flow must enforce a minimum and maximum payment amount. The maximum must be hard-capped at the current account balance; a guest payer must not be able to submit a payment that exceeds the outstanding balance. If the entered amount exceeds the balance, the system must display a clear inline validation error specifying the maximum allowable amount. The minimum payment amount must reflect any configuration set at the payment space level.

Why: Overpayments create reconciliation complexity and refund overhead. Enforcing a hard stop at the account balance with a clear, actionable error message prevents this problem class without requiring manual correction after the fact.

As a guest payer

Expired or Invalid Invite Link Handling. When a guest payer follows an invite link that has expired, already been used, or is otherwise invalid, the system must display a clear error message explaining that the link is no longer valid and instructing the guest to contact the person who sent the invite for a new one. The expired link error page must not expose any account details, student name, or balance information.

Why: Expired links are a predictable failure case, especially when guests delay acting on an invite. A clear, privacy-preserving error page prevents confusion, protects student account information from unauthenticated viewers, and directs the guest toward the correct resolution path.

Institution User Capabilities

As an institution user

Send Guest Payment Invite on Behalf of Student. An institution user must be able to initiate a guest payment invite on behalf of a student directly from the student's account view in the person dashboard. The invite form must include the same fields available to the student: recipient email and optional custom message. The expiration date must be displayed before sending. All invites sent by institution users must be logged with the institution user's identity in the audit trail. The invite must appear in the student's communication history, enabling the institution user to verify delivery.

Why: Students may request in-person or phone assistance when setting up a guest payment. Enabling institution users to send invites on the student's behalf extends the feature's utility to assisted service scenarios without requiring the student to be present at a terminal.

Configuration & Audit

Payment Space Configuration Gate. Guest payment functionality must be controlled by a payment space configuration toggle. When the feature is disabled for a payment space, the invite initiation UI must not be visible to any role — including students, APs, and institution users — for accounts within that space. The feature must be disabled by default and require explicit activation.

Why: Not all institutions will want to allow guest payments, and some may have compliance or policy constraints that prohibit third-party payments on student accounts. An opt-in configuration gate prevents unintended enablement across all payment spaces.

Features · Account

Assisted Payments

Assisted payments enable institution users to process payments on behalf of students and authorized parties — over the phone or in person — within a controlled, compliant workflow. This section defines supported payment methods, the authorization and disclosure requirements that must precede every transaction, receipt and notification behavior, and the audit, permissions, and configuration model that governs the feature.

Payment Methods & Scope

Supported Payment Methods by Channel. For in-person assisted payments, the only supported payment method is a physical card processed via a SRED swipe device. For phone-assisted payments, the institution user may accept either a card via a SRED device or a bank account (ACH). Apple Pay and third-party digital wallets must not be available in the assisted payment flow regardless of channel. The UI must only present payment method options valid for the active channel.

Why: SRED device card capture protects cardholder data by encrypting it at the point of swipe, ensuring the institution user never handles raw card numbers. Phone and in-person channels have distinct physical constraints that determine which methods are operable, and limiting the UI to valid options prevents errors and unsupported payment attempts.

No Saved Payment Methods and No Pay Over Time. Institution users must not be able to select or use a payer's saved payment methods during an assisted payment. Saved payment methods must not appear in the assisted payment UI, and no save option may be offered at any point. Additionally, Pay Over Time and payment plan enrollment options must be hidden from the institution user's view when in the assisted payment context — the workflow is scoped to one-time payment processing only. Institution users cannot enroll students or APs in payment plans on their behalf.

Why: Allowing institution users to access stored payment credentials raises security and consent concerns. Blocking plan enrollment during assisted payments preserves the integrity of the consent-driven plan enrollment process — enrolling a payer in a plan requires their informed agreement to plan terms, which is not operationalizable in the assisted payment workflow without additional legal scaffolding.

Scope Limited to Authenticated Students and Authorized Parties. Assisted payments may only be processed on behalf of authenticated students or APs with an established account relationship. Processing a payment on behalf of a guest payer is explicitly out of scope. The payer's person ID must be present in the payment session; if it is absent (as it would be for a guest), the system must block the assisted payment flow.

Why: The assisted payment workflow depends on a verified person identity to attribute the transaction correctly, generate a receipt, and notify the appropriate parties. Guest payers have no person ID, making it impossible to fulfill the audit and notification requirements of the feature.

Workflow & Authorization Confirmation

As an institution user

Required Disclosure and Authorization Confirmation. Before an assisted payment can be submitted, the institution user must be presented with the required compliance disclosure and authorization script applicable to the institution. The institution user must explicitly confirm — via a required checkbox or acknowledgment action — that verbal or written authorization was obtained from the payer before the submit action becomes available. The system must block payment submission if the authorization confirmation has not been completed.

Why: Processing a payment on behalf of someone else without documented confirmation of their authorization creates legal and compliance exposure for the institution. Requiring an explicit acknowledgment at the point of submission creates a consistent, auditable compliance gate that holds regardless of how the institution user was trained.

Receipt & Notification

Payer Receipt Delivery. Upon successful completion, a receipt must be sent to the payer — the student or AP on whose behalf the payment was made — at their email address on file. The receipt must include: payment amount, payment method type (masked), transaction timestamp, and a reference number. The receipt must not include the institution user's name or identity.

Why: The payer needs a record of the transaction for their own financial records regardless of who executed it. Omitting the institution user's identity from the receipt keeps the payer-facing communication clean and avoids confusion about transaction attribution.

Student Notification When AP Is the Assisted Payer. If the assisted payment is processed on behalf of an authorized party, the student must receive a payment notification in addition to the AP receiving their receipt. The notification must include the payment amount and date. It must not expose the AP's identity or payment method details to the student.

Why: The student is the account holder and must be informed of all payment activity on their account, including payments processed by authorized parties through an assisted channel.

Audit, Permissions & Configuration

Institution User Identity Logged on Every Assisted Transaction. Every assisted payment must be recorded in the audit log with: institution user identity, person ID of the student or AP assisted, payment amount, channel (in-person or phone), and the timestamp of the authorization confirmation. Transaction records must use the payer's person ID — not the institution user's — so the payment appears correctly in the payer's transaction history. The institution user's identity lives in the audit record only.

Why: Assisted payments create a situation where one party's credentials are used to act on another's behalf. A complete, tamper-proof audit trail protects the institution from disputes and enables compliance reviews to confirm every assisted transaction had documented authorization and a traceable operator identity.

Payment Space & Role-Based Access Control. The assisted payment option must only be visible when: (1) the assisted payment feature is enabled in the payment space configuration, AND (2) the institution user's assigned role has been explicitly granted assisted payment permissions. When either condition is not met, the assisted payment entry point must not be visible. The feature must be disabled by default and require deliberate activation at the payment space level.

Why: Not all payment spaces will support assisted payments, and not all institution staff are trained or authorized to take payments on behalf of payers. A two-condition gate (payment space + role) ensures only designated, trained staff at appropriately configured institutions can access the feature.

Features · Account

Authorized Party Management

Authorized parties (APs) are trusted individuals — typically family members or sponsors — whom a student designates to view account information and make payments on their behalf. This section defines the full lifecycle of an AP relationship: invitation and registration, status progression, role-based access control, the actions available to both the student and AP to manage the relationship, and the notification and audit requirements that accompany every change.

Invite & Registration

As a student

AP Invite Form. A student must be able to invite an authorized party by submitting an invite form that captures the recipient's email address and the access role to be granted. Upon submission, an invite email must be sent to the specified address and the AP must appear in the student's AP list with a status of "Invitation Sent." The student can see the invite's pending status at any time before the AP completes registration.

Why: Providing clear confirmation that an invite was sent — and persistent visibility of its pending status — ensures students can track which invites are outstanding and take action (resend or delete) when needed, without having to contact support to determine whether their invite was delivered.

As an authorized party

Knowledge-Based Verification at Registration. During AP registration, the prospective authorized party must correctly answer a knowledge-based verification challenge — such as providing the last four digits of the student's phone number on file — before registration can be completed. If the AP fails verification, registration must be blocked and an appropriate error must be displayed. The specific verification question is determined by the institution's configuration.

Why: An AP invitation email could be forwarded or accessed by an unintended party. Knowledge-based verification ensures only someone with genuine knowledge of the student's account can complete registration, providing a second layer of identity assurance beyond possession of the invite link.

Status Management

As a student

AP List with Status Display. The student's AP management view must display all associated authorized parties with their current status clearly labeled: "Invitation Sent" (invite delivered, registration not yet completed), "Active" (AP has registered and has current access), and "Access Removed" (student has revoked AP access). Each entry must show the AP's name or email, their assigned role, and the date of the most recent status change.

Why: Students need a clear, at-a-glance view of who has access to their account and in what state. Surfacing status and role for each AP reduces the risk of students unknowingly leaving active access in place for parties they intended to remove.

As a student

Resend and Delete Actions for Pending or Expired Invites. For an AP with a status of "Invitation Sent" where the invite is pending or has expired, the student must have two actions: resend the invite (delivers a new invite email to the same address with a refreshed expiration) and delete the invite (removes the AP entry from the list entirely). Delete must only be available while no AP account has been created — once the AP has registered, access management occurs through the remove and restore workflow instead.

Why: Pending invites represent a potential access grant the student may need to cancel or reissue. Providing both options in context — while making delete unavailable once an account exists — prevents accidental removal of an active AP relationship through the wrong action path.

Access Control & Role-Based Visibility

As an authorized party

Role-Governed Account Visibility. The account features and data visible to an AP after login must be determined by the access role assigned by the student at the time of invitation. Depending on role, an AP may have access to: account balance summary, payment history, upcoming payment schedule, and the ability to make payments. Role assignment must be enforced at the API level, not solely in the UI, so no AP can access data beyond their role's scope through direct API calls.

Why: Students have varying levels of trust in different APs — a parent paying tuition may warrant broader access than an employer reimbursing a specific charge. API-level enforcement ensures scope restrictions cannot be circumvented by technically sophisticated users.

As an authorized party

AP Cannot View Student's Saved Payment Methods. An authorized party must never be able to view, select, or manage the student's saved payment methods, regardless of their assigned access role. Payment method details must be restricted to the account holder who saved them. This restriction must be enforced at the data access layer and must not be overridable by any role configuration.

Why: Saved payment methods carry sensitive financial credentials the student entered for their own use. Exposing them to APs — even trusted ones — creates a vector for unauthorized use and conflicts with standard cardholder data protection expectations.

Relationship Lifecycle — Remove, Restore & Disconnect

As a student

Remove AP Access. A student must be able to remove access for any active AP. Upon removal, the AP's status changes to "Access Removed" and the AP immediately loses the ability to access account activity and payment options. The AP retains access to their own transaction history, their own communications, and their own saved payment methods — these are personal records belonging to the AP's identity, not the student's account. The access removal must take effect within one authentication cycle.

Why: Students may need to revoke access promptly due to a change in relationship or financial circumstances. Preserving the AP's own transaction history ensures the AP can still reference records of payments they made after removal, protecting against disputes about past transactions.

As a student

Restore AP Access (Grant Access). For an AP with status "Access Removed," the student must be able to restore access using a "Grant Access" action. Upon restoration, the AP's status returns to "Active" and the AP regains the account access defined by their original role assignment. No new invite is required for restoration — the existing AP account relationship is reactivated. The restore action must be logged in the audit trail.

Why: Relationships change over time, and a student may wish to reinstate access for a previously removed AP without requiring the AP to go through the full registration flow again. Supporting restore preserves the AP's role assignment and historical records.

As an authorized party

AP Self-Disconnect from Student Account. An authorized party must be able to voluntarily disconnect from a student account provided they have no active payment plans associated with that account. Upon disconnection, the AP loses access to the student's account activity and payment options but retains access to their own transaction history and communications. If an active payment plan exists, the disconnection must be blocked and the AP must be shown a message explaining they must resolve or complete the active plan before disconnecting.

Why: APs should have agency over their own account relationships. Blocking disconnection when an active plan exists protects the integrity of the payment plan — which may have scheduled future payments — and prevents the AP from abandoning a financial obligation mid-term.

Notifications & Audit

Student Notification on AP or Guest Payment. When an authorized party or guest payer successfully completes a payment on a student's account, the student must receive a notification confirming the payment. The notification must include the payment amount, date, and payer type (authorized party or guest). It must not expose the payer's payment method details. Notification is delivered to the student's email address on file.

Why: The student is the ultimate owner of the account balance and must be aware of all credits applied to their account regardless of who made the payment. Real-time notification supports account transparency and allows the student to detect any unexpected or incorrect payments promptly.

Audit Trail for All Relationship Changes. Every AP relationship event — invite sent, invite resent, invite deleted, registration completed, access removed, access restored, AP self-disconnect — must be recorded in an immutable audit log. Each entry must capture: actor (student or AP), action performed, affected AP identity, and timestamp. The audit log must be accessible to institution users with appropriate permissions and must not be editable by any user-facing role.

Why: AP relationship changes affect who has access to sensitive financial account information. A complete, tamper-proof audit trail provides the evidence base needed to resolve disputes about access history, support compliance reviews, and investigate unexpected access changes.

Scenario 1 · Student

First Time Student

Scenario Description

A student arriving at the Nelnet payment portal for the very first time. They authenticate via SAML SSO from their university's student portal — no separate Nelnet login is created. Upon authentication, a full ERP sync delivers all account data automatically.

This student has no existing payment methods, authorized parties, or communication preferences on file. Every decision in this flow is being made for the first time this term. The prototype for this scenario is the "First Time Student" prototype on the index page.

Institution Configuration — This Scenario
AuthenticationSAML SSO from university portal
ERP integrationFull sync — charges, aid, enrollment
Tuition insuranceEnabled (GradGuard) — school has active GradGuard contract
School agreementsEnabled — includes GradGuard refund policy agreement (required when GradGuard is on)
Payment plan offers1 — Pay Over Time
Accepted payment methodsACH (bank) + Credit Card
University disclosures3 (individually acknowledged)
POT first payment windowMust be within 30 days of today
POT minimum down payment5% of plan balance
⬡ Prototype: Onboarding — Full Flow
Authentication & Data Pre-population

First semester = no Nelnet history = full onboarding flow. A first-semester student has no existing payment methods, authorized parties, insurance decisions, or communication preferences on file anywhere in Nelnet's system. They must complete every step of the onboarding flow to establish their account state for this term. No steps can be skipped or pre-filled from prior decisions.

Why: Unlike a returning student who can pick up where they left off, a first-semester student is establishing their account from scratch. Every decision — insurance, payment path, authorized parties, communications — is being made for the first time. The system must present the full flow without assumptions about what the student wants.

First semester → full onboarding flow, no shortcuts

No account creation step. A first-semester student does not create a Nelnet account through Horizon — they authenticate exclusively via SAML SSO from their school's student information system (SIS/ERP portal). The student already has institutional credentials; Horizon receives their identity from the SSO assertion and creates an internal Nelnet record automatically. The student never sees a "Create an account" or "Set a password" screen for Nelnet.

Why: Requiring a separate Nelnet account creation defeats the purpose of SSO integration. The institution has already authenticated this student — a second account setup flow creates unnecessary friction, abandonment risk, and a separate credential the student must manage. Nelnet's record is created automatically behind the scenes from the SSO handshake.

ERP / SSO

The student arrives exclusively via SAML SSO from the university portal. No Nelnet-specific username or password entry occurs within Horizon.

Why: Requiring a separate Nelnet login creates friction and abandonment. Students are already authenticated by their institution — forcing a second login adds no security benefit and creates a barrier to completing payment setup.

ERP / SSO

Upon authentication, the system must automatically populate: student first name, last name, preferred name (if available), student ID, current term, total charges, applied financial aid, anticipated financial aid, balance due, primary email address, and phone number — all sourced from the ERP. None of these require manual entry.

Why: No duplicate entry. The student should never type what the institution already knows. This is a core product principle.

ERP / SSORequired
1
Balance Overview

Present the student's full account balance breakdown: total charges, applied financial aid, anticipated financial aid, and resulting balance due. All values are sourced from the ERP — no manual entry.

Why: Students must understand what they owe before making any payment decision. This is the anchor for all downstream choices in the flow.

ERP / SSO

The term "Anticipated" (adjacent to the anticipated aid figure) must be interactive — tapping or clicking it opens an inline explanation: anticipated aid has been subtracted from the balance shown, but is not yet officially applied to the student's school account. If it does not finalize, the student may still owe that amount.

Why: Anticipated aid is a leading driver of student confusion and support contacts. An inline explanation surfaces at the moment of need without adding a screen.

The balance breakdown must remain accessible to the student throughout the entire onboarding flow. They should be able to reference their balance at any point while making decisions.

Why: Payment decisions (plan type, down payment amount, insurance acceptance) are all made in relation to the balance. Hiding or removing the balance context mid-flow forces the student to hold the number in memory, increasing errors and second-guessing.

2
Tuition Insurance Institution: GradGuard enabled

This step is shown only when the institution has tuition insurance (GradGuard) enabled. If not enabled, the flow proceeds directly to Step 3.

Why: Not all institutions offer tuition insurance. Surfacing the step when it is not available confuses students and makes the flow longer than necessary without benefit.

Institution settingIF: GradGuard enabled → show step

The insurance offer must not be presented until the correct premium can be calculated. Premium varies by the student's state of residence. Ask first: "Do you live in [institution state]?" — Yes / No. This is the only question shown initially.

Why: Showing an offer before knowing the applicable premium is either misleading or requires a rate percentage — which means nothing actionable to most consumers.

IF: Student answers "No, I live out of state"

Reveal a state selector so the student can indicate their state of residence. Once a state is selected, the correct premium is calculated and the offer can be shown.

Why: GradGuard premiums vary by state. The state selector must only appear when needed — surfacing it unconditionally would add unnecessary steps for in-state students.

Once state is resolved (either "Yes, I live in [state]" or an out-of-state selection is made), show the tuition insurance offer card. Display the premium as a dollar amount only — do not show a rate percentage.

Why: A percentage rate is not actionable. The dollar cost is what allows the student to make a real decision.

The student must have three response options: Accept, Decline, or Decide Later.

Why: A student may not be ready to decide on insurance before completing payment setup. "Decide Later" prevents onboarding abandonment when the student needs more time to evaluate the offer.

IF: Student accepts tuition insurance

Display an immediate confirmation note at the point of acceptance: "[Premium amount] will be added to your sign-up costs today." The student must know the premium is part of today's payment before they proceed.

Why: The premium is charged immediately — the student must not be surprised by an unexpected charge when they reach the payment confirmation. Transparency at the point of acceptance prevents disputes and loss of trust.

The insurance premium must be included in every downstream total-due-today calculation: the Pay Over Time down payment breakdown (Step 3), the payment confirmation screen (Step 4), and the success screen. The total must never show just the down payment or enrollment fee in isolation.

Why: The total due today is the number the student will compare against their bank account. Any omission — even temporary — creates a discrepancy the student will notice and question, generating a support contact.

Cascades to: Step 3 · Step 4 · Success screen
3
How to Pay

Present the available payment paths. Options are determined by institution settings. Always available: Pay in Full, Schedule a Payment. Conditional: Pay Over Time (shown only if the institution offers a payment plan).

Why: Not all institutions offer payment plans. Showing options the student cannot actually use creates confusion and wasted interaction. The available set must match exactly what the institution has configured.

Institution setting

Each option must describe what it means for the student — not just label the option. The Pay Over Time option description: "Split your balance into multiple payments over a longer period of time." Do not surface plan details (installment count, fees) at this selection step — those are determined in the inline setup that follows.

Why: Decision-first principle — explain the outcome, not the mechanics. Details are surfaced only when the student has chosen this path.

PATH: Pay in Full

Show the full balance due. Student proceeds to Step 4 (payment method collection) for the full amount.

Why: Pay in Full is the simplest path. The student has already seen the balance — confirming it here and proceeding directly to payment method keeps the flow minimal for students who don't need installment options.

PATH: Schedule a Payment

Allow the student to select a future payment date. Student then proceeds to Step 4 to enter their payment method for the scheduled amount.

Why: Some students want to pay in full but need a few extra days — for example, waiting for a paycheck or a parent's transfer. Scheduling avoids forcing them into a payment plan just to defer by a week.

PATH: Pay Over Time Institution: plan offered

The entire Pay Over Time setup must happen inline on the same screen where the student selected "Pay Over Time." The system must not navigate to a separate setup screen. The balance card must remain visible at the top of the screen throughout the setup.

Why: Keeping the balance context visible while making payment structure decisions reduces cognitive load and prevents the student from losing track of what they're paying.

Setup uses a progressive reveal pattern across 4 sequential decisions. Each decision step collapses to a summary row (with an Edit button) once confirmed. Editing any step resets all downstream confirmations — for example, editing frequency invalidates the installment count and down payment, since those depend on frequency.

Why: Downstream choices (installment count, last payment date) depend directly on upstream choices (frequency, first date). Preventing stale combinations avoids the student accidentally committing to an invalid plan.

Sub-step A — Payment Frequency. Options: Weekly, Every 2 weeks, Monthly. Once confirmed, collapses to a summary row showing the selected frequency, with an Edit button.

Why: Frequency alignment with the student's income cycle is the primary driver of plan success. A student paid bi-weekly who sets up a monthly plan may struggle; matching the cadence to their paycheck reduces missed payments.

Sub-step B — First Payment Date. The institution's date constraint must be displayed prominently before the student selects a date: "Your first payment must be within 30 days of today." The date picker must enforce this: minimum = tomorrow, maximum = 30 days from today. Once confirmed, collapses to a summary row showing the selected date.

Why: Institution requirements must be communicated upfront — not as a validation error after the student picks an invalid date. This is a decision-framing requirement, not just a validation rule.

Institution setting: 30-day window

Sub-step C — Number of Installments. The options shown depend on the frequency chosen in Sub-step A:
 · Weekly: 4, 8, 13, or 26 installments
 · Every 2 weeks: 3, 6, 9, or 12 installments
 · Monthly: 3, 6, 9, or 12 installments
The collapsed summary row must show: "[N] installments — last payment [calculated date] — [frequency]." The last payment date is calculated from Sub-steps A + B + C.

Why: The last payment date is the most meaningful signal of commitment length. Surfacing it in the summary immediately after selection confirms the student understands when the plan ends.

Sub-step D — Down Payment. A slider allowing the student to choose how much to pay today as a down payment. Slider minimum = 5% of the plan balance (the institution-required minimum), clearly labeled as "School min (5%)." Slider maximum = full balance. As the slider moves, the per-installment payment amount updates dynamically.

Why: Giving students control over the down payment empowers cash flow management. The 5% floor is a school requirement and must be communicated proactively — not encountered as a blocking error.

Institution setting: 5% minimum

Throughout Sub-step D, display a live breakdown of the total due today — updated in real time as the slider moves. The breakdown must include:
 · Down payment (selected amount)
 · Nelnet enrollment fee
 · Tuition insurance premium (only if accepted in Step 2)
 · Total due today

Why: The student is deciding how much leaves their account today. They need to see the complete picture in real time — not just the down payment value in isolation.

IF: Insurance accepted → include premium in breakdown
4
Payment Method & Confirmation

Collect the payment method for the amount due today (full balance, scheduled amount, or Pay Over Time total). Accepted methods are determined by institution settings. This scenario: ACH (bank account) and Credit Card.

Why: The payment method collected here becomes the default for all future auto-pay installments. Collecting it at this step — after the student has committed to a payment path — avoids asking for method details before the student knows what they're paying for.

Institution setting: accepted methods

If a saved payment method exists from a previous term, pre-select and display it. Only request new payment details if no saved method is on file.

Why: No duplicate entry. Payment methods carry forward term over term.

IF: Saved method on file → pre-populate

Before charging, present a full confirmation screen showing a complete breakdown of everything due today. For Pay Over Time, this includes: down payment, Nelnet enrollment fee, tuition insurance premium (if applicable), total due today, plus the plan summary — installment count × installment amount, payment frequency, first payment date, and remaining balance after today's payment.

Why: The confirmation screen is the student's last opportunity to review and catch errors before money moves. A complete breakdown — not a single total — allows them to verify each component is correct and builds confidence before authorizing the charge.

IF: Insurance accepted → show premium rowIF: POT path → show plan summary
5
Authorized Parties

Allow the student to designate authorized parties — individuals who can access and pay on the student's behalf. Authorized parties are managed within Nelnet's system, not by the institution. The student controls who has access.

Why: Many students have parents or guardians who manage payments. Capturing this during onboarding means the AP can be active immediately, without a separate re-entry loop later.

Collect name and email for each authorized party. Send each AP an invitation email with their account setup link immediately upon submission.

Why: The AP needs to complete their own account setup to access the student's account. An immediate invite ensures there is no delay between the student granting access and the AP being able to act — especially important if a parent needs to make the first payment.

The student can add multiple authorized parties, or skip this step entirely.

Why: Not all students have parents or guardians who manage payments. Requiring AP setup to complete onboarding would block students who are self-paying. The step is optional and can be completed post-onboarding.

IF: One or more authorized parties added

Post-onboarding: the Manage Authorized Parties quick action on the home screen must show the names of the APs added here, not just a generic label.

Why: Showing names rather than a generic label confirms to the student that their APs were successfully added and makes the quick action more immediately meaningful — they can see who has access at a glance.

Cascades to: Home screen quick actions

Post-onboarding: if any authorized party subsequently sets up a Pay Over Time plan, a new "AP Pay Over Time Plans" quick action must appear on the student's home screen.

Why: The student is responsible for their account's total coverage. If a parent sets up a plan, the student needs visibility so they understand what portion of the balance is being covered by someone else's plan.

Cascades to: Home screen · IF AP creates POT plan
6
Communication Preferences

Transactional SMS (payment confirmations, reminders, account alerts) must be enabled and is not toggleable. Label it as required for account activity.

Why: Transactional messages are required to service the account. Opt-out is not available for this category.

Marketing/promotional SMS is opt-in and toggleable. The default for a first-time student is off unless the institution has configured a different default. Whatever state the student sets here carries forward to their Account Details screen.

Why: Defaulting marketing SMS to off respects consumer communication preferences and regulatory requirements. The student's explicit choice here must persist — re-asking in Account Details would be inconsistent and frustrating.

Cascades to: Account Details · SMS opt-in state

The student's email address is pre-populated from SSO/ERP. No re-entry required.

Why: No duplicate entry. The email is already known from SSO. Asking the student to type it again provides no value and would contradict the ERP-first data principle.

ERP / SSO
7
Security Questions

The student must set security questions for account recovery. Answers are stored and accessible (masked) from the Account Details screen post-onboarding, with a "Change" option to update them.

Why: Authorized parties authenticate with Nelnet credentials (not SSO), and students may need to recover their account outside of the institution's SSO flow. Security questions provide a fallback verification path for account recovery scenarios.

8
Disclosures Institution setting: count

Display the institution-configured number of disclosures (this scenario: 3). Each disclosure must be individually acknowledged before the student can complete onboarding.

Why: Legal requirement. Disclosure count and content vary per institution.

Institution setting: disclosure count
Post-Onboarding
Consumer Home Screen
Greeting & Identity Area

Greet the student by first name — large, left-aligned. Account access (initials avatar + "Account" label) is positioned on the right side of the greeting area and is always tappable to reach Account Details. The initials avatar is the only account access entry point; no duplicate link elsewhere in the header.

Why: A personal greeting confirms the correct student is logged in and sets a consumer-first tone. A single, consistent entry point to account settings prevents confusion about where to manage profile or payment details.

To-dos Section

A "To dos" section appears above the account summary. To-do items are entirely dynamic — generated from the student's current account state. Show nothing in this section if there are no actionable to-dos.

Why: The to-do list is the guided experience in action — it tells the student exactly what they still need to do without them having to interpret their balance or navigate to find it. An empty to-do section should not imply there are things left undone.

If an open (unpaid, unscheduled) balance exists: show a to-do card displaying the open amount, with the copy "Hasn't been paid or scheduled to be paid yet."

Why: An unaddressed balance is the most actionable item on the student's account. Surfacing it as a to-do — not just in the balance summary — ensures it cannot be overlooked.

IF: Open balance exists

If a payment is due within the next 30 days: surface it as a to-do with the amount and due date.

Why: Students access the portal infrequently. A timely to-do ensures they see upcoming auto-pay dates and can resolve any issues (expired card, insufficient funds) before the payment fails.

IF: Payment due within 30 days

Account activity from the last 30 days must be surfaced in this area as context — payments made, plan changes, etc.

Why: Students who log in to check their account often arrive after receiving a notification. Showing recent activity confirms what has already happened, reducing contacts from students who don't know if their payment went through.

Account Summary Section

Show a visual balance bar below the "Account summary" section label. The bar is composed of up to two segments representing how the total balance is distributed:

 · On Pay Over Time plan (teal/green segment) — only present if student has an active POT plan
 · Open balance (accent color segment) — always present if there is any open/unpaid balance

The proportions of each segment reflect the actual split of the student's total balance.

Why: The visual bar makes the balance structure immediately legible. A student can see at a glance how much is covered by their plan vs. still open — without doing math. This directly reduces the "what do I still owe?" confusion that drives bursar contacts.

IF: POT plan active → two-segment bar IF: No POT plan → single segment

Below the balance bar: display the open balance dollar amount prominently on the left. The label "Open balance" appears to the right of the number. Brief supporting text explains what "open balance" means in this context.

Why: The open balance is the primary number the student needs to act on. Labeling it clearly and adding supporting text reduces the terminological confusion ("which balance do I pay?") that is the leading driver of bursar contacts.

A "View full statement" button must be present within the account summary section — not in the quick actions. It is a secondary/outline-style button (not a primary CTA).

Why: Statement access is contextually adjacent to the balance — that's where students will look for it. It does not belong in quick actions as a distinct action.

Quick Actions (Dynamic, Priority Ordered)

Quick actions are shown and ordered dynamically based on the student's account state. The full ordered list:

1. My Pay Over Time Plan — shown only if the student has an active POT plan
2. Manage Authorized Parties — always shown; sub-label: "People with full payment access to your account"
3. Guest Payment Link — always shown; framed as sending a one-time payment link
4. Make a Payment — always shown; sub-label sets expectation: make a payment now
5. Account History — always shown
6. AP Pay Over Time Plans — shown only if at least one authorized party has an active POT plan

Why: Quick actions replace the need for navigation — the most relevant action for the student's current state should always be one tap away. Dynamic ordering ensures that a student with an active plan sees plan management first, not buried behind actions that don't apply to them.

IF: Student has POT → show #1 IF: Any AP has POT → show #6
Decision Impact Summary — How Onboarding Choices Affect the Home Screen

The table below consolidates how decisions made during onboarding directly shape what the student sees on their home screen.

Onboarding decision Home screen impact
Student selects Pay Over Time Balance bar gains a teal "on-plan" segment. "My Pay Over Time Plan" quick action (position #1) appears. Open balance reflects only the unpaid, un-planned portion.
Student accepts tuition insurance Insurance premium was included in today's payment — no recurring home screen impact. Plan confirmation and success screens reflect the correct totals.
Student adds one or more authorized parties "Manage Authorized Parties" quick action shows the AP names. If any AP later sets up a POT plan, "AP Pay Over Time Plans" quick action (position #6) activates.
Student sets marketing SMS to on Marketing SMS preference is reflected as "on" in Account Details → Communication Preferences section.
Student pays in full today No open-balance to-do on home screen. Balance bar shows single green segment (paid). No POT quick action.
No authorized parties added "Manage Authorized Parties" still shown — allows the student to add APs post-onboarding. "AP Pay Over Time Plans" is hidden until an AP is added and sets up a plan.
Post-Onboarding Sub-screens
Supporting Screens
Account Details

Accessible from the initials avatar on the home screen. Must display: first name, last name, preferred name (editable), student ID (read-only — from ERP). Contact section: email addresses and phone numbers, each individually editable and addable. SMS opt-in section: transactional (locked on, labeled as required), marketing (toggleable). Security questions section: answers masked, with a "Change" action that launches the security question update flow.

Why: Students need a single place to manage all their account-level settings post-onboarding. Separating these into multiple screens or burying them increases the chance a student can't find what they need and contacts support instead.

Student ID: ERP / read-only
Manage Authorized Parties

Show all authorized parties with their current active/inactive status. Student can toggle any AP between active and inactive. Deactivating an AP must require an explicit confirmation step to prevent accidental removal. Student can invite additional APs directly from this screen.

Why: The student owns access control. A confirmation step on deactivation protects against accidentally cutting off someone who is actively managing payments.

Guest Payment Link

Frame this as a one-time payment link — not account access. Show the student's current open balance as context. Allow the student to set a cap amount (must be ≤ open balance) and an optional note to the guest. Explicitly and clearly distinguish this from an authorized party: the guest has zero ongoing account access — they can only pay once via this link.

Why: Some students want a family member to make a single payment without granting ongoing account visibility or control. The distinction between "guest payer" and "authorized party" must be unambiguous — otherwise students may unknowingly grant more access than intended, or be confused when the guest can't pay again.

AP Pay Over Time Plans

Read-only view of Pay Over Time plans set up by the student's authorized parties. Accessible from quick action #6 on the home screen, which is only shown when at least one AP has an active POT plan.

Why: The student needs to know if an AP's plan is covering their balance — especially if multiple parties are paying. Read-only access provides coverage visibility without giving the student control over an AP's plan (which belongs to the AP).

IF: AP has active POT plan → quick action visible
Scenario 2 · Student

Returning Student

Detailed requirements coming soon. Core scenario logic captured below — full step-by-step requirements will be added here.
Scenario Description

A student returning for a subsequent term who has completed the full onboarding flow at least once before with Nelnet. They have existing history: at minimum a saved payment method, and potentially existing authorized parties and communication preferences. They authenticate via SAML SSO from their school's SIS portal — same as their first term. No account creation occurs.

The key distinction from Scenario 1 is that this student is not starting from zero. The system knows them and their prior decisions, and the flow adapts accordingly — presenting only what may need re-confirmation or updating rather than walking through every decision from scratch.

Known Logic — What Changes for a Returning Student

SSO authentication — no account creation, no login screen. A returning student authenticates through their school's SIS portal exactly as they did in their first term. Nelnet recognizes the returning student via their SSO identity and links them to their existing Nelnet record automatically. The student never sees a "Create account" screen.

Why: The returning student should experience Horizon as an account they already have — not a new system. Forcing re-registration or re-login creates a jarring experience and a support contact driver.

ERP / SSO

Streamlined re-onboarding. The returning student does not repeat the full first-time onboarding flow. Prior decisions that carry forward — saved payment method, authorized parties, communication preferences, security questions — are pre-populated and confirmed rather than re-collected. The student is only asked to make decisions that are new for this term (e.g., new balance, new insurance offer if re-presentation is configured, updated disclosures).

Why: Requiring a returning student to re-enter information they already provided creates friction and signals that the system doesn't remember them. The set-it-and-forget-it goal applies here — if nothing changed, the student should need to do as little as possible.

Returning student → pre-populate from prior decisions

Tuition insurance re-presentation (institution-configured). Whether the insurance offer is shown to a returning student who previously declined depends on the institution's configuration.
