Some institutions re-present every term; others suppress the offer after a student has declined once. If the institution has set "re-present each term," the student will see the insurance step again with a new premium calculated on the current term's charges. If "never re-present after decline," the step is skipped.

Why: Insurance decisions are term-specific (the policy covers a specific enrollment period), so re-presenting each term is academically correct. However, some institutions prefer not to prompt students who have previously opted out. Institution-configured behavior allows both approaches.

Institution setting: insurance re-presentation IF: Re-present each term → show step; ELSE → skip

Scenarios — Home Screen

Home Screen Scenarios

These scenarios document the distinct balance states a returning student may encounter on the Home Screen — each representing a specific financial situation that the Home Screen must handle clearly. Each scenario has a corresponding click-through prototype. See Features · Home Screen for the feature-level requirements that underpin all scenarios.

Scenario 1b · Student

Balance Increase While on Plan

Prototype: home-1b-balance-increase.html · Student: Alex · Balance state: on-plan-open

Setup: Alex is on an active pay over time plan ($4,680 remaining, $517/month, next May 10). A new lab fee of $350 was added to the account after enrollment. The $350 is not covered by the plan — it shows as an open balance alongside the on-plan amount.

⬡ Prototype: 1b — Balance Increase

As a student payer

I need to be able to immediately see that a new charge has been added to my account that is not covered by my existing pay over time plan, with a clear to-do item explaining the charge and offering a direct action path.

Why: A student on a plan who gets a new charge has no mental model that it won't be auto-handled — they need a proactive, prominent signal that action is required. Without this, students assume the charge will be added to their plan and are surprised when it goes to collections.

As a student payer

I need to be able to see a clear visual distinction between my plan balance (covered, auto-debit scheduled) and my open balance (not covered, action needed) on the balance card — without having to navigate away from the home screen to understand my financial status.

Why: Mixing covered and uncovered amounts without visual distinction causes confusion and support calls. The balance card in on-plan-open mode shows two segments: teal for on-plan, blue for open. This distinction must be present at home-screen level.

As a student payer

I need to be able to address the open balance directly from the home screen to-do item — either by paying the open amount immediately or by adding it to my existing plan (if the institution allows plan balance increases).

Why: The further a student has to navigate to resolve an open balance, the more likely they are to defer the action. The to-do CTA ("Address now") must take the student directly into the resolution flow.

Scenario 2b · Student

Simple Balance, No Plan

Prototype: home-2b-no-plan.html · Student: Emily · Balance state: open

Setup: Emily has an $8,750 balance due September 15 with no payment plan and no saved payment method. She has not completed onboarding. The home screen shows the balance due to-do, and provides the option to pay in full or set up a plan.

⬡ Prototype: 2b — Simple Balance No Plan

As a student payer

I need to be able to see my outstanding balance, due date, and available payment options clearly as my primary to-do when I land on the home screen with no active plan, without having to navigate into an account detail view first.

Why: A student without a plan who lands on the home screen has one primary financial job to complete: decide how to pay. Surfacing this as the lead to-do with a direct CTA reduces time-to-action and reduces the likelihood of the balance becoming past-due.

As a student payer

I need to be able to initiate pay-in-full or set up a pay over time plan from the home screen to-do with a single tap, proceeding directly into the selected payment flow without an intermediate navigation step.

Why: Every extra navigation step between intent and action reduces completion rates. The CTA "Pay or plan" from the to-do card should route directly into the appropriate flow based on the student's selection.

Scenario 3b · Student

Credit Balance & Refund Pending

Prototype: home-3b-credit-balance.html · Student: David · Balance state: credit

Setup: David has a $2,150 credit balance (overpayment from excess aid). A refund of $2,150 is pending, expected October 1. A partial refund of $1,500 has already been issued by check. The home screen shows the upcoming refund in the upcoming payments section with no open balance to-dos.

⬡ Prototype: 3b — Credit Balance & Refund

As a student payer

I need to be able to see that I have a credit balance on my account and understand when and how my refund will be disbursed, without needing to contact the institution or navigate to a separate refund tracking screen.

Why: Credit balances and pending refunds are a major source of student service calls at institutions. Surfacing refund status proactively on the home screen reduces inbound calls and gives the student confidence that the process is underway.

As a student payer

I need to be able to see partially-issued refunds and pending remaining refunds as separate line items, so I understand that a portion has been issued and the remainder is still processing — not that the full refund is still outstanding.

Why: Partial refund situations (e.g., one check issued, one still processing) look like a discrepancy if shown as a single "refund pending" amount. The split display prevents the student from calling to ask why their refund isn't the amount they expected.

Scenario 4b · Student

Defaulted Payment Plan

Prototype: home-4b-defaulted-plan.html · Student: Nicole · Balance state: defaulted

Setup: Nicole's pay over time plan has defaulted. $7,400 past-due is immediately due. She also has $6,500 due December 15 for the current term. A registration hold is active. Her saved payment method is on file. Total balance: $11,275.

⬡ Prototype: 4b — Defaulted Plan

As a student payer

I need to be able to immediately understand that my payment plan has failed, what is immediately due, and that a registration hold is in effect — with high-urgency visual treatment that is distinct from informational to-dos.

Why: A defaulted plan with a registration hold is the highest-stakes situation a student can arrive on the home screen with. Understated visual treatment would cause the student to under-prioritize the action. The danger-colored to-do items and registration hold indicator must be unmissable.

As a student payer

I need to be able to see both the defaulted amount and the upcoming term balance clearly separated — understanding that the $7,400 is immediately due and the $6,500 is a separate future obligation — so I can address them in the correct order.

Why: Presenting all balance components together without chronological priority causes students to be confused about how much they actually need to pay right now to clear the hold. Clear separation of "immediately due" vs. "due December 15" prevents this confusion.

Scenario 5b · Student

Past Due & Mixed Due Dates

Prototype: home-5b-past-due-mixed.html · Student: James · Balance state: past-due

Setup: James has a $2,500 past-due balance from Summer 2025 (overdue), a $9,500 current-term balance due September 15, a $50 returned payment fee due immediately, and a $1,000 balance with no due date. Total: $12,450. No active plan. No registration hold.

⬡ Prototype: 5b — Past Due & Mixed Dates

As a student payer

I need to be able to see which of my charges are past-due (requiring immediate action) and which are upcoming (due on specific dates) separately, so I understand my financial priority order without having to add up line items myself.

Why: Students with multiple balance components across different terms and due dates are the most likely to be overwhelmed and do nothing. The home screen must impose a clear priority order — past-due first, then upcoming by date — rather than presenting an undifferentiated list.

As a student payer

I need to be able to see the returned payment fee of $50 as a separate, immediately-actionable to-do item — not bundled into the general past-due balance — because it has a different resolution path (paying a fee, not a tuition balance).

Why: A returned payment fee has a specific cause and a specific action. Bundling it with other past-due amounts obscures its nature and makes it harder for the student to understand and resolve it. The to-do card must surface it discretely with a "Pay now" CTA.

Scenario 6b · Student

Active Plan + Outside-Plan Charges

Prototype: home-6b-outside-plan-charges.html · Student: Marcus · Balance state: outside-plan

Setup: Marcus has an active pay over time plan ($6,000 remaining, $1,500/month). A meal plan charge and an enrollment fee totaling $1,550 are due September 15 but are NOT included in his pay over time plan. Total account balance: $9,200.

⬡ Prototype: 6b — Active Plan + Outside Charges

As a student payer

I need to be able to see that I have charges on my account that are outside my pay over time plan and due on a specific date, distinct from the plan amount that is auto-debit — so I know I need to take action on the $1,550 separately from my scheduled plan payments.

Why: This is a very common scenario: a student sets up a plan for tuition, then gets a separate meal plan or fee charge that is not plan-eligible or was added after enrollment closed. If this charge is not surfaced prominently, it goes past-due while the student assumes their plan is covering everything.

As a student payer

I need to be able to clearly see both my plan amount (covered, auto-debit on Oct 1) and my outside-plan amount (not covered, due Sep 15) as separate line items on the balance card — understanding that I need to act on the Sep 15 amount and that the Oct 1 amount will process automatically.

Why: The visual split between "on-plan" and "outside-plan" on the balance card (mode: outside-plan) is the core feature of this scenario. Without this split, a student would see a total balance of $9,200 and not understand that $6,000 of it is auto-handled while $1,550 requires action in the next two weeks.

Features

Onboarding Features

How to read this section

Each feature below represents a discrete step or capability within the onboarding flow. Requirements here are written cross-scenario — they describe behavior across all current and future scenarios. Scenario chips indicate which scenarios each feature currently applies to, and which are pending.

When a new scenario is added, return to each relevant feature and update its requirements and scenario chips to reflect any scenario-specific business rules.

🔐
Authentication
How consumers enter the Horizon experience
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S6 · Authorized Parties
Cross-scenario rule: Authentication method differs by user type. Students always authenticate via institution SSO. Authorized parties authenticate via a Nelnet-issued invite link and create independent credentials — they never use the student's login.

Student authentication is exclusively via institution SAML SSO. Students access Horizon by clicking a link within their institution's portal. The session is pre-authenticated — no Nelnet username or password is required. Students never create a Horizon-specific login.

Why: Eliminates credential friction and ensures identity is always validated through the institution's existing auth system.

ERP: identity + enrollment passed via SSO token

The SSO token carries enrollment, identity, and authorization context. The institution passes student name, email, enrollment status, and account identifiers as part of the SAML assertion. Horizon reads these values directly — students are never asked to re-enter what the school already knows.

Why: The SSO token is the technical implementation of the no-duplicate-entry principle. If Horizon cannot read these values automatically, onboarding degrades into a manual data collection form — defeating the ERP-first strategy.

RequiredERP integration

Authorized party (AP) authentication is separate from the student's credentials. When a student invites an authorized party, Nelnet sends that person a unique invite link. The AP follows the link to create their own Nelnet account. They never share or reuse the student's login. Their access and permissions are scoped to exactly what the student granted.

Why: APs are external to the institution's identity system — they cannot use SSO. Independent credentials scoped to granted permissions ensure the AP can access what they need without ever seeing the student's login or accessing the institution's portal.

IF: Student has set up APs → AP invite link exists

Session state persists through onboarding. If a student begins onboarding but doesn't complete it in one session (e.g., chooses "I'll complete this later" on the authorized parties step), their progress is saved. When they re-enter via SSO, they resume from where they left off — or can choose to start over.

Why: Students are interrupted — by class, phone calls, or uncertainty about a decision. Losing all progress on re-entry is a significant friction point that would drive abandonment or duplicate submissions. Progress persistence ensures onboarding can be completed across sessions without re-work.

Required
💰
Balance Overview
How account charges and financial aid are presented
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S4 · New AP (Payer)
Cross-scenario rule: Balance is always derived from ERP in real time. No balance is ever hard-coded or estimated by Horizon. Returning students see a comparison of prior-term vs. current-term amounts. APs see only the balance components the student has granted visibility to.

Display a full balance breakdown on entry to the payment decision step. Show: total charges (tuition + institutional fees), financial aid applied, school enrollment fee (if applicable), and the resulting net balance. Each component must be labeled clearly — no abbreviations the student may not recognize.

Why: Students make their payment decision (pay in full vs. plan) based on this breakdown. If any component is missing or unlabeled, the student cannot verify their balance is correct — leading to calls to the bursar or hesitation to complete setup.

ERP: charges + financial aidInstitution: enrollment fee amount

Distinguish estimated vs. finalized balances. If the ERP has not yet posted final charges (e.g., registration is still open), the balance is marked "estimated" with a plain-language explanation. Decisions made on an estimated balance (e.g., POT enrollment) are confirmed again once the balance is finalized.

Why: Students who enroll in a plan based on an estimated balance and later see a different amount feel misled. Clearly flagging the estimate sets expectations and triggers a re-confirmation step to keep plan terms accurate.

ERP: balance finalization flag

Balance math must always resolve to $0 open balance when fully enrolled in Pay Over Time. net balance − down payment − on-plan amount = $0. No rounding or UI artifact should show a non-zero open balance when the student has enrolled their entire balance in a plan.

Why: A student who enrolls their full balance in a plan and still sees an "open balance" will call to ask what they still owe. Rounding artifacts create phantom balances that generate unnecessary support contacts and erode trust in the system's accuracy.

Required · Bug prevention

Insurance premium is excluded from the "balance owed" calculation. When a student accepts tuition insurance, the premium is charged immediately as a separate transaction — it does not add to the open balance that feeds the payment plan or pay-in-full flow.

Why: The insurance premium is a separate product purchase, not part of the tuition balance. Including it in the plan balance would distort installment amounts and create confusion about what is being paid off via the plan.

IF: GradGuard enabled + student accepted insurance
🛡️
Tuition Insurance
GradGuard integration — opt-in/opt-out decision during onboarding
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student Institution-configured
Cross-scenario rule: Tuition insurance is an institution-level toggle. When enabled, every new student in onboarding is presented the offer. The offer is not re-surfaced to returning students who already made a decision in a prior term unless the institution resets the offer. APs are never offered tuition insurance — it is a student-only decision.

Insurance step is conditional on institution enabling GradGuard. If GradGuard is not enabled for the institution, this step is skipped entirely — no placeholder, no mention of it.

Why: Mentioning an unavailable product creates confusion and support questions. If the institution hasn't contracted with GradGuard, the step must be completely invisible — not just disabled.

Institution: GradGuard toggleIF: GradGuard enabled → show insurance step

Present the insurance offer with the calculated premium for this student's enrollment. The premium is derived from the student's total charges and the institution's GradGuard plan. Show the annual premium amount, what is covered (medical withdrawal, academic dismissal, etc.), and the GradGuard plan name. Do not require the student to navigate elsewhere to understand what they're buying.

Why: Students cannot make an informed accept/decline decision if they don't know the cost and coverage. Forcing them to navigate elsewhere to understand what they're buying breaks the decision-first UX principle and increases abandonment at this step.

ERP: enrollment charges for premium calc

Student may accept or decline. Both paths must be equally accessible — no dark patterns. "Accept" and "Decline" must be visually equivalent choices. Do not pre-select "Accept", do not style "Decline" as a secondary/tertiary action.

Why: Students have the right to make a genuine choice. Pre-selecting "Accept" or visually de-emphasizing "Decline" manipulates the student's decision — which is both ethically problematic and potentially a regulatory concern given the insurance context.

Required

If accepted: premium is charged immediately as a separate transaction. The insurance premium appears in Recent Activity on the home screen — NOT in Upcoming Payments. It is not folded into the POT plan installments. The student's effective balance for payment decisions is the net balance excluding the premium.

Why: The premium is a completed charge, not a future obligation. Placing it in Upcoming Payments would imply a future debit that will never occur — confusing the student and generating support contacts from people wondering about the charge.

IF: insurance accepted → premium in recent activity, NOT upcoming

Active insurance is always visible on the home screen with the GradGuard claims number. Once enrolled, an insurance card appears on the home screen showing the policy status and GradGuard's claims phone number (800-918-2899). This number must be reachable at any time — not buried in settings.

Why: A student filing a claim after a medical withdrawal needs to reach GradGuard quickly — often in a stressful situation. Burying the claims number in settings means they can't find it when they need it most, defeating the value of the insurance product.

IF: insurance accepted → home screen insurance card visible
💳
How to Pay
Payment path selection, payment plan setup, and method enrollment
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S4 · New AP (Payer) Institution-configured
Cross-scenario rule: Returning students may have a saved payment method and/or a prior POT plan. Their "How to Pay" step is abbreviated — confirm prior method still valid, present new-term plan options. APs can set up their own payment path independently of the student's — each payer has a distinct method on file.

Two primary paths: Pay in Full or Pay Over Time (POT). The choice is presented clearly at the top of the payment step. The institution configures whether POT is offered, and may offer one or more distinct POT plans. If only one plan exists, the student is not shown a plan picker — they simply confirm the single plan.

Why: Students should not have to choose among payment plan options they don't need to see. When only one plan exists, eliminating the picker reduces steps and avoids creating a false sense of complexity.

Institution: POT enabled + plan count

POT plans require a down payment selection before the schedule is confirmed. The down payment amount and/or percentage is configurable per plan. The resulting installment schedule (number of payments, amount per installment, payment dates, plan end date) must be displayed in a natural-language summary — not a raw table — before the student commits.

Why: A raw installment table requires the student to mentally parse numbers. A natural-language summary ("4 payments of $1,250 starting November 1") communicates the same information in a form students can actually act on and remember.

Institution: down payment rules per plan

Card service fee (2.75%) must be disclosed before the student selects a payment method. The fee notice must appear as contextual copy on the payment method selection screen — not in a tooltip, not buried in disclosures. ACH (bank) payments must be clearly identified as having no service fee.

Why: Students who discover a service fee after selecting a card feel misled. Surfacing it before method selection allows them to make an informed choice — often switching to ACH to avoid the fee — and prevents post-payment disputes.

Required · Regulatory

Auto-pay enrollment for POT installments requires explicit disclosure. When the student selects a payment method for a POT plan, a clear notice explains that all future installments will be automatically charged to this method on their scheduled dates. The student must acknowledge this before the plan is confirmed — not buried in small print.

Why: Unexpected recurring charges are the leading cause of payment disputes and unauthorized transaction claims. Explicit acknowledgment before enrollment creates a clear consent record and reduces post-enrollment "I didn't know" contacts.

Required · RegulatoryIF: payment path = POT → auto-pay disclosure required

Supported payment methods: ACH (bank account) and credit/debit card. Additional methods (Apple Pay, PayPal, etc.) may be added in future iterations per the product vision. Institution may restrict available methods. If a method type is not configured by the institution, it is not shown.

Why: Showing payment method types the institution hasn't enabled — even as "coming soon" — creates confusion and support questions. The available set must exactly match what the institution has contracted and configured.

Institution: allowed payment method types
👥
Authorized Parties
Student-controlled access management for third-party payers and viewers
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3 · New AP — Single Payer S4 · New AP — Multi Payer S5 · AP Non-Payer S6 · Returning AP
Cross-scenario rule: The student is always the owner of authorized party access. APs cannot modify their own permissions — only the student can. Each AP scenario (S3–S6) will add AP-perspective requirements to this feature. As those scenarios are built, update this section to capture full business logic for each AP type and permission combination.

Students control who has access and at what level. During onboarding, the student is offered the opportunity to set up authorized parties. They specify: the AP's name and email, a balance visibility cap (percentage of the total balance the AP can see), and whether the AP can make payments. APs are managed within Nelnet's system — not within the institution's ERP.

Why: The student is the account owner and must remain in control of who sees and can pay their account. Managing APs within Nelnet (not the institution ERP) allows for granular permission levels that the ERP's access model cannot support.

Required

This step may be deferred during onboarding. The student can choose "I'll complete this later" on the AP invite screen. If they have started filling in any AP details, a partial-save modal is presented: they can save their progress and continue to the next step, or start over and skip the step entirely. Saved progress is pre-populated when they return.

Why: Students often need to ask a parent before inviting them — they may not have the AP's email address handy. Deferring without losing progress prevents abandonment of the full onboarding flow just because one optional step isn't ready to complete.

IF: partial data entered → partial-save modal on defer

Invited APs receive a Nelnet-issued invite link at their email address. The invite link allows the AP to create independent Nelnet credentials. They do not share the student's login. Their session is scoped to the permissions granted by the student.

Why: The AP has no institutional identity — they cannot use the student's SSO. A Nelnet-issued invite link bootstraps their access cleanly without requiring the institution's IT team to provision them, and ensures scoped access from the first login.

Required

Guest payment links are distinct from authorized party access. A guest payment link allows a one-time payment by a third party with zero ongoing access. The student sets a maximum payment cap (≤ open balance) and an optional note. The recipient cannot log in, cannot see the full account, and cannot make a second payment with the same link. The UI must make this distinction unambiguous — "guest payer" and "authorized party" must never appear interchangeable.

Why: A student who wants grandma to pay once should not be forced to grant her ongoing account access and visibility. Without a clear guest payment path, students either over-grant access (creating privacy and control issues) or turn away one-time helpers entirely.

Required · Critical

Multiple APs may be added during a single onboarding session. The student can add more than one authorized party before completing the onboarding flow. Each AP has independently-configured permissions. There is no hard limit specified — institution may configure a maximum if needed.

Why: Multi-payer arrangements (divorced parents, student + grandparent, scholarship sponsor + parent) are common. Requiring students to return post-onboarding to add additional APs creates an avoidable second trip through a setup flow.

Institution: AP count limit (optional)
📬
Communications
Contact information and notification preference management
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S6 · Authorized Parties
Cross-scenario rule: Each user (student or AP) has independent communication preferences. A student's preferences do not affect their APs, and vice versa. Returning users are taken directly to a confirmation/edit screen — they are not re-prompted to enter information already on file.

Primary email is pre-populated from the SSO token and is required. The student can update or add additional email addresses. At least one email address must always be on file.

Why: No duplicate entry — the email is already known. Requiring at least one email ensures all transactional communications (payment confirmations, plan reminders) have a delivery address for the lifetime of the account.

ERP / SSO: primary email

Students may add multiple email addresses and phone numbers. There is no single-value limit on contact info. Each additional address or number has an "Add another email / Add another phone" affordance. Any entry can be removed except the primary (SSO) email.

Why: Students often want payment confirmations to go to a parent's email as well as their own. Supporting multiple contact entries avoids the need for manual forwarding and ensures all parties with financial responsibility receive relevant notifications.

Required

Text (SMS) preferences are split into two independent categories: Informational and Marketing. Informational texts cover account activity — billing updates, payment confirmations, plan change alerts. Default is on. Marketing texts cover promotional content — default is off. These two categories are shown as separate, labeled toggles. Transactional confirmations (receipts, one-time passcodes) are always sent and are not shown as a user toggle.

Why: Bundling informational and marketing SMS into a single toggle forces students to choose between getting useful account alerts or no texts at all. Separating them lets students opt out of promotions without losing payment reminders — which directly supports collection rates.

Required

Phone number is required to enable SMS notifications. If no phone number is on file, SMS toggles are inactive and labeled "Add a phone number to enable." Once a number is added, the toggles become active.

Why: SMS cannot be sent without a phone number. Showing active toggles when no number is on file would create a misleading UX — the student thinks they've opted in but will never receive texts. The disabled state with a clear prompt prevents this confusion.

IF: no phone → SMS toggles disabled
📄
Disclosures & E-Signature
Sequential acknowledgment of institution and Nelnet disclosures
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S4 · New AP (Payer) Institution-configured count
Cross-scenario rule: Disclosure requirements vary by user type. Students typically have more disclosures than APs. Returning users who have previously signed disclosures may only need to re-sign if terms have changed. As additional scenarios are added, specify which disclosure sets apply to each user type.

Disclosures are presented as a sequential accordion — one section at a time. The student must open and read each disclosure section before the next one unlocks. They cannot skip ahead. The progress indicator shows how many sections remain. All sections must be acknowledged before the e-signature field activates.

Why: Presenting all disclosures at once makes it trivial to scroll past without reading. Sequential unlocking creates a reasonable acknowledgment path and provides a record that each section was opened — important for legal enforceability of the agreement.

Required · Regulatory

Institution configures the number and content of disclosure sections (default: 4). Disclosure content is pulled from the institution's configured disclosure templates. Nelnet may include a universal disclosure section in addition to institution-specific sections.

Why: Each institution has different legal agreements, refund policies, and enrollment terms. A fixed disclosure set would not meet the compliance needs of institutions with custom policies or state-specific requirements.

Institution: disclosure count + content

E-signature is required after all disclosure sections are acknowledged. The signature field requires the student to type their full name and check a confirmation checkbox. The typed name must be at least 3 non-whitespace characters. Submission is blocked until all sections are acknowledged, the name is typed, and the checkbox is checked.

Why: A typed name signature creates a legally defensible consent record — stronger than a simple checkbox alone. The blocking validation prevents the student from accidentally submitting without completing all required acknowledgment steps.

Required · Regulatory

Each disclosure section must be downloadable as a PDF. A "Download PDF" link is available within each expanded disclosure section. The PDF is generated from the same disclosure content shown on screen — not a different document.

Why: Students and institutions may need to reference disclosure terms later — for a payment dispute, a withdrawal situation, or an audit. A downloadable copy ensures the student has a record of exactly what they agreed to, without needing to contact the bursar.

Required
Features · Home Screen

Home Screen Features

Context

The home screen is the persistent hub a consumer returns to after completing onboarding. It surfaces the most important information and actions for their current account state — adapting in real time as charges post, plans change, payments are made, and authorized parties take action.

Requirements below define each home screen module independently. As more scenarios are added (APs, returning students), return here to extend each module's rules for those user types.

⚙️
Account Settings
Personal info, payment methods, authorized parties, and notification preferences
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S6 · Authorized Parties
Cross-scenario rule: Settings belong to the individual user. A student's settings page always shows authorized party management. An AP's settings page never includes AP management (APs cannot invite sub-parties). Returning students see pre-populated values from prior term.

Account Settings is accessible from the home screen at all times — not gated behind completion of any other action. A persistent settings entry point (gear icon or equivalent) must be available in the home screen header or navigation area.

Why: Students need to update their contact info, payment methods, or AP access at any point in the term — not just during onboarding. Gating settings access behind other actions creates a support burden when students can't find where to make a change.

Required

Settings contains four sub-sections: (1) Personal contact info — name, email addresses, phone numbers; (2) Payment methods — saved bank accounts and cards, with add/remove; (3) Authorized parties — view current APs, add new, remove, or update permissions; (4) Notification preferences — same informational/marketing SMS split as during onboarding.

Why: These four areas cover all post-onboarding self-service needs. Organizing them under a single Settings entry point reduces the number of places a student must look when they need to make a change to their account.

Required

Changes made in Settings take effect immediately and do not trigger re-onboarding. Updating a phone number, adding a payment method, or removing an AP does not restart or re-surface any previously completed onboarding steps.

Why: Re-triggering onboarding for any settings change would be deeply disruptive — forcing a student who just wants to update their phone number through insurance and disclosure steps again. Settings changes are independent of onboarding state.

Required

An AP can be removed by the student at any time from Settings. Removing an AP immediately revokes their access — they can no longer log in or view account information. An email notification is sent to the AP at the time of removal.

Why: Student circumstances change — a previously helpful payer may become a source of conflict. Immediate revocation protects the student's privacy and account control. Notifying the AP prevents confusion when they can no longer access the account.

Required
✅
To-dos
Outstanding actions that require the student's attention
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S6 · Authorized Parties
Cross-scenario rule: To-do items are scoped to the user's role. A student sees to-dos related to their account decisions and payments. An AP sees to-dos relevant to their specific responsibilities (e.g., a pending payment they were invited to make). To-dos for one user are never shown to another.

To-dos are action-required items that the user has not yet completed. Examples: unsigned disclosures, incomplete onboarding (deferred AP setup), payment due within 7 days, payment method expiring, open balance with no payment path set, AP invitation pending acceptance.

Why: The to-do list is the primary mechanism for guided UX post-onboarding. It tells users exactly what still needs their attention, eliminating the need to scan the full account to figure out what to do next.

Required

Each to-do links directly to the relevant action. Tapping a to-do item routes the user to the exact screen or step where they can complete the action — not to a generic settings page.

Why: To-dos that require navigating elsewhere to complete break the guided experience. A direct deep-link from alert to action is the difference between a useful prompt and a frustrating hint that still requires the user to find their own way.

Required

To-dos are automatically dismissed when the action is completed. No manual "dismiss" is needed for completed items — they disappear from the list. Time-sensitive items (payment past-due, method expired) remain until resolved even if previously acknowledged.

Why: Manual dismissal creates stale lists — users dismiss items without acting, then lose track of what's real. Auto-dismissal based on account state ensures the to-do list always reflects actual outstanding actions, not user cleanup behavior.

Required

When no to-dos exist, the section is either hidden or shows a neutral empty state. Do not show an empty to-do section with placeholder text that implies the user might be missing something. Empty state copy should be affirmative: e.g., "You're all caught up."

Why: An empty to-do list is a positive signal — it means the student is on top of their account. Neutral or negative empty states ("Nothing here yet") undermine that signal and can create anxiety. The tone should confirm the student has nothing left to do.

Required
🕐
Recent Activity
All account transactions from the last 30 days
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S4 · New AP (Payer)
Cross-scenario rule: Returning students' recent activity spans the current and prior term if within 30 days. APs only see activity they themselves initiated, unless the student has granted full account visibility. The 30-day window is the same for all user types.

Recent Activity shows all account transactions posted in the last 30 days. Transaction types include: payments made (by student or AP), credits applied, financial aid posted, institutional fees charged, tuition insurance premium charged, plan enrollment fees.

Why: Students log in after receiving a notification — they want to verify what happened. A complete 30-day activity feed lets them confirm payments landed, credits posted, and fees were charged correctly without calling the bursar.

RequiredERP: transaction feed

Tuition insurance premium appears in Recent Activity — not in Upcoming Payments. Because the premium is charged at the moment of acceptance (not on a future schedule), it is a completed transaction. Showing it in Upcoming would incorrectly imply it's a future obligation.

Why: Miscategorizing a completed charge as an upcoming one would cause students to believe they owe money again in the future — generating both anxiety and a support contact to ask about it.

IF: GradGuard enabled + student accepted → premium in recent activity

Each activity item shows: description, date, amount, and status. Status values: Posted, Pending, Reversed. Amount is signed: payments are shown as negative (reducing balance), charges are positive.

Why: Without status and signed amounts, students cannot tell whether a payment has cleared or is still pending — and cannot easily tell what reduced their balance vs. what added to it. This distinction is required for self-service balance reconciliation.

Required

Items are sorted chronologically, most recent first. If there are more than a practical display limit (e.g., 5 items), a "View all activity" link reveals the full list or navigates to a dedicated transaction history screen.

Why: Students checking on a recent payment want to see it first — not buried below older transactions. Most-recent-first matches the mental model of someone verifying "did my payment go through."

Required
📅
Upcoming Payments
Scheduled payments due in the next 30 days
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S4 · New AP (Payer)
Cross-scenario rule: APs who have their own payment plan see their own upcoming installments — not the student's full schedule (unless explicitly granted). The 30-day window is standard across user types.

Upcoming Payments shows only scheduled installments due within the next 30 days. This section does not include: one-time payments the user may choose to make, the tuition insurance premium (already charged), or charges not yet due. It reflects auto-pay commitments — scheduled, automatic debits from the payment method on file.

Why: The purpose of this section is to help students anticipate auto-debits so they can ensure funds are available. Including discretionary or already-completed charges muddies this signal — students need to know specifically what will be charged automatically and when.

RequiredIF: payment path = POT → upcoming installments shown

Each upcoming item shows: due date, amount, and payment method to be charged. If the payment method on file has expired or is flagged as invalid, the item is highlighted as requiring attention — and a to-do item is simultaneously generated.

Why: A student needs to know which card or account will be debited — not just the amount. Surfacing an expired method warning before the debit date gives them time to update it, preventing a failed payment and the fee or penalty that follows.

Required

When no payments are due in the next 30 days, the Upcoming section is hidden. Do not show an empty state for this section — it should not exist on screen unless there is at least one upcoming item to show.

Why: An empty Upcoming Payments section with copy like "No payments due" could be misread as "you have no upcoming obligations at all" — which may not be true for students whose next installment is 31+ days away. Hiding it entirely avoids false reassurance.

Required
📊
Account Presentment
Current balance snapshot, plan status, and enrollment context
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S4 · New AP (Payer)
Cross-scenario rule: APs see only the balance amounts the student has granted visibility to — if the student set a 50% cap, the AP sees 50% of the actual balance. Returning students see current-term balance, with prior-term context available on request. Balance is always synced from ERP in real time — never cached or stale.

Account Presentment is the primary balance summary on the home screen. It shows: total charges for the current term, financial aid applied, net balance, current open balance (amount not covered by a payment plan or prior payments), and amount currently on a payment plan.

Why: Students return to the home screen to verify their account state. Showing all balance components in one place — charges, aid, plan coverage, open balance — eliminates the need to navigate to multiple screens to understand the full financial picture.

RequiredERP: real-time balance

Balance components are shown as a clear breakdown — not a single number. Students should be able to understand at a glance what they owe, what's covered by aid, and what remains to be paid vs. what's already on a plan. A single "Balance: $X,XXX" without context fails this requirement.

Why: Research consistently shows students seek one primary number then work backwards to understand it. A single unexplained number triggers questions — "Does this include my financial aid? My plan?" A breakdown answers those questions proactively and reduces contacts.

Required

When enrolled in Pay Over Time, show the active plan status inline. Plan summary: plan name, number of remaining installments, next payment amount and date. The student should not need to navigate elsewhere to know when their next payment is.

Why: The next installment date is the most time-sensitive piece of information for a student on a plan. Surfacing it on the home screen — without requiring navigation — reduces missed payments and gives students advance notice to ensure funds are available.

IF: payment path = POT → plan summary visible on home screen

Open balance is $0 when the student is fully enrolled in a POT plan. The math must always resolve: net balance − down payment − on-plan amount = $0 open balance. No rounding artifact should produce a non-zero open balance when the student has enrolled their entire net balance in a plan.

Why: A phantom open balance shown to a fully-enrolled student generates an immediate support contact — they will call asking what they still owe. This is a high-frequency, entirely preventable contact category.

Required · Bug prevention
⚡
Quick Actions
Dynamic, prioritized shortcuts surfaced based on account state
S1 · First Time Student S2 · Returning Student S3–S6 · Authorized Parties
Cross-scenario rule: Quick actions are determined by account state, not user type alone. The same logic engine evaluates conditions for students and APs — but the available action set differs by role. APs never see "Add Authorized Party." Students see "View AP Payment Plan" only when an AP has enrolled in one. As scenarios are added, extend the priority table below to include AP-specific actions and their conditions.

Quick actions are dynamic — they appear, change, and disappear based on real-time account state. The system evaluates conditions on every home screen load and renders only the actions currently relevant to this user. No quick action is ever hard-coded to always display.

Why: A student who has already set up APs and paid in full should not see "Add Authorized Party" or "Pay Balance" cluttering their home screen. Hard-coded always-on actions quickly become noise — reducing the usefulness of the entire quick actions section for students in later account states.

Required

Quick actions follow a strict priority order. When multiple actions are valid simultaneously, they are displayed in the order defined in the priority table below. The highest-priority action is always shown first. Institution configuration may suppress individual actions, but cannot reorder them.

Why: When multiple actions are valid, their order communicates urgency and relevance. An open balance outstanding is more pressing than reviewing an AP plan. Fixed priority ordering ensures the student always sees the most important action first — regardless of which happened to evaluate to true last.

Required

Quick Action Priority Table — Student Scenarios

# Action Label Condition (shows when…) Destination / Result
1 Pay Balance Open balance > $0 One-time payment flow
2 Set Up Payment Plan No active POT plan AND institution offers POT Payment plan setup flow
3 Add Tuition Insurance GradGuard enabled AND student has not yet accepted or declined Insurance offer screen
4 Add Authorized Party No authorized parties on file AP invite screen
5 Manage Payment Methods No saved payment method on file Payment methods settings
6 View AP Payment Plan At least one AP has an active POT plan Read-only AP POT plan view
7 Tuition Insurance Student has accepted insurance (active policy) Insurance details & GradGuard claims (800-918-2899)

Why: The priority table encodes the product's judgment about what matters most to a student at any given account state. Documenting it formally prevents ad-hoc reordering in implementation and ensures the product experience consistently guides students toward the most important next action.

Priority order is fixedInstitution may suppress individual actions

The maximum number of quick actions displayed simultaneously is determined by the UI layout — not a business rule cap. All valid actions from the priority table should be shown. If the layout needs to limit visible items (e.g., for mobile), a "See all" affordance must reveal the remaining actions — they must never be permanently hidden.

Why: Hiding valid actions because of a business-rule cap would mean a student with an active POT plan, no payment method on file, and an AP pending — all simultaneously valid conditions — might miss a critical action. Layout constraints should never silently suppress account-relevant prompts.

Required

Each quick action has a label, a one-line supporting description, and an icon. The supporting description provides context so the user understands what tapping the action will do — not just what it is. Example: "Tuition Insurance" alone is less useful than "Tuition Insurance · GradGuard · claims: 800-918-2899".

Why: A label alone requires the user to know what the action does before tapping it. A supporting description eliminates that knowledge requirement — especially for first-time users who may not know what "Guest Payment Link" or "AP Pay Over Time Plans" means.

Required

When no quick actions are valid, the Quick Actions section is hidden. This state is rare (fully paid, no pending items, insurance already decided, APs already set up, payment method on file) but must be handled gracefully — never show an empty quick actions section.

Why: An empty quick actions section with no content implies the product has nothing useful to show — which signals a broken or incomplete state to the student. Hiding it entirely is a cleaner result that doesn't raise unnecessary questions.

Required
Features

Pay Over Time Features

Feature requirements for the Pay Over Time consumer experience — the enrollment flow, plan confirmation, ongoing plan management, balance change handling, and default recovery flow. These requirements apply to all plan types (Standard, Past-Due, LTPP, International, Hidden, Guarantee, Custom) unless a specific plan type section calls out an exception.

Features · Pay Over Time

Plan Enrollment Flow

Consumer-facing requirements for how a student or authorized party enrolls in a Pay Over Time plan — from seeing available plan offers through TILA disclosure acceptance and payment method entry.

Offer Display & Eligibility

Student / AP

Quick Pick Single Offer. When exactly one plan is available for the student's current balance and term, the platform presents a Quick Pick card that pre-selects that plan and advances directly to the Schedule Selection step — no grid selection required.

Why: Reduces friction for the majority of students who have only one eligible plan, minimizing drop-off on the most common enrollment path.

Student / AP

Multi-Offer Selection Grid. When two or more plans are available, the platform displays a card grid with one card per plan showing plan name, number of installments, estimated installment amount, enrollment fee, and total amount financed. The student must explicitly select a card before proceeding.

Why: Allows students to compare offers side-by-side and make an informed choice — a Reg Z best practice and a requirement when institutions offer tiered plan structures.

Student / AP

No-Plan-Available State. When no plan is available (balance outside eligible range, term enrollment window closed, student already on an active plan, etc.), the platform displays an explanatory message stating the specific reason and provides a contact path to the bursar office. The message must not use generic error language.

Why: Students who cannot enroll deserve a clear explanation rather than a dead end, reducing unnecessary bursar contact volume for cases where the reason can be stated automatically.

Student / AP

Eligibility Window Enforcement. The enrollment offer is only surfaced during the institution-configured enrollment window for the term. Outside that window, the Pay Over Time entry point is hidden or shows an informational message indicating when enrollment opens or closed.

Why: Institutions must control when plans can be created to align with their billing and ERP processing cycles; surfacing the option outside the window creates support burden and invalid enrollments.

Student / AP

Existing Active Plan Guard. A student with an existing active plan for the current term cannot enroll in a second plan for the same term unless parallel agreements are enabled. The offer display step detects this state and presents a message linking the student to their existing plan rather than offering a new enrollment path.

Why: Prevents duplicate plan creation which would create accounting reconciliation issues with the institution's ERP and potential double-charging.

Student / AP

Minimum Balance Eligibility Messaging. When a student's eligible balance falls below the institution-configured minimum, the platform informs the student that their balance is below the minimum required for a Pay Over Time plan and displays the minimum threshold.

Why: Transparent eligibility messaging prevents confusion and reduces support tickets from students who attempted to enroll on a low remaining balance.

Schedule Selection

Student / AP

Installment Count Picker. For plans that offer multiple installment count options (e.g., 3, 4, or 5 payments), the schedule selection step presents each option as a selectable tile showing count, per-installment amount, and total financed. Quick Pick defaults to the institution-configured default count (typically the highest count available).

Why: Giving students control over installment count improves plan completion rates, as students can choose a cadence that fits their cash flow.

Student / AP

Payment Day Selection. When the institution enables payment day selection, the student may choose their preferred day of month (from institution-configured options) during schedule selection. The platform recalculates projected installment dates in real time as the selection changes and displays the resulting first payment date.

Why: Aligning installment dates to student payroll or financial aid disbursement dates reduces failed payment rates and improves plan completion.

Student / AP

Full Eligible Balance Requirement. Pay Over Time plans must cover the student's full eligible balance — partial enrollment (covering only a portion of the eligible balance) is not permitted. The balance amount used for plan calculations is fetched from the institution's SIS/ERP at the time of enrollment and is not editable by the consumer.

Why: Partial enrollment creates reconciliation complexity with institutional billing systems and may leave an unpaid balance that triggers separate collection activity.

Student / AP

Balance Amount Display with Pre-Disclosure Math. The schedule selection screen displays: the total plan amount (balance + enrollment fee), the number of payments, the per-installment amount, and the first installment date. All figures must match the TILA disclosure that will be shown in the next step.

Why: Presenting the math before the disclosure reduces the cognitive load of the TILA screen and ensures consumers have already processed the key numbers before legally accepting them.

Student / AP

Rounding Transparency. When installment amounts do not divide evenly, the platform applies the institution-configured rounding rule and displays a note on the schedule screen explaining that one installment may differ by a small amount due to rounding.

Why: Unexplained installment amount variance is a top consumer support contact reason; proactive disclosure eliminates that confusion.

TILA & Reg Z Pre-Disclosure

Student / AP

Required TILA Disclosure Fields. Before a consumer can confirm enrollment, the platform must display all of the following in a TILA-formatted disclosure block: (1) Total Amount Financed, (2) Number of Payments, (3) Amount of Each Scheduled Payment, (4) Enrollment Fee, (5) First Payment Date, (6) APR (0.00% for standard non-interest-bearing plans), (7) Finance Charge ($0.00 for standard plans), and (8) Total of Payments.

Why: Federal Regulation Z requires these disclosures to be provided before a consumer is bound to a credit-like repayment agreement; omission creates regulatory exposure for the institution.

Student / AP

Auto-Debit Authorization Language. The TILA disclosure must include the institution-configured auto-debit authorization statement, which must identify: the plan name, the payment method to be charged, the recurring installment amount, and the consumer's right to revoke authorization. The statement text is configurable per institution but must include all four elements.

Why: NACHA rules and most state consumer protection statutes require explicit, written auto-debit authorization that names the payee, amount, and revocation rights.

Student / AP

Right-to-Cancel Period Disclosure. If the institution configures a right-to-cancel period (e.g., 3 business days after enrollment), the disclosure must state the cancellation deadline date and the method for exercising cancellation. Plans without a cancellation period must still display a statement indicating the enrollment is binding upon confirmation.

Why: Several states require a cooling-off period for installment payment agreements; institutions in those states require this to be visible in the enrollment flow.

Student / AP

Disclosure Version Persistence. The exact text of the TILA disclosure shown to the consumer at enrollment is stored in immutable form tied to the plan record. The stored version, disclosure timestamp, and consumer IP address are accessible in the plan's change history for compliance audit purposes.

Why: If a consumer disputes the terms they agreed to, the institution must be able to produce the exact disclosure text and evidence that the consumer viewed and accepted it.

Student / AP

Scroll-to-Unlock Acceptance. The "Continue to Payment Method" button on the TILA disclosure screen is disabled until the consumer has scrolled to the bottom of the disclosure content or explicitly checked an acknowledgment checkbox. The mechanism used is configured per institution.

Why: Documented evidence that the consumer accessed the full disclosure strengthens the institution's position in any dispute and aligns with best practices for electronic consent.

Payment Method Entry at Enrollment

Student / AP

New Card or ACH Entry. A consumer with no saved payment methods is presented with an inline card entry form (card number, expiration, CVV, billing zip) or an ACH entry form (routing number, account number, account type). The form is embedded in the enrollment flow — the consumer does not navigate to a separate payment settings page.

Why: Requiring navigation away from the enrollment flow to add a payment method is a primary abandonment point; inline entry removes that friction.

Student / AP

Saved Method Selection. A consumer with one or more saved payment methods sees a list of those methods (card brand + last 4, or bank name + last 4) and can select one for the plan. A "Use a different method" option allows entry of a new method without removing existing saved methods.

Why: Re-entering payment details is a friction point for returning users; saved method selection accelerates re-enrollment between terms.

Student / AP

Service Fee Disclosure at Method Selection. When a consumer selects or enters a credit card, the platform immediately displays the applicable service fee rate (e.g., "A 2.75% service fee applies to credit card payments. This fee is charged per installment in addition to the installment amount.") before the consumer proceeds. ACH methods must display a $0 service fee confirmation.

Why: Surprise fees at confirmation are the leading cause of plan abandonment; disclosing the fee at the point of method selection gives consumers the opportunity to switch to ACH before committing.

Student / AP

Payment Method Validation. Card entries are validated via Luhn check client-side and authorization attempt server-side before enrollment confirmation. ACH entries are validated via routing number lookup (ABA check). Invalid entries display inline field-level error messages identifying the specific issue.

Why: Pre-validating the payment method before plan creation prevents the partial enrollment state that results when a plan is created but the initial charge fails due to an invalid method.

Confirmation & Enrollment Email

Student / AP

Confirmation Screen Contents. The post-enrollment confirmation screen must display: plan name, term, total plan amount, number of installments, per-installment amount, enrollment fee charged, first payment date, payment method (card brand + last 4 or bank name + last 4), and a plan reference number. A "Return to home" button is the primary CTA.

Why: A complete confirmation screen reduces immediate post-enrollment contact volume by giving the consumer all the information they need to verify their enrollment was successful.

Student / AP

Enrollment Confirmation Email. An enrollment confirmation email is sent to the consumer's institution email address (and secondary email if configured) within 5 minutes of successful enrollment. The email includes all fields shown on the confirmation screen plus a link to the consumer portal and the institution's bursar contact information.

Why: Email confirmation provides the consumer with a durable record of their enrollment details that they can reference without logging into the portal, reducing repeat logins and confusion at payment time.

Student / AP

Home Screen Plan Card Immediate. Immediately upon successful enrollment, the consumer's home screen displays an active plan card on next page load showing: plan name, next payment date, next payment amount, and remaining balance. The active plan card replaces any "Enroll in Pay Over Time" CTA for the same term.

Why: Immediate home screen visibility confirms the enrollment succeeded and transitions the consumer into plan management mode, reducing duplicate enrollment attempts.

Institution / ERP

ERP Enrollment Notification. The institution's ERP or SIS receives an enrollment notification event within the institution-configured sync window (default: within 15 minutes, maximum: next nightly batch). The notification payload includes: student ID, plan ID, term, total plan amount, installment schedule, enrollment date, and enrollment fee amount.

Why: Institutions must reflect the plan enrollment in their student accounts receivable records to update the student's balance status and prevent duplicate billing activity on the covered balance.

Features · Pay Over Time

Confirmation & Agreement

Requirements for the plan confirmation screen, the binding agreement acceptance step, and what happens in the immediate post-enrollment state.

Pre-Confirmation Summary Screen

Student / AP

Complete Plan Summary Before Confirmation. The pre-confirmation screen must display all of the following before the "Confirm enrollment" button appears: plan name, term, covered balance, number of installments, per-installment amount, enrollment fee (labeled "charged today"), total amount to be paid, first payment date, and payment method (last 4 digits only, with card brand or bank name).

Why: Consumers must have a complete, scannable summary of their commitment before they take the binding action; an incomplete summary is grounds for dispute that the institution cannot defend.

Student / AP

Edit Path from Summary. Each major section of the summary (plan selection, schedule, payment method) has an associated "Change" link that navigates the consumer back to that step without resetting subsequent selections. The consumer returns to the summary screen after making a change.

Why: Without a clear edit path, consumers who notice an error at the summary step may abandon enrollment entirely rather than starting over.

Student / AP

Projected Installment Schedule Table. The confirmation summary includes a collapsible table showing all projected installment dates and amounts. For plans where service fees apply per installment, the table shows both the principal installment amount and the service fee for each row.

Why: Consumers who can see the full schedule at confirmation have lower rates of surprise-related contacts when charges process — they have already reviewed what to expect and when.

Agreement Acceptance

Student / AP

Explicit Multi-Element Acceptance. The consumer must take an explicit acceptance action for each of the following before enrollment is processed: (1) TILA / Reg Z disclosure, (2) auto-debit authorization, and (3) financial responsibility statement. Acceptance is captured via individual checkboxes or a combined explicit button with clear label text. Pre-checked checkboxes are not permitted.

Why: Bundling all acceptance into a single implicit action does not satisfy Reg Z requirements for documented consumer consent to each distinct legal obligation.

Student / AP

Agreement Timestamp and Document Version Storage. Upon enrollment confirmation, the platform stores: the UTC timestamp of the consumer's agreement action, the version identifier of the TILA disclosure template used, the exact disclosure text rendered to the consumer, and the consumer's session IP address. This record is immutable and retained for a minimum of 7 years.

Why: Institutions are subject to audit and must be able to produce evidence of consumer agreement, including the exact terms presented, for any plan within the retention window.

Student / AP

Financial Responsibility Statement. The financial responsibility statement — configurable per institution — must acknowledge that: the balance underlying the plan represents a real obligation to the institution, failure to complete plan payments may result in the balance returning to collections or a hold on records, and enrollment in the plan does not constitute a waiver of the underlying debt.

Why: Without explicit acknowledgment, some consumers assume the plan replaces the underlying balance obligation rather than structuring its payment, creating disputes after plan default.

Enrollment Fee Processing

Student / AP

Fee Charged at Confirmation. The enrollment fee is processed as a payment transaction at the moment the consumer confirms enrollment — not deferred to the first installment date. The plan is not created in an active state until the enrollment fee transaction is confirmed as successfully authorized by the payment processor.

Why: Deferred fee collection creates a class of "zero-cost" plan starts where the consumer benefits from the plan without paying the setup cost, creating revenue leakage for the institution.

Student / AP

Fee Payment Failure Behavior. If the enrollment fee charge is declined or returns an error, the plan is not created. The consumer sees a clear, specific error message and is returned to the payment method selection step with their previously entered method details pre-populated for correction.

Why: Creating a plan in an active state before the enrollment fee is collected forces the institution into a manual recovery process; blocking plan creation on fee failure is cleaner operationally.

Student / AP

No Partial Enrollment State. The system must operate as an atomic enrollment transaction: either all of the following succeed together — agreement stored, enrollment fee charged, plan record created — or none of them are committed. A partial state is a system fault condition and must be surfaced for operational review.

Why: Partial enrollment states create both financial reconciliation problems and consumer confusion (consumer believes they are enrolled when they are not, or vice versa).

Student / AP

Retry with Different Method. After an enrollment fee failure, the consumer may enter an entirely different payment method and retry. The retry does not require restarting the enrollment flow from the plan selection step; the previously accepted TILA disclosure and agreement are preserved for the retry attempt.

Why: Requiring a full restart after a payment failure dramatically increases abandonment; preserving the agreement state through a method change keeps the consumer in the funnel.

Post-Enrollment State

Student / AP

Plan in Communication History. The enrollment event — confirmation email sent, TILA acceptance recorded, enrollment fee receipt — appears as the earliest entries in the plan's communication history tab within the consumer portal. Communication history entries are timestamped, labeled by event type, and linked to any associated receipt or document.

Why: A complete communication history starting from enrollment gives the consumer a single in-app audit trail and reduces the need for consumers to search their email inbox for plan records.

Institution / Finance Admin

Admin Enrollment Visibility. Finance Admin and CSR roles see the newly enrolled plan in the admin plan management view within 5 minutes of enrollment. The plan is marked as "Active" and shows the full schedule, payment method last 4, and enrollment timestamp. Admin view does not require a page refresh or manual sync action.

Why: Finance staff frequently receive student calls immediately after enrollment; near-real-time admin visibility allows staff to confirm enrollment and answer questions without delays.

Features · Pay Over Time

Plan Management

Plan Summary — Always visible on home screen. While a student has an active Pay Over Time plan, the home screen permanently displays: plan name, total remaining balance, current installment amount, next payment date, and payment method on file. A "View full schedule" link expands the complete payment schedule showing all past and future installments.

Why: Students need a clear, persistent view of their plan so they are never surprised by a charge. Surfacing the next payment date prominently reduces support contacts driven by "I didn't know a payment was coming."

Plan Owner Attribution. In multi-actor scenarios (e.g., a parent enrolled a student), the plan summary must display who the plan owner is. The label "Plan enrolled by [Name]" appears in the plan summary. Both the student and the plan owner can view the plan. Only the plan owner can modify the payment method or cancel the plan.

Why: When a parent sets up a plan on behalf of a student, the student's portal should reflect that context — otherwise a student calling support doesn't understand why they can't edit the plan. Clear ownership attribution prevents confusion and reduces support escalations.

Update Payment Method. The plan owner can update the payment method on an active plan at any time before the next scheduled payment. The new payment method takes effect on the next scheduled installment. A confirmation is shown on screen and sent via the student's preferred notification channel.

Why: Payment methods expire, cards get reissued, and bank accounts change. Restricting method updates leads to failed payments and plan defaults that could have been avoided.

Required

Cancel Plan — with Bursar escalation messaging. The plan owner can initiate plan cancellation from the portal. Before cancellation is confirmed, the student sees a safety screen that: (1) shows the full remaining balance that will become due immediately upon cancellation, (2) displays the Bursar's Office contact information (phone + email, sourced from institution configuration), and (3) requires an explicit "I understand" acknowledgment before confirming. Cancellation sends an immediate notification to both the student and the institution.

Why: Plan cancellation is a high-stakes, often impulsive action. The safety screen surfaces the financial consequence (full balance immediately due) and gives the student a direct path to speak with the Bursar before they make an irreversible decision. Escalation contact is institution-specific because bursar office hours and channels vary.

Required

Scheduled Payment Confirmation. After each scheduled installment is successfully processed, the student receives a notification showing: amount charged, last 4 digits of the payment method, remaining balance on the plan, and next scheduled payment date.

Why: Students enrolled in auto-pay plans have high anxiety about mystery charges on their bank statements. Proactive "your payment processed" notifications dramatically reduce "what was this charge?" support contacts.

Pause Plan (institution-configured). If the institution has enabled plan pausing, the plan owner can request a one-cycle pause from the portal. A paused plan skips the next installment and extends the plan end date by one period. The institution must explicitly enable this feature; it is off by default.

Why: Some institutions use pausing as a retention tool — students facing a temporary hardship pause rather than cancel. Making it institution-controlled prevents it from being abused as a default payment avoidance mechanism.

Installment Schedule View

Student / AP

Full Installment Schedule Display. The consumer can access a full installment schedule view from the home screen plan card that lists every installment in the plan — past and future — with each row showing: installment number, scheduled date, amount, and status (Processed, Upcoming, Failed, Skipped, or Cancelled).

Why: A full schedule view is the most common thing a consumer checks when they want to understand their plan status; without it, they contact the bursar for information the platform could provide.

Student / AP

Schedule Accessible from Home Plan Card. The installment schedule view is reachable in two taps from the home screen: one tap on the plan card to open the plan detail, and one tap on "View full schedule" to open the schedule list. The route does not require navigating into account settings or a separate menu.

Why: Schedule access buried in menus is a primary driver of "where do I see my payments?" support contacts; a prominent path from the plan card is the standard consumer expectation.

Student / AP

PDF / Print Export of Schedule. From the installment schedule view, the consumer can export or print a PDF version of the full schedule. The PDF includes: institution name, plan name, student name, plan ID, enrollment date, and all schedule rows with the same fields shown in the on-screen view. The export is generated on-demand and does not require a CSR to produce it.

Why: Students frequently need a printed or saved copy of their installment schedule for personal financial records, scholarship offices, or employer tuition reimbursement submissions.

Student / AP

Remaining Balance Display. The schedule view prominently displays the current remaining plan balance (total plan amount minus all processed principal installments). The remaining balance updates after each processed installment and after any ad-hoc payment. The remaining balance figure is clearly labeled and differentiated from the per-installment amount.

Why: Consumers frequently confuse the per-installment amount with the remaining balance; explicit display of both eliminates the most common plan math confusion.

Privacy Rules Between Student and AP

Student / Authorized Party

Plan Owner Full Access. The plan owner (the student on whose account the plan was created) can view all plan details including: full installment schedule, payment method card brand and last 4, all receipt and communication history events, and plan management actions (update method, cancel, make ad-hoc payment).

Why: The student is the financially responsible party and must have complete visibility into the plan that covers their balance.

Authorized Party (View-Only)

AP View-Only Access Scope. An Authorized Party granted view-only access may see: plan name, plan status (Active / Defaulted / Cancelled), next payment date, next payment amount, and remaining balance. An AP with view-only access must NOT see: the payment method card number (even last 4), full payment history details, or any management actions.

Why: Authorized Parties are often parents or guardians who need high-level plan visibility but should not have access to the student's payment instrument details, which may belong to the student personally.

Authorized Party (Paying AP)

Paying AP Access Scope. An Authorized Party granted paying access may view the payment method, update the payment method, make ad-hoc payments, and view receipts — but cannot cancel the plan or change plan structure. The distinction between paying AP and plan owner is displayed in the plan detail header.

Why: Families where a parent is the paying party need full payment method visibility and management capability; restricting this forces students to act as intermediaries for payment operations.

Student / AP / Institution Admin

Privacy Rules Enforced at API Level. Access scope restrictions on payment method visibility and plan management actions are enforced server-side in the API authorization layer — not only in the UI. A request from a view-only AP token to retrieve payment method details must return a 403 response regardless of the client making the request.

Why: UI-only privacy enforcement can be bypassed by direct API calls; server-side enforcement is the only defensible control for sensitive financial data.

Ad-Hoc / Early Payment on Plan

Student / AP

Ad-Hoc Payment Availability. A consumer with an active plan can initiate an additional payment against the plan balance at any time — not only on a scheduled installment date. The "Make a payment" option is accessible from the plan detail screen and from the plan card on the home screen. Ad-hoc payments are available for plans in Active status only; defaulted or cancelled plans do not offer this option.

Why: Students who receive financial aid, scholarships, or gift money mid-term want to reduce their plan balance proactively; blocking this forces them to wait for scheduled installments and pay more in fees over time.

Student / AP

Ad-Hoc Payment Amount. The consumer can enter any payment amount between a platform minimum ($10.00) and the full remaining plan balance. The entry field displays the current remaining balance as a reference. A payment equal to the remaining balance pays off the plan in full.

Why: Constraining ad-hoc payments to specific amounts reduces their utility; open-amount entry matches consumer expectations for online bill payment.

Institution / Finance Admin

Ad-Hoc Payment Balance Reduction Modes. The institution configures how an ad-hoc payment affects the remaining installment schedule. Three modes are supported: (a) Proportional Reduction — future installments are recalculated proportionally; (b) Skip Next — the next scheduled installment is eliminated and the remaining balance continues on the existing schedule; (c) Shorten Plan — the end date is moved earlier by eliminating trailing installments. The configured mode applies to all ad-hoc payments on plans at that institution.

Why: Different institutions have different ERP allocation models; a configurable mode allows each institution to select the approach that aligns with their accounts receivable system.

Student / AP

Immediate Ad-Hoc Processing. Ad-hoc payments are processed in real time (not batched with the nightly installment run). The consumer sees a processing confirmation screen immediately after submission and a receipt in communication history within 5 minutes of successful processing. The remaining balance on the plan card updates within the same session.

Why: Real-time processing with immediate balance update confirms to the consumer that their payment was received and applied, preventing duplicate payment attempts.

Student / AP

Ad-Hoc Payment Receipt. The consumer receives an email receipt for each ad-hoc payment showing: payment amount, payment method used, date and time processed, new remaining plan balance, and the revised next installment amount (if the configured mode changes future installment amounts). The receipt is also logged in the plan's communication history.

Why: A receipt that includes the updated schedule impact gives the consumer immediate visibility into how their extra payment changed their plan, reinforcing the value of making additional payments.

Features · Pay Over Time

Balance Change Handling
