⬡ See Prototype: Charges Added After Plan Exists

New Charge Alert — Prominent "to-do" card. When a new charge is added to the student's account after an active Pay Over Time plan exists, and that charge is not covered by the plan, the student's home screen immediately displays a distinct informational card: "New charge added to your account — not covered by your plan." The card shows the charge description, amount, and a direct action button to pay it or manage it. This card persists until the charge is resolved.

Why: Students on a plan assume all charges will be automatically handled. Without a prominent, proactive alert they will not discover the uncovered balance until it becomes delinquent. The card must be impossible to miss — not a buried notification.

Required

Dual Balance View — plan balance separate from open balance. When both an active plan and an uncovered open balance exist simultaneously, the student sees both clearly separated: (1) "On your payment plan: $X remaining, $Y/month" and (2) "Open balance not on plan: $Z — action required." The two balances are never merged or aggregated in a way that obscures what is and is not covered.

Why: Merging balances creates confusion about what the scheduled payment covers. Dual-view gives the student full clarity: their plan is on track, but there is a separate item needing attention.

Required

Balance Adjustment Preference — student chooses how new charges affect the plan. When a new charge is added mid-plan and the student elects to add it to their existing plan (if the institution allows), they are presented with an explicit choice: (A) Keep current installment amount and extend the plan end date, or (B) Keep the same plan end date and increase the installment amount. The student must select one option before the plan is recalculated. A before/after comparison is shown for each option before confirmation.

Why: This is a meaningful financial decision. Choosing for the student (defaulting to one option) creates resentment when the outcome surprises them. Showing both options with explicit numbers empowers the student and reduces disputes about why their monthly payment changed.

Required

New Charge Notification. When a new charge is added to the account while a plan is active, the student receives an immediate notification (via preferred channel: email/SMS/push) containing: the charge description and amount, a link to view it in the portal, and a clear statement that the charge is not covered by the existing plan and requires action.

Why: Students are not monitoring their portal daily. A push notification ensures they are made aware of the uncovered charge before it goes overdue, not after.

Credit / Charge Removal — automatic plan recalculation. When a charge is removed from the student's account (add/drop, institutional correction, financial aid applied) and that charge was included in the active plan, the plan balance is automatically reduced. The student sees a notification showing: the removed amount, the new remaining plan balance, and the updated installment amount or end date (per the student's previously stated preference). No student action is required for a reduction.

Why: Students who drop a class expect their balance to decrease. If the plan amount stays the same after a credit, students will call support to dispute the "overcharge." Automatic recalculation with transparent notification prevents that confusion.

Features · Pay Over Time

Default & Recovery

Requirements for how the platform handles failed installment payments — from first notification through escalation, plan cancellation, and the state the consumer encounters after default.

⬡ See Prototype: 4b — Defaulted Plan

Credit / Debit Card Decline Handling

Student / AP

Immediate Decline Notification. When a scheduled installment charge is declined by the card processor, the consumer receives a notification (email + in-app) within 30 minutes of the attempted charge. The notification specifies the amount that was attempted, the card last 4 that was charged, and a direct link to update their payment method.

Why: Prompt notification gives the consumer the maximum time to resolve the payment method issue before the retry window closes or the plan enters default.

Institution / Finance Admin

Configurable Retry Logic. The institution configures the retry schedule for declined card charges from three options: (a) Retry same day after a 4-hour delay; (b) Retry after a configured number of days (1–7); (c) No auto-retry (consumer must manually update method and trigger retry). The configured retry behavior is applied consistently to all plans at the institution.

Why: Retry timing preferences vary significantly between institutions; some prefer aggressive same-day retry while others prefer to give students time to resolve the issue without additional declines that may affect their credit standing.

Student / AP

Consumer Notification Per Retry Attempt. Each automatic retry attempt — whether successful or declined — generates a consumer notification. Failed retry notifications include the retry count, how many attempts remain before escalation, and a method update link.

Why: Consumers who do not know retries are occurring may be surprised by a charge that processes on a retry; transparency about each attempt prevents confusion about unexpected charges.

Institution / Finance Admin

Decline Code Logging. Every decline event records the processor decline code in the plan's payment audit trail. Decline codes are visible to Finance Admin in the CSR plan detail view and are included in the plan failure reporting export.

Why: Decline codes are necessary for diagnosing whether failures are systemic (invalid card) vs. transient (insufficient funds) and for making informed decisions about retry strategy.

Bank Return (ACH) Handling

Student / AP

Return Code-Specific Consumer Messaging. ACH return messages are tailored by return code category: R01/R09 (insufficient funds) — "Your bank returned this payment due to insufficient funds. Please update your payment method or ensure sufficient funds are available for retry."; R02/R04 (account closed/invalid) — "Your bank returned this payment because the account is no longer valid. Please update your payment method to a current account."; R07/R10 (authorization revoked) — "Your bank has indicated that payment authorization was revoked. Please contact your bank or update your payment method." Generic return messages are not permitted.

Why: Return code-specific messaging allows the consumer to take the correct corrective action immediately rather than contacting support to understand what happened.

Institution / Finance Admin

Returned Payment Fee Assessment. The institution configures a returned payment fee amount (or $0 to disable). When an ACH return is received, the platform assesses the configured fee against the student's account as a separate charge transaction.

Why: Returned payment fees are a standard institutional policy that must be enforced consistently; manual fee assessment is error-prone and creates staff workload.

Student / AP

Method Update Requirement Before Plan Continues. After an ACH return, the plan's scheduled installments are paused until the consumer updates their payment method to a valid account. The paused state is clearly indicated on the plan card and detail screen. The plan does not automatically retry against the returned account number.

Why: Retrying an ACH payment against a closed or invalid account generates additional return fees from the processor and may violate NACHA rules around re-presentment limits.

Reschedule After Recovery

Student / AP

New Date Confirmation After Method Update. When a consumer updates their payment method following a failed installment, the platform immediately sends a notification confirming: (1) the payment method has been updated, (2) the next installment will be retried on a specific date, and (3) the amount to be charged.

Why: Consumers who update their payment method need explicit confirmation that the retry is scheduled and when to expect the charge, so they can ensure funds are available.

Student / AP

Rescheduled Installment in Schedule View. After a reschedule event, the installment schedule view reflects the updated date for the affected installment. The schedule view distinguishes rescheduled installments from originally-scheduled installments with a label (e.g., "Rescheduled from [original date]").

Why: Showing both the original and rescheduled date gives the consumer (and admin) a clear picture of the plan's history and prevents confusion about why the charge date differs from the original schedule.

Plan Default & Cancellation State

Institution / Finance Admin

Default Threshold Configuration. The institution configures the number of consecutive failed installment attempts that triggers plan default. The minimum configurable value is 1 (default on first failure after retries exhausted); the maximum is 3. Upon reaching the threshold, the plan status transitions to "Defaulted" and no further installment processing occurs.

Why: Default thresholds are a risk tolerance decision that varies by institution; a configurable threshold avoids one-size-fits-all defaults that may not match the institution's student population or collection policies.

Student / AP

Defaulted Plan Card on Home Screen. A defaulted plan is displayed on the consumer's home screen with a distinct "Defaulted" status badge. The card shows the full remaining balance now due, a summary of the failure event, and a CTA to contact the bursar. The plan card is not removed from the home screen upon default.

Why: Hiding defaulted plan information leaves consumers unaware of their outstanding balance obligation; visible status with remaining balance due provides the necessary urgency to prompt resolution.

Institution / Finance Admin

ERP Cancelled Plan Status Notification. Within the institution-configured sync window after default, the ERP/SIS receives a plan cancellation event with: student ID, plan ID, cancellation reason code (system-initiated default), remaining balance at time of default, and cancellation timestamp. The ERP must re-activate the full remaining balance as a standard accounts receivable balance.

Why: When a plan defaults, the institution must restore the full balance to their AR system for standard collection follow-up; automated ERP notification prevents manual re-entry and timing gaps.

Student / AP

Consumer Default Notification. At the time the plan enters default status, the consumer receives an email and in-app notification that clearly states: the plan has been cancelled due to non-payment, the remaining balance is now the full amount due to the institution, and the consumer should contact the bursar to discuss resolution options.

Why: Consumers must be explicitly informed that the plan structure no longer applies and the full balance is due — unclear communication at default creates disputes and delays resolution.

Consumer Recovery Path

Student / AP

Bursar Contact Path from Defaulted State. The defaulted plan card and the default notification email both present a direct link or contact button for the institution's bursar office. This path is available without requiring the consumer to navigate menus.

Why: The most important recovery action after default is direct bursar contact; surfacing the contact path prominently from the default state reduces time-to-resolution.

Institution / Finance Admin

Re-Enrollment After Default Configuration. The institution configures whether a student who has defaulted on a plan is eligible to enroll in a new plan for the same or a future term, and the mandatory waiting period before re-enrollment is permitted (options: no waiting period, 30 days, 60 days, or never). This configuration is enforced at the offer display step.

Why: Institutions have divergent policies on re-enrollment after default; some use re-enrollment as a recovery tool, others restrict it to limit risk. Configurable control allows each institution to apply their own policy.

Student / AP

One-Time Payment from Defaulted State. A consumer with a defaulted plan can make a one-time payment toward their remaining balance directly from the defaulted plan card — without needing to re-enroll in a plan. The one-time payment flow collects payment method and amount, processes the payment in real time, and updates the remaining balance displayed on the card.

Why: Students who cannot or do not want to re-enroll should still be able to make partial or full payments toward their balance through the portal; removing this path forces all post-default payments through the bursar.

Features · Pay Over Time

Scheduled Payment Processing

Requirements for how the platform's installment engine runs, processes, and communicates scheduled plan payments — covering the processing schedule, advance notifications, fee handling, and receipt presentation.

Installment Engine Execution

Institution / Finance Admin

Nightly Processing Run. The installment engine runs once nightly and processes all active plan installments whose scheduled date matches the current processing date. The processing date uses the institution's configured timezone — not UTC — to determine which installments are due. Plans at institutions in different timezones are processed in the appropriate local-date context.

Why: Timezone-aware processing prevents installments from being triggered a day early or late for institutions on the east or west coast, which creates reconciliation mismatches with the institution's end-of-day accounting.

Institution / Finance Admin

Processing Window Completion Requirement. The nightly installment processing run must complete — with all transactions submitted to the payment processor and results received — before 8:00 AM institution local time. If the run has not completed by 7:30 AM, the platform generates an operational alert to NBS support. The processing SLA is tracked and reported monthly.

Why: Finance staff begin their day processing student account activity; installment results must be available before the business day starts to allow timely response to failures and student inquiries.

Institution / Finance Admin

Processing Results Available by 9 AM. A processing results report is available in the admin dashboard by 9:00 AM institution local time showing: total installments processed, total dollar amount, count and amount of successful payments, count and amount of failed payments, and list of failed plans requiring attention. The report is filterable by plan type, term, and failure reason.

Why: Finance staff need a daily operational summary to prioritize follow-up on failed payments; a report available at the start of the business day enables same-day resolution outreach.

Institution / Finance Admin

Installment Skip on Non-Business Days. When a scheduled installment date falls on a weekend or institution-configured holiday, the installment is automatically rescheduled to the next business day. The reschedule is applied during the nightly run prior to the original date and a consumer notification is sent informing them of the adjusted date. The platform uses the institution's holiday calendar for this determination.

Why: ACH transactions submitted on non-processing days are rejected or delayed by the banking network; proactive rescheduling prevents processing failures caused by calendar timing.

Advance Payment Notifications

Student / AP

Configurable Advance Notice Period. The institution configures the advance notice period for installment notifications — default is 3 business days before the scheduled installment date. The minimum configurable period is 1 business day; the maximum is 7 business days. The advance notice is sent even if the installment amount has not changed since the previous notification.

Why: Consumers need sufficient advance notice to ensure their payment method has adequate funds; the default 3-day period aligns with ACH processing timing and allows a business day to resolve issues before the charge date.

Student / AP

Advance Notification Required Fields. The advance payment notification must contain: the exact amount to be charged, the last 4 of the payment method to be charged (with card brand or bank name), the scheduled charge date, a link to update the payment method, and the plan name and term. Advance notifications are sent to all email addresses associated with the account (student + any configured APs with notification access).

Why: All five fields are necessary for the consumer to take action — without the amount, date, or method, the notification does not give them enough information to prepare or to identify which plan and method is affected.

Student / AP

Service Fee Pre-Disclosure in Advance Notice. For plans where a service fee applies to each installment (credit card plans), the advance notification separately discloses: the principal installment amount, the service fee amount, and the total to be charged including the service fee rate (e.g., "2.75% of $X = $Y service fee").

Why: Service fees that appear without advance notice are the second most common reason for installment disputes; proactive per-installment disclosure reduces disputes and establishes a clear paper trail.

Service Fee Handling on Installments

Institution / Finance Admin

Per-Installment Fee Calculation. For plans on a credit card payment method, the service fee is calculated per installment as: (installment principal amount) × (institution-configured service fee rate). The fee is recalculated for each installment — it is not fixed at enrollment. If the installment amount changes due to rounding or a prior ad-hoc payment, the fee is recalculated accordingly.

Why: Dynamic fee calculation ensures the fee is always proportional to the actual installment amount; a fixed fee based on the enrollment-time amount becomes incorrect if installment amounts change mid-plan.

Student / AP

Fee as Separate Transaction. The service fee is charged as a separate payment transaction concurrent with the principal installment — not bundled into a single inflated installment amount. The two transactions are linked by a common installment event ID in the payment audit trail.

Why: Separate transactions allow the institution to account for fee revenue separately from plan principal revenue, and give consumers transparent visibility into exactly how much they are paying in fees.

Student / AP

Fee Not Charged on Failed Installment. If the principal installment charge fails (declined or returned), the service fee transaction is not submitted. The fee is only charged when the associated principal installment is successfully processed. On a subsequent retry that succeeds, both the principal and fee are charged together at that time.

Why: Charging the fee on a failed installment — where the institution receives no payment — creates an unjustified consumer charge and complicates refund processing.

Student / AP

Fee Receipt in Same Communication History Event. After a successful installment with a service fee, the communication history shows a single combined receipt event — not two separate entries for principal and fee. The receipt event expands to show the itemized breakdown (principal amount, fee amount, total), but the top-level list shows one line per installment event.

Why: Two separate communication history entries per installment doubles the visual noise in the consumer's history view and causes confusion about whether separate charges represent separate problems.

Combined Receipt View

Student / AP

Single Receipt Event Per Installment. After each installment processes, the consumer receives one receipt notification (email + in-app communication history entry) containing: installment principal amount, service fee amount (if any), total amount charged, payment method last 4, processing date, remaining plan balance, next installment date, and projected next installment amount.

Why: A single, comprehensive receipt gives consumers all the information they need to reconcile the charge on their bank statement and understand their plan's remaining trajectory.

Student / AP

Downloadable PDF Receipt. Each installment receipt in the communication history view has a "Download PDF" option that generates a formatted receipt document. The PDF includes: institution name and logo, student name and ID, plan name, installment number (e.g., "Payment 2 of 4"), all receipt fields, and a footer with the institution's contact information.

Why: Students frequently need proof-of-payment receipts for scholarship reimbursements, employer tuition assistance programs, or personal records; on-demand PDF generation eliminates the need to contact the bursar for receipt copies.

Failed Processing & Retry Queue

Institution / Finance Admin

Retry Queue Entry on Failure. When an installment fails processing, the failed installment enters an institution-configured retry queue with the scheduled retry date calculated per the institution's retry logic. The retry queue entry records: original scheduled date, failure reason, failure code, retry count, and next scheduled retry date. The queue is visible in the admin dashboard under the plan's detail view.

Why: A visible retry queue gives Finance staff clarity on what will happen next without requiring them to manually track retry timing; it also prevents staff from manually re-triggering payments that are already in the automated retry path.

Institution / Finance Admin

Retry Attempts Logged in Audit Trail. Each retry attempt — whether successful or failed — is recorded as a distinct entry in the plan's payment audit trail with: attempt timestamp, amount attempted, payment method used, result (success/failure), and processor response code. The audit trail is immutable and accessible to Finance Admin and NBS PAS roles.

Why: A complete retry history is necessary for dispute resolution, compliance auditing, and diagnosing systemic payment failure patterns across a portfolio of plans.

Institution / Finance Admin

Manual Retry Trigger by Admin. A Finance Admin or NBS PAS agent can manually trigger a retry attempt on a failed installment from the CSR plan detail view, regardless of the scheduled automatic retry date. Manual retry requires a written reason and is logged in the change history.

Why: When a student calls the bursar to report they have updated their payment method, staff need the ability to immediately trigger a retry rather than waiting for the next scheduled automatic attempt.

Features · Pay Over Time

Plan Servicing by CSR

Requirements for how institution finance admins and NBS PAS Support Agents view and service active Pay Over Time plans on behalf of students — including cancellation, installment rescheduling, payment cancellation, and change history.

CSR Plan Detail View

Finance Admin / CSR / NBS PAS Agent

Full Plan Detail View Contents. Authorized users can access a full plan detail view from the student account screen showing: plan summary (name, term, status, enrollment date, total amount, remaining balance), complete installment schedule (all past and future installments with status), payment method last 4 and type, plan owner name and student ID, all associated APs, and enrollment date.

Why: CSR staff answering student calls need all plan information in a single view; requiring navigation across multiple screens to piece together plan status increases handle time and error risk.

Finance Admin / CSR / NBS PAS Agent

Communication History in Plan Detail. The plan detail view includes a communication history tab showing every notification sent to the consumer (advance notices, receipts, failure notifications, admin action notifications) in reverse-chronological order, with: event type, send date/time, recipient email address, delivery status (sent/bounced/opened if available), and a link to view the message content.

Why: When a student claims they never received a notification, CSR staff need to verify delivery status from the plan record without contacting the email service provider separately.

Student Services Rep

Read-Only for Student Services Rep Role. Users with the Student Services Rep role see the full plan detail view including all informational fields but have no management action buttons (cancel, reschedule, override). The read-only restriction is enforced at the API level — Student Services Rep tokens cannot submit POST/PATCH requests on plan resources.

Why: Front-line advisors need plan visibility to answer student questions but should not be able to modify plans, reducing the risk of unauthorized changes and maintaining a clear segregation of duties.

Finance Admin / NBS PAS Agent

Payment Audit Trail Access. From the plan detail view, Finance Admin and NBS PAS agents can access the full payment audit trail: every payment transaction (authorization, capture, failure, retry, refund) with processor transaction IDs, timestamps, amounts, payment method last 4, response codes, and the installment event each transaction belongs to. The audit trail is exportable to CSV.

Why: Payment disputes and chargeback responses require access to the complete transaction-level record; without this in the plan view, staff must query the payment processor directly, which is slower and less auditable.

Cancel Plan (Admin-Initiated)

Finance Admin / NBS PAS Agent

Cancellation Requires Written Reason. When a Finance Admin or NBS PAS agent initiates a plan cancellation, they must select a cancellation reason from a configured list (e.g., Student request, Student withdrew, Billing adjustment, Error correction) and optionally enter a free-text note. Cancellation cannot be submitted without a reason selection. The reason and note are stored in the change history.

Why: Cancellation reason data is required for reporting on plan attrition drivers and for audit purposes; mandatory capture prevents the change history from having unexplained administrative actions.

Student / AP

Consumer Cancellation Notification. Within 30 minutes of admin-initiated plan cancellation, the consumer receives an email notification stating: the plan has been cancelled, the remaining balance is now the full amount due to the institution, and the consumer should contact the bursar for questions.

Why: Consumers must be promptly notified of admin-initiated cancellations so they can plan for the restored balance obligation and take timely action.

Finance Admin / NBS PAS Agent

Cancellation Logged in Change History. The admin cancellation action creates an immutable change history entry recording: action type (Plan Cancelled), authorizing user ID and display name, role, timestamp, reason code, free-text note, and the plan's remaining balance at the time of cancellation.

Why: A tamper-evident record of who cancelled a plan and why is required for internal governance, audit, and for resolving consumer disputes about unauthorized cancellations.

Reschedule Installment

Finance Admin / NBS PAS Agent

Single Future Installment Reschedule. An authorized CSR can change the scheduled date of a single future installment (one that has not yet been submitted for processing). The rescheduled date must fall within the same calendar month as the original scheduled date unless the institution configures a broader window. A reschedule requires a mandatory reason selection and is logged in the change history with the original and new dates.

Why: Single-installment reschedule covers the primary use case (student requests a specific month's payment be moved to align with a paycheck) without creating the complexity and audit risk of bulk schedule modifications.

Student / AP

Consumer Notified of Reschedule. Within 30 minutes of a CSR reschedule action, the consumer receives a notification stating: the original date, the new date, the amount to be charged, and which plan and installment number was affected.

Why: Consumers must know about any changes to their expected charge dates so they can ensure funds are available; undisclosed date changes are a source of NSF fees and consumer complaints.

Cancel Individual Payment

Finance Admin / NBS PAS Agent

Cancel Future Installment Without Cancelling Plan. An authorized CSR can cancel a specific future installment that has not yet been processed without cancelling the entire plan. The cancelled installment's amount must be redistributed per the institution's configured redistribution rule: (a) spread proportionally across remaining installments, (b) added to the final installment, or (c) removed from the plan balance entirely (requires Finance Admin role).

Why: Individual installment cancellation is needed when a student receives a financial aid disbursement that partially offsets their balance; cancelling the full plan is not appropriate when only one payment needs to be eliminated.

Student / AP

Consumer Notified of Cancelled Payment. Within 30 minutes of a CSR cancelling an individual installment, the consumer receives a notification stating: which installment was cancelled, the original amount, the redistribution method applied, and the updated amounts for affected future installments. A revised schedule summary is included in the notification.

Why: Changes to the installment schedule — even favorable ones like a cancelled payment — must be communicated to the consumer so they have accurate expectations about future charges.

Change History View

Finance Admin / NBS PAS Agent

Tamper-Evident Change History. Every administrative action on a plan — CSR cancel, installment reschedule, individual installment cancellation, payment method override, allocation rule change, status override — is recorded as an immutable entry in the change history. Entries cannot be deleted or modified by any user or role. The change history is stored with cryptographic integrity protection.

Why: Tamper-evidence is required for regulatory compliance and legal defensibility; a change history that can be altered after the fact does not satisfy audit requirements.

Finance Admin / NBS PAS Agent

Change History Entry Required Fields. Each entry must contain: action type (from a controlled vocabulary), authorizing user display name and user ID, role at the time of the action, timestamp (UTC and institution local time), stated reason (reason code + optional free-text note), and before/after values for all fields affected by the action.

Why: Before/after values are critical for reconstructing the state of a plan at any point in its history; without them, the change history only confirms that an action occurred, not what specifically changed.

Finance Admin / NBS PAS Agent

System-Generated Events in Change History. In addition to admin-initiated actions, the change history includes system-generated events: plan creation (enrollment), each installment processed, each retry attempt, each status transition (Active → Defaulted, Paused → Active), and each ERP sync event. System events are labeled with a "System" actor identifier and are visually distinguished from admin-initiated entries.

Why: A complete change history — not just human-initiated actions — provides a full audit trail of the plan's lifecycle, enabling root cause analysis and complete reconstruction of the plan's history from a single view.

Finance Admin / NBS PAS Agent

Change History Export. The complete change history for a plan can be exported to PDF or CSV from the plan detail view. The export is watermarked with the exporting user's name, role, and export timestamp to support chain-of-custody for compliance submissions.

Why: Institutions responding to external audits or regulatory inquiries need to produce the change history as a document; an in-platform export eliminates the need to request data extracts from NBS support.

Institution Configuration

Institution Configuration Options

Scope of this section

All scenarios represent students authenticating via SAML SSO directly from their university's portal, with full ERP integration — charges, financial aid, and enrollment data synced automatically. Authorized payers are managed within Nelnet's system; the student controls who has access and at what level.

This section documents every institution-level setting that changes what a student or authorized party sees and can do inside the Horizon experience. Settings are configured per institution at the time of implementation. Where the current prototype uses a specific value, that value is marked Prototype default.

💳
Payment Methods
ACH / Bank Account
Allow students and authorized payers to pay via direct bank transfer (ACH). No service fee applies to ACH payments.
Options Enabled Prototype default Disabled
Consumer impact: If disabled, bank account will not appear as a payment option. Students will only see card-based methods — meaning the 2.75% service fee will always apply.
Credit Card
Allow payments via credit card. A service fee applies; the percentage is institution-configured (see below).
Options Enabled Prototype default Disabled
Consumer impact: If disabled, credit card will not appear as a payment option. The service fee disclosure note is also suppressed when all card types are disabled.
Debit Card
Allow payments via debit card. Treated the same as credit card for fee and routing purposes unless the institution explicitly separates them.
Options Enabled Prototype default Disabled
Consumer impact: Same as credit card. If both credit and debit are disabled but ACH is on, students pay via bank account only with no service fee.
Card Service Fee Percentage
The percentage added to any card-based payment (credit or debit). Disclosed to the student before they select a payment method, and reflected in the payment confirmation total.
Options Institution-configured % 2.75% in prototype
Consumer impact: The fee notice reads "Card payments include a [X]% service fee" — the percentage is dynamic. A student paying $1,000 by card at 2.75% sees their total displayed as $1,027.50 before confirming. ACH always shows no fee.
School Enrollment Fee
A one-time, non-refundable fee charged by the institution at the time the student confirms their payment setup. Appears as a separate line item in the balance breakdown.
Options $0 (waived) or institution-set amount $25 in prototype
Consumer impact: When set to $0 the enrollment fee line is hidden entirely. When set to a positive amount it appears in the balance summary and is included in the total the student pays at confirmation. It does not roll into POT installments.
📆
Pay Over Time
Pay Over Time — Feature Toggle
Master on/off for payment plan offerings. When disabled, students only see the Pay in Full path during onboarding.
Options Enabled Prototype default Disabled
Consumer impact: If disabled, the "How to Pay" step shows only Pay in Full. The POT plan setup screens, plan confirmation, and the "Set Up Payment Plan" quick action on the home screen are all suppressed.
Number of Plans Offered
How many distinct Pay Over Time plans the institution makes available to students. Each plan can have different down payment requirements, installment counts, dates, and fees.
Options 1 plan Prototype default 2 plans 3+ plans
Consumer impact: When exactly 1 plan is configured, the student skips the plan-selection screen and goes directly to down payment selection for that plan. When 2 or more plans exist, the student sees a plan picker first and chooses between the available options.
Down Payment Configuration (per plan)
Defines how the required down payment is determined for each plan. Can be a fixed percentage of the net balance, a tiered range the student selects within, or a flat minimum amount.
Options Fixed % of balance Prototype default Student-selected % within a min–max range Flat minimum dollar amount
Consumer impact: A fixed percentage requires no input from the student — the down payment is shown and confirmed. A range lets the student choose how much to put down (within bounds), showing how their selection changes the installment amount in real time. This is one of the highest-impact configuration decisions for perceived flexibility.
Number of Installments (per plan)
How many equal installment payments the remaining balance is divided into after the down payment. Drives the per-installment amount displayed during plan confirmation.
Options Institution-configured count per plan 4 in prototype
Consumer impact: Directly determines the installment amount shown in the natural-language plan summary: "you'll be charged [frequency] — [N] payments of [$X] each." Smaller installment counts mean larger per-payment amounts.
Payment Frequency (per plan)
How often installment payments are charged — monthly is the most common, but institutions may offer bi-weekly or term-specific schedules.
Options Monthly Prototype default Bi-weekly Custom schedule
Consumer impact: The payment frequency label appears in the plan summary ("charged monthly") and determines the spacing between dates in the installment schedule. It also affects the Upcoming Payments module — a monthly plan will show at most one upcoming installment at a time.
Plan Start Date & End Date (per plan)
The date range during which the plan is active. The first installment date is derived from the plan start date; the final installment aligns with the plan end date.
Options Institution-configured per plan and term End date: Dec 15, 2026 in prototype
Consumer impact: Both dates appear in the plan confirmation summary. If today's date is after the plan start, the first installment due date is adjusted to the next valid payment date in the schedule.
Plan Enrollment Fee (per plan)
An optional fee charged to the student when they enroll in a specific Pay Over Time plan. Distinct from the school enrollment fee — this is plan-specific and may differ across plans at the same institution.
Options $0 (no fee) Institution-set flat amount
Consumer impact: When a plan enrollment fee exists, it is shown as a separate line in the plan confirmation screen and added to the amount due today alongside the down payment. It is not rolled into future installments.
🛡️
Tuition Insurance (GradGuard)
GradGuard — Feature Toggle
Master on/off for the tuition insurance offering. When enabled, students are presented an insurance offer during onboarding with their calculated premium.
Options Enabled Prototype default Disabled
Consumer impact: If disabled, the insurance step is skipped entirely — no mention of GradGuard anywhere in the experience. The "Add Tuition Insurance" and "Tuition Insurance" quick actions are also suppressed. The insurance card on the home screen never appears.
GradGuard Plan / Premium Calculation
The specific GradGuard plan the institution has contracted, which determines the premium percentage applied to the student's total enrollment charges to produce their individual premium quote.
Options Institution-specific plan rate (applied to total charges)
Consumer impact: The dollar amount of the premium shown to the student is entirely determined by this rate × their total charges. Two students at the same institution with different enrollment amounts will see different premium quotes for the same plan.
Insurance Offer Re-presentation
Whether the insurance offer is re-surfaced to a returning student in a new term if they previously declined (or if it's a new term's policy year).
Options Re-present each term Never re-present after decline
Consumer impact: A student who declined insurance last term will either see the offer again at the start of this term (re-present) or proceed past the step automatically (never re-present). This setting is most relevant for Scenario 2 (Returning Student) and will be documented further there.
👥
Authorized Parties
Authorized Party Feature — Toggle
Master on/off for the ability to invite and manage authorized parties. When disabled, the AP invite step is removed from onboarding and the AP management section is hidden from Account Settings.
Options Enabled Prototype default Disabled
Consumer impact: If disabled, students cannot add payers or viewers. The "Add Authorized Party" quick action is suppressed. APs cannot receive invite links or log in.
Maximum Authorized Parties per Student
The maximum number of authorized parties a student may add to their account simultaneously. Once the limit is reached, the "Add Authorized Party" option is replaced with a message indicating the limit.
Options Unlimited Prototype default Institution-set limit (e.g. 2, 5)
Consumer impact: Students at institutions with a limit see the AP invite step disabled once they reach it. The "Add Authorized Party" quick action is hidden at that point even if other AP conditions would normally show it.
Available AP Permission Levels
Which levels of access a student can grant to an authorized party. Institutions may restrict the available options to control the maximum access an AP can receive.
Options View only Can make payments Prototype default Can manage payment methods Full account access
Consumer impact: The permission level picker shown to the student during AP setup only shows options the institution has enabled. A student at an institution that only allows "View only" and "Can make payments" will never see the "Full access" option, regardless of what they might want to grant.
Guest Payment Links
Allow students to generate a one-time payment link for a third party who should be able to make a single payment with no ongoing account access. Distinct from an authorized party — the recipient cannot log in and the link expires after one use.
Options Enabled Prototype default Disabled
Consumer impact: When enabled, students see a "Send guest payment link" option when managing their AP settings. When disabled, this option is hidden and the student's only option for involving a third party is to add a full authorized party.
🤝
School Agreements
School Agreements — Feature Toggle
Master on/off for requiring students to formally sign school agreements within Horizon during onboarding. When enabled, a dedicated agreements sign-off step is included in the onboarding flow before final confirmation. When disabled, the school handles agreement collection outside of Nelnet — through their own processes and timing — and the step is skipped entirely inside Horizon.
Options Enabled — agreements collected in Horizon Disabled — school handles outside Nelnet
Consumer impact: If disabled, students never see an agreement step — their school's agreements process happens through a separate institutional channel. If enabled, students must formally accept one or more agreements (with e-signature where required) before completing onboarding.
Agreement Types Configured
The specific agreements a school has set up within Horizon. Each agreement is a distinct document the student must acknowledge. Common types include: enrollment agreements, payment terms, refund policies, and financial responsibility statements. The number and content of agreements varies by institution and may differ by term.
Options 1–N agreements configured by institution
Consumer impact: Each configured agreement adds a sign-off step the student must complete. The onboarding progress indicator updates to reflect how many agreements are required. Students cannot proceed past this step until all agreements are accepted.
GradGuard Refund Policy — Required Agreement
If the institution has GradGuard tuition insurance enabled, they must also have a refund policy configured as a school agreement. The refund policy is a GradGuard prerequisite — it defines how the institution handles withdrawals and governs what the insurance covers. Schools with GradGuard who do not have a refund policy agreement set up in Horizon cannot complete the tuition insurance integration correctly.
Dependency GradGuard enabled → Refund Policy agreement required GradGuard disabled → no requirement
Consumer impact: Students at GradGuard schools will encounter the refund policy agreement as part of the agreements step. The policy must be reviewed and accepted before they can proceed. This is not optional — it is a GradGuard contractual requirement that the student acknowledge the school's refund terms before purchasing insurance.
Agreement Signing Format
Whether agreements require a typed e-signature or acknowledgment-only (checkbox). E-signature is recommended for agreements with legal or financial weight (e.g., enrollment agreements, financial responsibility statements). Acknowledgment-only may be appropriate for informational agreements.
Options E-signature required (typed full name + confirmation) Acknowledgment only (checkbox)
Consumer impact: E-signature agreements require the student to type their legal name and check a confirmation box. The submit button stays disabled until both conditions are met, preventing accidental acceptance. Acknowledgment-only agreements activate immediately when the checkbox is checked.
Best Practice Recommendation
Collecting school agreements within Horizon (rather than externally) is the recommended approach. In-system collection ensures there is a single audit trail, agreements are time-stamped and linked to the student's account, and re-signing is automatically triggered if agreement content changes. Schools that manage agreements outside Nelnet introduce timing gaps and risk agreements not being completed before a student's first payment.
Recommendation In-system (Horizon) — best practice
Operational impact: Schools using external agreement collection must ensure their process completes before students access the payment portal. Any gap between account access and agreement completion creates a compliance risk for the institution.
📄
Disclosures
Number of Disclosure Sections
How many sequential disclosure accordion sections the student must open and acknowledge before they can e-sign. Each section is a distinct policy or agreement — e.g., payment terms, refund policy, enrollment agreement, Nelnet terms.
Options Institution-configured (1–N) 4 sections in prototype
Consumer impact: More sections = more steps before the e-sign field activates. The progress indicator updates accordingly. Each section requires an explicit acknowledgment tap before the next opens. The total count is shown so students know what to expect upfront.
Disclosure Content & Templates
The actual text of each disclosure section. Institutions provide their own policy text. Nelnet may include a universal section in addition to institution-specific sections. Content is managed outside this prototype.
Options Institution-provided text per section Nelnet universal section (appended)
Consumer impact: Students see exactly the disclosure text their institution has configured. The PDF download for each section produces a document matching that institution's content — not a generic template. Changes to disclosure content require an institution to update their configured templates.
E-Signature Requirement
Whether a typed full-name signature and confirmation checkbox are required to complete the disclosures step. In practice this should always be required, but is documented here as a configuration point.
Options Required Prototype default Waived (acknowledgment only)
Consumer impact: When required, the student must type their name (min 3 characters) and check a confirmation box before submitting. The submit button remains disabled until both conditions are met. When waived, acknowledgment of each section alone is sufficient to proceed.
📬
Communications
Available Notification Channels
Which notification channels are offered to students during the Communications setup step. Email is always required. SMS is optional — institutions may enable or disable text messaging entirely.
Options Email (always on) SMS / Text Prototype default: enabled SMS disabled
Consumer impact: If SMS is disabled by the institution, the phone number field and all SMS preference toggles are hidden. The Communications step becomes email-only. Students are not asked for a phone number if SMS is not offered.
Informational SMS Default State
The default opt-in state for informational text messages (billing updates, payment confirmations, plan changes). Students can always change this, but the starting position is institution-configured.
Options Default ON Prototype default Default OFF
Consumer impact: Default ON means students are opted into informational texts unless they explicitly turn them off. Default OFF means students receive no texts unless they opt in. This is a meaningful business rule — institutions in regulated environments may require explicit opt-in.
Marketing SMS — Visibility
Whether the marketing text messages toggle is shown to students at all. Some institutions may not have a marketing SMS program and should not surface an irrelevant preference toggle.
Options Shown (default OFF) Prototype default Hidden
Consumer impact: When hidden, the Communications step is simpler — students see only the informational SMS toggle without a separate marketing row. When shown, the toggle defaults to OFF and students can choose to opt in.
University Disclosure Count in Context Block
The number shown in the "institution settings" chip on the index page and referenced in onboarding — specifically the count of university-specific disclosures a student will see.
Options Institution-configured count 3 university disclosures in prototype
Consumer impact: This count is surfaced in the onboarding progress indicator so students know upfront how many institution-specific disclosures they will encounter versus Nelnet's universal terms.
Pay Over Time

Guarantee Plans

Why This Exists — Regulatory Background

In the states of Virginia, Florida, Georgia, and Alabama, state or system-wide regulations require that all tuition must be collected for students enrolled as of a state-defined Census Date in order for state-funded institutions to qualify for state funding in the following year.

A standard payment plan does not satisfy this requirement — it allows students to pay over time with no guarantee that the full amount will be collected by the Census Date. The Guarantee Program was developed to allow institutions to offer a payment plan while ensuring NBS remits the full contracted amount for every enrolled student by the deadline. NBS incurs financial risk by guaranteeing this amount, which is why enrollment fees are higher and down payments are larger the closer a student enrolls to the Guarantee Date.

How it fits into the product: Guarantee plans share the same consumer-facing sign-up flow as standard Pay Over Time plans — students select a plan option and proceed through the same payment, disclosure, and confirmation steps. The differences are in eligibility rules, fee structures, date-driven validations, SSN collection, and post-enrollment behavior. All requirements below define where the guarantee flow diverges from or extends the standard plan flow.
Key Terminology
Census Date
The date established by the state to report enrollment numbers of students that impact state funding to those institutions. This is the last date of drop/add classes at the institution. All other Guarantee dates are calculated from this date.
Guarantee Date
The date NBS determines which agreements qualify for guarantee payment to the school. Calculated as 2 business days before the Census Date — giving the school a chance to drop students before the Census Date. The Guarantee Date cannot fall on a payment day, the day prior to a payment, or within 2 days after a payment.
Last Day for Increases
The last date that a school can increase the balance of an agreement prior to the Guarantee Date. Same as the last date to enroll. Once an agreement has been guaranteed, NBS will not allow increases to the amount.
1st Remittance Date
NBS remits all tuition payments collected (less any outstanding NBS fees) for agreements that were not guaranteed. May also include tuition collected for agreements that were guaranteed if the institution is configured for this. Typically about 10 business days from the Guarantee Date.
2nd Remittance Date
All guaranteed funds less decreases are remitted. Typically 30–60 days from the Guarantee Date. Calculated based on the number of days configured per the institution's contract (PSA).
Maximum Amount
The maximum amount NBS will guarantee for a single student's tuition payment plan. Any agreement amount above this threshold must be handled through one of three configured enforcement rules.
Default (Guarantee context)
An agreement that was guaranteed but still has a remaining balance as of a specific pre-determined Default Date. The Default Date is 5 business days from the last scheduled payment date of the term.
Configuration Requirements

Guarantee plan option available alongside regular plans at the term level. Institutions in qualifying states must be able to offer guarantee plans for tuition accounts and regular payment plans for non-tuition accounts (e.g., housing) within the same term simultaneously.

Why: Only tuition is subject to the guarantee requirement. Students may owe tuition (requiring a guarantee plan) and housing (which can use a standard plan) in the same term. The system must support both plan types co-existing for a single student in the same term — this removes a current constraint in Enterprise where only one agreement per term is supported when RTAA and balance compare are active.

Sophie review needed The current system does not support a student having more than one agreement in the same term when RTAA and balance compare are used. Confirm whether lifting this constraint is in scope for Horizon, or whether this requires a separate term structure (e.g., "Guarantee Term — Fall 2026" and "Housing Term — Fall 2026"). This is a core architectural decision.

Configure Guarantee stage dates from a single Census Date input. The NBS Administrator enters the Census Date; the system automatically calculates all dependent dates — Guarantee Date, Last Date to Enroll, Last Date for Increases, 1st Remittance Date, Default Date. Calculated dates are suggestions that can be edited by the NBS Administrator.

Why: All guarantee milestones are mathematically derived from the Census Date. Calculating them automatically eliminates manual entry errors and ensures the date relationships are always consistent with program rules.

  • Census Date: Entered by NBS Admin — drives all other dates
  • Guarantee Date: 2 business days before Census Date (cannot be on or within 2 days after a payment date)
  • Last Date to Enroll / Last Date for Increases: 5 business days before Guarantee Date
  • 1st Remittance Date: 10 business days after Guarantee Date (with option to include guaranteed payments)
  • 2nd Remittance Date: Configurable number of days after Census Date — set per institution PSA
  • Default Date: 5 business days from the last scheduled payment date of the term
Sophie review needed Confirm which of these calculated dates can be edited after agreements are already on the term, and which are locked once students have enrolled. Define the warning/impact when an admin edits a date that has active agreements.

Guarantee Custodial Account. A dedicated NBS-owned custodial account must be configured for each Guarantee institution. All student tuition payments are deposited to this account prior to remittance to the institution. Institution remittances are transferred automatically from this account on the configured Remittance Dates.

Why: Commingling guarantee funds with standard operating funds creates accounting, compliance, and reconciliation risk. A dedicated custodial account ensures that guaranteed amounts are ringfenced and available for remittance on schedule — independent of other NBS cash flows.

Maximum Guarantee Amount. The NBS Administrator configures the maximum dollar amount NBS will guarantee per student. This maximum is enforced at enrollment, during balance increases (manual, real-time, and batch), and in balance compare processes. Three enforcement modes must be configurable:

  • Deny eligibility: Student cannot enroll if the agreement amount exceeds the maximum
  • Collect overage immediately: Student pays the overage above the maximum as an additional immediate down payment at enrollment, in addition to the standard required down payment
  • Set up for maximum, resolve overage with school: Agreement is set up for the maximum amount; the remaining overage is handled directly between the student and institution

Why: NBS's financial exposure in guaranteeing agreements is capped per contract. Enforcing the maximum at every touch point — enrollment, balance adjustments, batch processes — prevents NBS from inadvertently guaranteeing more than the contracted limit.

Sophie review needed The third enforcement mode (set up for max, resolve overage with school) introduces the concept of editable RTAA amounts and has not been fully scoped. Confirm whether this mode is in scope for Horizon and what the institutional data flow looks like when the student's agreement balance differs from their RTAA balance.

Payment options validated against required percentage by Guarantee Date. When calculating installment options for a guarantee plan, the system must only present options where the cumulative payments scheduled before the Guarantee Date meet or exceed the institution-configured required percentage of the total agreement. The NBS Administrator configures the required collected percentage (e.g., 50%, 60%).

Why: NBS guarantees the full agreement amount on the Guarantee Date, but only if the student has met their payment commitment. Preventing the system from offering installment schedules that wouldn't hit the required percentage by Guarantee Date removes a core risk vector — students signing up for plans that NBS would have to guarantee without sufficient collection.

Differentiated enrollment fees by payment option and by state system. Each payment option (based on number of installments scheduled before the Guarantee Date) has a different enrollment fee. Fee schedules vary by state and institution system. The NBS Administrator configures enrollment fees per payment option count. Current fee schedules:

  • Virginia: 1–2 payments → $45 · 3 payments → $40 · 4–6 payments → $35
  • Florida & Georgia Technical Schools: 1–2 payments → $40 · 3 payments → $35 · 4–6 payments → $30
  • Georgia University System (Modified Guarantee): 1–2 payments → $70 · 3 payments → $60 · 4–6 payments → $50

Why: When a student enrolls later (fewer payments before the Guarantee Date), NBS collects less before the guarantee obligation triggers — increasing NBS's financial exposure. Higher enrollment fees for fewer pre-guarantee payments compensate for this increased risk. The fee structure must be dynamically applied based on the payment option the student selects, not as a flat fee.

Enrollment Requirements

Collect SSN for Plan Owner when the system detects the agreement is a guarantee plan. During enrollment for a guarantee payment plan, the system must collect and store the Social Security Number of the plan owner (student or authorized payer). SSN is used to facilitate collections in the event of a default.

Why: NBS guarantees the institution's full tuition amount. If a student defaults, NBS must pursue collection of the outstanding balance from the plan owner. Having the SSN on file significantly improves the likelihood of successful collection and is standard practice in financial guarantee programs.

Sophie review needed Compliance/audit requirements for SSN storage must be confirmed (encryption at rest, access controls, purge schedule, display masking, when it's included in reports or collection files). Input from Legal/Compliance required before this requirement is finalized. Also confirm whether SSN validation logic (Luhn-style check) is needed, and how to handle refusals.

Do not allow enrollment if the student has a past-due balance from a prior term. If the student (or any of their Authorized Parties) has an unpaid defaulted amount from a previous term, enrollment in a new guarantee agreement must be blocked until the prior balance is paid in full. This rule applies regardless of who owns the existing defaulted agreement.

Why: Allowing a student with an existing default to enroll in a new guarantee plan would expose NBS to double guarantee risk — guaranteeing a new term while a prior term balance is still outstanding. The prior default is evidence of a collection risk that must be resolved before NBS accepts new exposure.

Disclose fees and program parameters during enrollment. A disclosure must notify the plan owner that: (1) the agreement may be terminated if it becomes delinquent, and (2) NBS fees may be deducted from any amount collected. This disclosure is required before the plan owner finalizes enrollment.

Why: The guarantee program has unique fee-withholding rules (outstanding NBS fees are deducted from remittance on non-guaranteed agreements) and a plan termination risk that does not exist in standard plans. Consumers must understand these conditions before committing.

Terminate the current agreement if a new default is detected for the student. If a new agreement is finalized before a prior-term agreement has defaulted, and the prior agreement subsequently goes into default before the new agreement is guaranteed, the new agreement must be automatically terminated or placed on hold until the prior balance is resolved.

Why: There is a timing gap where a student can slip into default on an old term while a new term's plan is already active. Without this safeguard, NBS would be obligated to guarantee the new plan while simultaneously absorbing a prior-term default — compounding exposure.

Agreement Maintenance

Early warning for agreements at risk of not being guaranteed. For agreements that are past due prior to the Guarantee Date with no reattempts scheduled, a warning notification must be automatically sent to the student and plan owner when the system detects a returned payment that will not automatically reattempt before the Guarantee Date. The warning alerts them that the agreement is scheduled for termination on the Guarantee Date if not resolved.

Why: Students with a returned payment close to the Guarantee Date have a brief window to act. Without proactive notification, they may be unaware their plan is about to terminate — resulting in a surprise loss of guarantee status, institutional disruption, and student confusion at a critical time.

Highlight Early Warning agreements prominently on the consumer profile page. Any agreement scheduled for termination (due to a pending guarantee risk) must display a clearly visible warning indicator on the student/AP profile — visible to all user types (NBS, institution, consumer). This ensures that service staff give accurate information when a student calls with questions.

Why: If a service representative is unaware that an agreement is scheduled to terminate and tells the student otherwise, NBS may be pressured to guarantee an ineligible agreement — or the student may delay action based on incorrect information received from staff. The profile warning prevents this misinformation risk.

Enforce Maximum Amount during all balance increase processes. The maximum guarantee amount limit must be enforced at every point where a balance increase can occur: manual adjustments (consumer, NBS, institution), real-time balance compare, and batch balance compare. If an increase would cause the total guarantee-eligible amount to exceed the maximum, the increase must be blocked, with a clear message explaining the reason and the limit.

Why: Balance increases can occur through multiple pathways after initial enrollment (manual adjustments, RTAA updates, batch processes). If any one of these bypasses the maximum enforcement, NBS can inadvertently take on guarantee exposure beyond its contracted limit — a direct financial risk.

Restrict institution user actions on guarantee agreements. Institution users must not be able to: modify the payment schedule, place the agreement on hold, or activate the agreement. NBS users retain full servicing capability. Key guarantee dates (Census Date, Guarantee Date, Remittance Dates) should be visible to NBS users on the servicing screen for reference when handling schedule modification requests.

Why: Guarantee agreements have a fixed structure that is tied to regulatory dates and NBS's financial commitments. If an institution user modifies the payment schedule, it can invalidate the guarantee eligibility calculation — creating liability for NBS. Restricting institution users from these actions protects the integrity of the guarantee program.

Upload of changes must account for NBS-processed but unposted payments. The batch upload-of-changes process must calculate the comparison balance as: agreement balance minus the amount of payments processed by NBS but not yet posted to the student's account in the SIS. This prevents balance compare from treating NBS-processed payments as an outstanding balance.

Why: For guarantee institutions, there is a timing gap between when NBS processes a payment and when it is posted to the student's SIS account. Without this adjustment, the batch process would see an apparent balance discrepancy and incorrectly attempt to increase or adjust the agreement — creating reconciliation problems and double-counting risk.

The Guarantee Process

On the Guarantee Date, the system runs an automatic job that evaluates every active agreement for the term. Agreements are classified as either guaranteed or terminated based on whether the student is current on all payments.

Guarantee Day — automatic job. The system must automatically run a process on the Guarantee Date that: (1) identifies all agreements scheduled to be guaranteed, (2) identifies all agreements scheduled to terminate, and (3) updates agreement status accordingly. The process must run after all returns for that day have posted.

Why: The Guarantee Date evaluation must be comprehensive and accurate — missing an agreement or misclassifying one creates either a financial loss for NBS (guaranteeing an ineligible agreement) or an institutional/student service problem (terminating an eligible one). The timing dependency on returns posting means the job must have a controlled execution window.

Guaranteed agreements. Agreements current on all tuition and NBS fees on the Guarantee Date are automatically guaranteed. The agreement status updates clearly to indicate guaranteed status on the student profile. The guarantee amount (estimated as payments processed + remaining scheduled payments) and, where applicable, the 1st and 2nd remittance amounts are displayed on the agreement screen for NBS and institution users.

Why: Institution staff and NBS service teams need to see the expected remittance amounts per agreement to answer institutional and student inquiries accurately. Displaying this on the agreement eliminates the need to run a report for individual lookups.

Non-guaranteed agreements. Agreements past due on tuition and/or NBS fees on the Guarantee Date are terminated and their balance cleared. The agreement record must include the termination reason ("Agreement not guaranteed"). The remittance amount and fee accounting must also be displayed. Automatic notifications must be sent to the student and plan owner explaining that tuition collected (less outstanding NBS fees) will be remitted to the institution, and any refund will follow the institution's refund policy.

Why: Non-guaranteed students and their payers will call the institution asking why their plan was terminated. The notification and agreement-level accounting prevent misinformation and give the institution the data needed to answer questions — and to process any applicable refund.

Remittance — automatic deposits on configured dates. All remittances to the institution must be automatically processed from the NBS Guarantee Custodial Account to the institution's configured bank account on the 1st and 2nd Remittance Dates. No manual trigger required.

Why: Institutions rely on the guarantee remittance for their own funding cycle (state reimbursement depends on receipt by the Census Date). Manual remittance processes introduce risk of delay, error, or missed deposit — which has regulatory and institutional financial consequences.

Default notices — automatic, with escalating intervals. On the Default Date, the system automatically generates a notification to the plan owner and student that the agreement has defaulted. Reminder notices are generated at 30-day intervals thereafter. At 90 days, a paper notice is generated and mailed to the address on file. Notices continue until the balance is resolved or the agreement is sent to collections.

Why: Defaulted guarantee agreements represent a direct financial loss to NBS (NBS has already remitted the guaranteed amount to the institution). Proactive, escalating outreach maximizes the probability of recovery and creates a documented communication record for any subsequent collections or legal action.

Default management process. Default management for guarantee agreements follows the same structure as the Delinquency Management process in Enterprise. NBS generates an auto-dial file after 30 days of default. The agreement appears on the default report at 30-day intervals until resolved or purged for collections.

Why: Systematic, automated default follow-up at defined intervals ensures NBS recovers as much of its guaranteed exposure as possible and maintains a consistent process that satisfies any regulatory or contractual requirements for collections outreach.

Reports

Guarantee reports are split into two audiences: institution reports (available to institution users and NBS users) and finance reports (available to NBS Finance only). A dedicated Guarantee Reports section is added to both the institution and NBS report menus.

Institution Reports
Available to Institution & NBS Users

Guarantee Report (by term). Available once the Guarantee has been finalized. Shows all guaranteed agreements: plan owner name, student name, student ID, original contract amount, current remaining balance, and guaranteed amount.

Why: Institutions need to verify which students were guaranteed so they can reconcile expected remittances, confirm enrollment counts for state funding, and respond to student inquiries about plan status.

Non-Guaranteed Report (by term). Available once the Guarantee has been finalized. Shows all agreements not guaranteed: plan owner name, student name, student ID, original contract amount, amount of payments processed, and reason not guaranteed.

Why: Institutions need to identify students who did not meet the guarantee threshold so they can take appropriate action (direct billing, holds, or refund processing) and understand the reason for non-guarantee at the individual student level.

Guarantee Adjustment Report (by term). On-demand report of any guaranteed agreements that have been terminated or decreased since the Guarantee Date. Includes: agreement number, plan owner, student ID, student name, agreement status, original guarantee amount, adjusted guarantee amount, current estimated remittance amount.

Why: Post-guarantee adjustments (e.g., a student withdraws, reducing the guarantee amount) affect the institution's expected 2nd remittance. This report gives institutions real-time visibility into any changes after the guarantee snapshot — preventing surprises at remittance time.

2nd Remittance Cash Flow Report (by term). On-demand report of the estimated 2nd remittance amount for all guaranteed agreements for the term. Allows the institution to estimate their cash flow for the 2nd remittance date.

Why: Institutions need to plan their cash flow around the 2nd remittance. Given that the 2nd remittance date is 30–60 days from the Guarantee Date, institutions use this report for treasury planning and to verify that the expected deposit matches their internal projections.

Remittance Reports. Shows total amount remitted for each guarantee deposit in the term. Similar structure to the existing Enterprise remittance report. Each report includes: deposit date, accounting of all payments remitted, accounting of all fees assessed (NBS fees, credit card fees). Each line item includes the reason for deposit (refund for non-guaranteed agreement, guarantee deposit 1, guarantee deposit 2).

Why: Institutions reconcile NBS remittances against their own financial records. A detailed per-deposit report with fee accounting allows institutions to match NBS deposits to student accounts and confirm that all guarantee and non-guarantee amounts were remitted correctly.

Default Report. Cumulative list of students who have defaulted with NBS. Includes: student name, student ID, term of default, outstanding amount owed, length of time in default.

Why: Institutions need visibility into which students are in default so they can apply holds, notify the student independently, or refer the account to their own collections process in parallel with NBS's efforts.

Finance Reports
NBS Finance Only

Deposits Report. Shows all deposits and debits to the Guarantee Custodial Account by date, amount, and type (ACH/CC). Available as summary or detail. Detail view includes: institution, term, credit card amount (with CC type drill-down), ACH amount.

Why: NBS Finance must track the custodial account independently from operating accounts to ensure funds are properly segregated, available for remittance, and reconcile against bank statements. This report provides the daily custodial account activity needed for that reconciliation.

Estimated Remittance Report. Projects the amount of funds needed for guarantee remittances to institutions across the next 30, 60, and 90 days. Date-driven (not term-based), based on configured remittance dates across all active guarantee institutions.

Why: NBS Finance must ensure sufficient funds are available in the custodial account before remittance dates arrive. This forward-looking report enables treasury planning and prevents situations where the custodial account has insufficient funds to fulfill a remittance obligation.

Remittance Report (Finance). Shows actual remittances to each institution: date, institution, total remitted. Available as summary or detail. Detail view includes: institution, term, credit card amount, ACH amount, fees deducted. Line items link to further detail including credit card type and amounts.

Why: NBS Finance needs to verify that every scheduled remittance was processed correctly and to audit fee deductions. This report is the internal control document for the remittance process.

Default Report (Finance). Cumulative report of all accounts in default at NBS across all institutions. Includes: institution, term, plan owner, student name, student ID, amount of default, time in default.

Why: NBS Finance tracks the aggregate default exposure across the entire guarantee portfolio. This report drives reserve calculations, collections prioritization, and periodic program risk reviews.

Summary Report (Finance). High-level program metrics by institution and term: total agreements guaranteed (count and amount), total remitted on 1st and 2nd remittance (count and amount), total defaulted (count and amount). Also includes NBS fees: enrollment fees, returned payment fees, credit card fees. Not a detail report.

Why: Program leadership and Finance need a single view of the guarantee program's performance — guarantee rate, remittance totals, and default exposure — to assess program health, identify underperforming institutions, and report to leadership.

Program Statistics. Higher-level summary than the Finance Summary Report. Provides: percentage of total agreements guaranteed, percentage not guaranteed, and percentage defaulted across the program.

Why: NBS periodically reviews the guarantee program's aggregate performance to determine whether enrollment fee schedules and down payment requirements need adjustment based on changes to state regulations, default rates, or tuition rates. This report provides the aggregate input for those reviews.

Pay Over Time

Long-Term Plans (LTPP)

Long-Term Payment Plans share the same auto-debit mechanics as standard payment plans but differ in duration, use case, and communication tone. Requirements below document what must be distinct; everything not called out here follows standard payment plan behavior.

Overview: How LTPP Is Different

Primary Use Case: Past-Due Balance Recovery. LTPP's primary use is collecting past-due accounts — balances that were not paid during the term and have aged beyond standard payment plan eligibility. The student is almost always no longer enrolled. Some institutions allow exceptions where a student remains enrolled while paying a past-due balance on an LTPP. The secondary use case is fixed-price programs longer than 12 months in duration.

Why: The collections context changes everything downstream: communications are different in tone (collections vs. onboarding), the student relationship to the institution is different (alumnus or former student vs. current student), and the institution's goals are different (debt recovery vs. retention). These differences must be reflected in the system configuration, not just the letter templates.

LTPP Is Auto-Debit, Not Invoice. Unlike International Payment Plans, LTPP uses the same automatic payment processing as standard payment plans. The student authorizes automatic withdrawals on a schedule. This is a critical distinction from loans or buy-now-pay-later arrangements.

Why: This shared mechanic means the core payment processing infrastructure is reused. Differences are in configuration options (duration, down payment thresholds), communication templates, and eligibility logic — not in the fundamental payment model.

The Original Receivable Remains. LTPP is explicitly NOT a loan and NOT a buy-now-pay-later arrangement. When a student enrolls in LTPP, the original receivable at the school remains outstanding and is only reduced as payments on the plan are processed. When a student fails to make scheduled payments the plan is terminated and the school resumes collection activities on the original receivable. The "flag" in the school's system that the student is on a payment plan is the only indicator — the original debt is not replaced or paid off by the plan itself.

Why: This distinction matters for school accounting, collections handoffs, and any downstream credit reporting. The system must accurately communicate plan status to the institution's SIS via the existing flag mechanism, and on termination must cleanly return the account to the school's collection workflow without requiring manual reconciliation.

Late Fees Pause, Then Resume. While a student is on an LTPP, late fees that would otherwise accrue on the past-due balance are paused. If the plan is terminated due to payment failure, late fee assessment resumes on the outstanding balance from the point of termination forward — not retroactively for the paused period.

Why: This is the institution's incentive for the student to stay on the plan. The system must accurately coordinate with the institution's late fee assessment processes and communicate the pause/resume status via the SIS flag or integration so the institution's billing system does not double-assess fees during the plan period.

Configuration Requirements
