Extended Duration Options. LTPP must support plan durations of 12, 18, 24, 30, and 36+ months. Standard payment plans typically run 4–12 months within a single term. Institutions must be able to configure which duration options are available for past-due accounts vs. fixed-price programs.

Why: Past-due balances often exceed what a student can repay in a standard term-length plan. A student with $10,000+ in past-due charges needs 24–36 months at a manageable monthly payment. The example from the LTPP source document: 24-month plan at $478/month for a ~$11,500 balance.

Down Payment Configuration. Institutions must be able to require a down payment at the time of LTPP enrollment. The down payment amount or percentage must be configurable per institution. This may be higher than the down payment for standard payment plans given the past-due context.

Why: A down payment serves as a commitment signal in a collections context — a student who won't make a down payment is unlikely to complete a 24-month plan. The institution needs control over this threshold to align with their collections policy and state regulatory requirements.

Eligibility Criteria by Account Status. Institutions must be able to configure which account statuses are eligible for LTPP vs. standard plans: minimum balance thresholds, age of debt, enrollment status (enrolled, non-enrolled, graduated). A separate eligibility ruleset from standard plans is required.

Why: Mixing past-due recovery accounts with current-term payment plans creates accounting complexity and student experience confusion. The eligibility rules must enforce the distinction so institutions don't accidentally offer LTPP to current students or vice versa.

Return Payment Policy. Institutions must be able to configure how many returned payments trigger plan termination (e.g., 1 return, 2 consecutive returns, 2 returns total). The LTPP example shows 2 returned payments leading to termination.

Why: Different institutions have different risk tolerances for plan continuation after returned payments. A single returned payment termination policy may be too strict; allowing unlimited retries with returns may expose the institution to prolonged collection delays. Configurability is needed to match institutional collections policy.

Enrollment Requirements

Distinct Enrollment Flow Entry Point. LTPP enrollment must be accessible through a different entry point than standard payment plan enrollment. A student visiting the standard payment setup flow should not encounter LTPP options unless they are eligible based on their account status. Where possible, the UI mechanics (plan selection, schedule preview, agreement acceptance, payment method entry) should reuse the standard enrollment flow components with appropriate labeling changes.

Why: Mixing past-due recovery plans with current-term plans in a single undifferentiated flow creates confusion for both students and institutional staff. The student experience must clearly communicate that they are setting up a plan for a past-due balance, not a current term.

Balance Snapshot at Enrollment. At the time of LTPP enrollment, the system must capture the exact balance being covered by the plan. Any subsequent charges assessed to the account (e.g., late fees after plan termination, new enrollment charges) are not included in the plan balance. The plan is for the balance as of enrollment date only.

Why: The original receivable remains at the school. The plan covers a fixed amount — the balance at enrollment. If the school adds new charges later (or if the student re-enrolls), those are separate from the plan balance. The system must clearly differentiate between plan balance and total account balance.

Financial Responsibility Agreement Acknowledgment. LTPP enrollment must include acknowledgment of a Financial Responsibility Agreement that specifically covers past-due collections practices, including: late fee assessment and pause, plan termination conditions, return of account to collections on plan failure, potential credit reporting, and collection agency referral. This is distinct from the standard enrollment FRA.

Why: As documented in the source material, Indiana University, Temple, and UMass Amherst all have FRAs that explicitly authorize collection practices. The LTPP context adds a collections-specific dimension that a standard enrollment FRA may not cover adequately. Regulatory risk requires explicit disclosure of what happens when the plan fails.

Payment Processing Requirements

Same Auto-Debit Infrastructure as Standard Plans. LTPP uses the same automatic payment processing as standard plans — Nelnet processes scheduled payments automatically. No invoice-and-wait model. No manual payment steps for the student. The student authorizes auto-debit at enrollment and payments process on schedule.

Why: Reusing existing infrastructure reduces build complexity and maintenance burden. It also reflects the actual product design: LTPP is a longer-duration variant of the existing plan, not a fundamentally different payment model.

Plan Balance Reduction on Payment. Each processed payment must reduce the outstanding plan balance and correspondingly reduce the original receivable at the school (via SIS integration flag/balance update). The remaining balance, next payment date, and remaining payment count must be visible in the student portal.

Why: Students on a 24–36 month plan need to see progress to maintain motivation to stay enrolled in the plan. Institutions need accurate receivable balance tracking for their financial reporting.

Returned Payment Handling and Retry. When a payment is returned, the system must: (1) notify the student immediately, (2) attempt a configurable number of retries on a configurable schedule, (3) track the return count against the institution's termination threshold, and (4) terminate the plan and notify the institution when the threshold is reached.

Why: The LTPP example shows a returned payment on 11/7 → re-attempt on 11/20 → second return on 11/22 → plan termination. The system must handle this lifecycle reliably with full audit trail so the institution can resume collections with accurate records.

Communication Requirements

Collections-Context Communication Tone. All LTPP communications (enrollment confirmation, payment reminders, returned payment notices, plan termination notices) must use a collections-appropriate tone that is firm but professional — distinct from the encouraging, supportive tone appropriate for current students setting up standard plans. The student relationship is different (former student / past-due account vs. current student).

Why: Communications calibrated for onboarding or retention are not appropriate for collections. Institutions managing past-due balances have legal considerations around collections communications (FDCPA compliance, TCPA for text/calls). The tone and content of these communications must align with collections best practices, not student onboarding communications.

Separate Communication Templates. LTPP must use a separate library of communication templates from standard plans. Institutions must be able to configure LTPP-specific templates for: plan enrollment confirmation, upcoming payment reminder, payment processed confirmation, returned payment notice, plan termination notice, and late fee resumption notice. These must not inherit from or accidentally send standard plan templates.

Why: Template separation prevents the wrong tone being applied to a collections communication and allows institutions to have their legal and collections teams review LTPP-specific communications independently from standard plan communications.

Institution Notification on Plan Termination. When an LTPP is terminated due to payment failure, the institution must receive an automated notification with: student name and ID, original plan balance, remaining balance at termination, payment history on the plan, and termination reason. This enables the institution to immediately resume collection activities without manual follow-up to determine account status.

Why: The institution's collections workflow resumes on plan termination. Any delay in their receiving accurate account status extends the time to collection resolution and increases the likelihood of the balance becoming uncollectable.

Termination & Default Requirements

Plan Termination Lifecycle. On plan termination: (1) automatic payments must stop immediately, (2) the SIS flag indicating the student is on a payment plan must be updated to reflect plan termination, (3) any paused late fee assessment must be resumed for future periods, (4) the institution must be notified per the requirements above, and (5) the student must be notified with the remaining balance owed and next steps for resolution.

Why: A clean handoff at termination is critical. If automatic payments continue after termination or the SIS flag is not updated, the institution cannot properly manage the account in their collections workflow. The termination event must be atomic and auditable.

Re-enrollment After Termination. Institutions must be able to configure whether a student whose plan was terminated can re-enroll in a new LTPP (e.g., after a period of time, or never). The system must enforce this configuration and display an appropriate message to the student if re-enrollment is not permitted.

Why: Some institutions may offer a second-chance plan with modified terms (higher down payment, shorter duration). Others may prefer to refer all terminated accounts to outside collections with no re-enrollment option. Configurability is required to match institutional policy.

Pay Over Time

International Plans

International Payment Plans are invoice-based plans paid through international payment vendors. They differ fundamentally from standard and LTPP plans in that there is no automatic debit — the student receives a payment notice and manually initiates payment through an international vendor. Requirements below document what is distinct; integration with the payment plan enrollment flow follows the same presentation patterns where possible.

Overview: How International Plans Are Different

Invoice-Based, Not Auto-Debit. International payment plans do not use automatic debit. Instead of processing a scheduled payment automatically, the system sends the student an invoice/payment notice on each scheduled due date. The student must manually log in to an international payment vendor (e.g., Flywire, Convera, or similar) and initiate the payment themselves. This is because international payment processing requires going through specialized international payment infrastructure that supports non-USD currencies and cross-border transactions.

Why: International students paying in non-USD currencies cannot use standard ACH or card auto-debit mechanisms. International payment vendors handle currency conversion, compliance with cross-border payment regulations, and local payment methods in the student's home country. The manual initiation model is the current operational reality for international payments; this may change if long-term auto-pay becomes feasible through international vendors in the future.

Triggered by Currency Need, Not Student Type. A student should be offered an international plan option when they need to pay in a currency other than USD. The trigger is not being an "international student" per se — it is the payment currency. A domestic student whose family is paying from a foreign account could also select an international plan. Conversely, an international student who has a USD bank account and wants auto-debit should be able to use a standard plan.

Why: Routing based on student type (international vs. domestic) rather than payment need would create a worse experience for both groups. The system should present plan options based on the student's indicated payment currency, not their visa status or country of origin.

Enrollment & Plan Selection

Dual Plan Presentation. When a student is selecting a payment plan, both standard (auto-debit) plans and international (invoice) plans must be presented simultaneously. The student must be able to see both options and choose between them. The presentation must clearly explain the difference: standard plans debit automatically, international plans require manual payment through an international vendor each period.

Why: A student who needs to pay in a non-USD currency needs to see international plan options presented alongside standard ones — they should not have to know in advance to look for a separate "international" section. At the same time, an international student who has a USD account and wants the convenience of auto-debit should not be forced into the manual invoice model. Simultaneous presentation of both options with clear explanation allows the student to make an informed choice.

Currency Selection at Enrollment. During international plan enrollment, the student must select the currency in which they will pay. The system must display the equivalent amount in the selected currency based on the current exchange rate from the international payment vendor at time of enrollment. The institution receives USD; the currency conversion is handled by the international vendor.

Why: The student's payment amount in their local currency will vary from period to period based on exchange rate fluctuations. This must be clearly disclosed at enrollment — the plan amount in USD is fixed, but the amount the student pays in their local currency may vary. This disclosure is both a regulatory requirement and a trust/transparency requirement.

International Vendor Selection or Routing. At enrollment, the student must be directed to the appropriate international payment vendor configured by the institution. If the institution supports multiple international vendors (e.g., Flywire for some regions, Convera for others), the routing must be configured at the institution level. The student should experience a seamless redirect to the vendor's payment interface rather than having to find and navigate the vendor on their own.

Why: Sending a student to "find an international payment vendor" without a specific link and routing creates drop-off and support burden. The enrollment flow must complete the handoff to the vendor's interface so the student can immediately initiate their first payment without friction.

Plan Agreement and Disclosure. International plan enrollment must include a disclosure specific to the invoice model: that payments are not automatic, that the student is responsible for initiating each payment by the due date, that failure to pay by the due date will result in (configurable: late fee, plan default, etc.), and that exchange rates will vary. Standard auto-debit authorization language must not appear in international plan agreements.

Why: Using the standard plan agreement language (which authorizes automatic debit) for an invoice-based plan would be legally incorrect. The agreement must accurately reflect the manual payment obligation and disclose the exchange rate risk.

Invoicing & Notifications

Payment Due Notifications (Invoice Equivalent). On each scheduled payment date, the system must send the student a payment due notification that includes: the amount due in USD, a link or redirect to the international payment vendor, the due date, instructions for completing payment, and the consequences of non-payment. This notification takes the place of the automatic debit that standard plans would process.

Why: The student cannot be reminded too clearly that they need to act. Unlike standard plans where the burden is on the system to process payment, international plans require the student to take action. The notification must be prominent and provide a direct path to completing payment.

Payment Confirmation and Reconciliation. When the international vendor processes the student's payment, the system must receive a payment confirmation from the vendor and update the student's plan balance accordingly. The payment confirmation must include the USD amount received (not the local currency amount paid) so the school's receivable can be accurately reduced. Reconciliation timing depends on the vendor's processing timeline (international payments may take 1–5 business days to settle).

Why: Without automated payment confirmation and reconciliation, institutions would need to manually match international payments to student accounts — a significant operational burden. The integration with the international vendor must include payment confirmation webhooks or polling sufficient to keep the student's balance accurate within one business day of settlement.

Overdue Notifications. If a student has not completed payment by the due date, the system must send escalating overdue notifications on a configurable schedule. The overdue notification must clearly state: the amount past due, the overdue date, the link to complete payment, and what happens if payment is not received (plan termination, late fees, etc.).

Why: Manual payment plans will have higher non-payment rates than auto-debit plans simply because they require the student to act. Proactive overdue communications reduce the time to resolution and give the student multiple opportunities to act before consequences are triggered.

Vendor Integration Requirements

International Payment Vendor API Integration. Horizon must integrate with at least one international payment vendor (e.g., Flywire) via API. The integration must support: (1) passing the student's payment amount and due date to the vendor to generate a payment link, (2) receiving payment confirmation and settlement amounts in USD, (3) handling failed or cancelled payments, and (4) supporting currency selection by the student.

Why: Without a real API integration, the international plan feature is not functional — it would require manual steps by institutional staff to create payment links and track payments. The integration is the core of the feature.

Multi-Vendor Support. The platform must support configuring different international payment vendors at the institution level. Different institutions may have existing relationships with different vendors (Flywire, Convera, Western Union Education, etc.). The vendor integration architecture must be extensible to add new vendor integrations without requiring structural changes to the plan enrollment flow.

Why: Forcing all institutions to use a single international vendor would block adoption by institutions with existing vendor contracts. Extensibility protects future market access as new international payment vendors emerge.

Currency & Amount Requirements

USD as the Plan Base Currency. All plan amounts, balances, and payment records within the Horizon system must be stored and displayed in USD. Currency conversion is handled at the vendor level when the student initiates payment. The school's receivable is reduced in USD regardless of the currency the student paid in.

Why: Storing multi-currency amounts in the core system creates reconciliation complexity and financial reporting risk. The clean separation — USD in Horizon, conversion at the vendor — keeps the accounting simple and auditable.

Exchange Rate Disclosure at Enrollment and Payment. At enrollment, the student must see an indicative exchange rate for their selected currency. At each payment due date, the notification must either include a current indicative rate or direct the student to the vendor's interface where the rate will be shown before confirming payment. The system must clearly disclose that rates change and the USD amount is fixed while the local currency amount may vary.

Why: Regulatory requirements and consumer protection best practices require clear disclosure of exchange rate risk. A student who sets up a "24-payment plan of $300/month" but doesn't realize their actual monthly cost in INR or CNY will vary significantly is likely to stop paying when rates move against them. Clear disclosure at enrollment reduces this risk.

Flywire Integration & Status Synchronization

Flywire as Primary Integration. The initial international payment integration must support Flywire as the primary vendor. Flywire integration must: (1) accept the student's payment amount, due date, student ID, institution ID, and payer contact information from Horizon to generate a payment session; (2) redirect the consumer to the Flywire-hosted payment interface; (3) receive real-time status events from Flywire for each stage of payment progression; (4) surface payment status in Account Activity and My Transactions for both consumers and institution users. Future vendors (Convera, Western Union Education, etc.) must be addable via the same extensible architecture without structural changes to the enrollment flow.

Why: Flywire is the most widely adopted international payment provider among NCC's existing client base. Delivering Flywire integration first maximizes immediate utility while the extensible architecture protects NCC's ability to serve institutions that use or prefer other vendors.

Real-Time Payment Status Tracking. International payments progress through multiple discrete stages before funds reach the institution. Horizon must track and display each status stage to consumers and institution users: Initiated (payer started the process at Flywire), In Progress (payment is being processed), Pending Delivery (funds received by Flywire, pending disbursement to institution), Delivered (funds received by institution — triggers ERP posting), Cancelled (payment cancelled by payer or timed out), and Failed (processing error). Status updates must be reflected in Account Activity and My Transactions within the sync interval configured for the integration. Consumers must see a plain-language status description — not raw status codes.

Why: International payments can take 1–5 business days to settle. Without transparent status tracking, students and parents make panicked calls to the bursar asking whether their payment arrived — a high-cost support interaction that the status display is designed to prevent. Institution users need accurate status to answer those calls when they do come.

Confirmation Notification on Delivery. When an international payment reaches Delivered status — indicating funds have been received by the institution — a confirmation notification must be sent to the student (account holder). If the payment was initiated by an Authorized Party or guest payer, both the AP/guest and the student must receive confirmation. The notification must include: amount delivered in USD, date of delivery, and any remaining balance on the student's account. Delivery status is also the trigger for ERP posting (the payment is automatically posted back to the institution's ERP when it reaches Delivered).

Why: Students and families making international payments are often anxious about delivery timing — they've made a payment and don't know when it will clear. The delivery notification closes that anxiety loop. ERP auto-posting at delivery ensures the institution's books reflect the payment accurately without requiring manual intervention from the bursar.

Refunds on International Payments

As a Finance Admin

Institution-Initiated Refunds. Institution users (Finance Admin and Full Admin) must be able to initiate refunds on international payments that have reached Delivered status — fully or partially. The refund workflow must: (1) only be available after a payment reaches Delivered (refunds cannot be initiated on in-progress or pending payments); (2) enforce that the refund amount does not exceed the delivered amount; (3) route the refund through the same Flywire integration that processed the original payment, so the student receives the refund in their original payment method; (4) log the refund initiation and completion in the audit trail; (5) update the student's account balance to reflect the refund. Flywire-side refund event confirmations must be received and recorded to confirm successful processing.

Why: International payment refunds are operationally complex — refunding to a foreign payment method through a third-party vendor requires precise integration. Limiting refunds to Delivered-status payments only prevents institutions from attempting to reverse payments that are still in-flight, which Flywire cannot process. Routing refunds back through Flywire ensures the student receives funds in a way that clears cross-border banking requirements.

ERP Posting & Reconciliation

Automatic ERP Posting on Delivery. When a Flywire international payment reaches Delivered status, the payment must be automatically posted back to the institution's ERP via the existing payment write-back integration. The ERP posting must use USD amounts (not local currency). The post must include the transaction ID, student ID, amount, posting date, and payment method type (International — Flywire). Auto-posting on delivery is the default behavior; future phases will add institution-configurable control over posting timing, but this is not included in the initial delivery.

Why: Institutions need delivered payments reflected in their SIS/ERP to update the student's account balance and release any registration holds. Manual ERP posting for international payments would require bursar staff to match each Flywire delivery confirmation to a student account and manually enter the payment — a high-effort, error-prone process that would erode the value of the integration.

Convera International Payments

Institution Admin

Convera as a Configurable International Payment Vendor. Convera is available as a second international payment vendor alongside Flywire. Institution admins can enable Flywire, Convera, or both. When both vendors are enabled, the institution configures a preference order that determines which vendor is presented first to a consumer for countries supported by both. If only one vendor supports the consumer's country, that vendor is presented without preference logic.

Why: Different institutions have existing commercial relationships or preferred currency corridors with one vendor over the other; supporting both vendors and an institution-configurable preference order avoids locking institutions into a single vendor relationship.

Student / Consumer

Convera Payment Lifecycle. Convera payments follow the same five-status normalized lifecycle as Flywire: Initiated → Guaranteed → Completed/Delivered → Cancelled → Expired. At Guaranteed status, a fee-only Service ID 2 transaction is applied to the student's account representing the Convera service charge to the institution, consistent with Flywire Guaranteed behavior. At Delivered status, ERP auto-posting triggers to write back the full payment amount to the student's ledger.

Why: Consistent lifecycle handling across vendors ensures that downstream processes — ERP posting, notifications, and reporting — operate on a single normalized model regardless of which vendor processed the payment.

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

Convera Payment Detail Storage. For each Convera payment, the platform stores and displays in the student's communication history: the original currency, the amount in original currency, the exchange rate applied, and the USD equivalent. These details are visible to institution admins in the student's payment history view.

Why: Institutions must be able to reconcile international payments against their ledger in USD; storing the currency conversion details provides the audit record needed for both institutional reconciliation and potential student disputes.

International Payment Vendor Status Normalization

Platform / Engineering

Normalized Status Model at Ingest. The platform maintains a single normalized status model for all international payment vendors. Vendor-specific status codes are mapped to the five standard lifecycle statuses (Initiated, Guaranteed, Completed/Delivered, Cancelled, Expired) at the point of ingest. Institutions and consumers always see the normalized status; vendor-specific codes are never surfaced in the institution or consumer UI.

Why: Exposing vendor-specific status codes to institutions would require institutions to maintain separate workflows per vendor; normalization ensures that institution configuration, reporting, and consumer communication are vendor-agnostic.

Platform / NBS Technical Support

Configurable Normalization Mapping Without Code Deployment. The normalization mapping between vendor-specific status codes and the platform's standard lifecycle statuses is configurable by NBS Technical Support without requiring a code deployment. New vendors can be onboarded and their status codes mapped through a configuration change alone.

Why: Requiring a code deployment for each new vendor or each vendor status code change creates an unacceptable onboarding lead time; configuration-driven mapping allows NBS to respond to vendor API changes or new vendor additions with operational rather than engineering effort.

Platform / Engineering

Vendor-Agnostic Downstream Trigger Behavior. Status change webhooks from any configured international payment vendor trigger the same downstream actions — consumer and institution notifications, ERP posting, and reporting pipeline events — regardless of which vendor originated the webhook. The consumer-facing communication history displays the normalized status and the vendor name (e.g., "Payment via Convera — Delivered").

Why: Vendor-specific webhook handling paths would duplicate downstream logic and create divergent behavior over time; a single normalized trigger ensures feature parity across vendors and reduces the regression surface when either vendor's API changes.

Solutions We Sell

One Time Payments

One-Time Student Account Payments is the first deliverable of Project Horizon's Payment Platform. It connects institutions to their student information systems, presents real-time account balance data in a clear, actionable format, and enables students and their authorized parties to make payments and invite others to help meet their financial obligations. The core promise: students can always answer what do I owe, why do I owe it, and when is it due — and act on that answer without leaving the portal.

Real-Time Balance Integration & Account Presentment

Real-Time Account Balance Integration. Horizon must connect to the institution's Student Information System (SIS) or ERP via a certified integration (cloud connector) to retrieve the student's current account balance in real time at the point of portal access. The balance must reflect all charges, credits, financial aid applied, and anticipated aid — sourced directly from the institution's system, never cached or approximated.

Why: Any lag between the institution's ledger and what the student sees in Horizon causes payment errors, double-payment disputes, and support calls. Real-time sourcing is the foundation of the trust model.

Account Presentment. The student's account view must display a clear breakdown of: total charges by type and date, financial aid applied vs. anticipated, net balance due, due date(s), and any holds or flags on the account. The presentation must answer the three core questions — what do I owe, why do I owe it, when is it due — without requiring the student to navigate to a separate screen or download a statement.

Why: The most common bursar support call is a student who cannot understand their bill. Presenting the balance in a clear, contextualized format directly reduces call volume and builds student confidence in their financial standing.

Real-Time Transaction Posting to ERP. Every payment processed through Horizon must post back to the institution's ERP/SIS in real time via the cloud connector. The posting must update the student's ledger balance within the institution's system as soon as the payment is confirmed, not on a batch schedule. Posting failures must be flagged immediately with retry logic and alerts to institution admins.

Why: If Horizon shows a payment as processed but the institution's system still shows a balance due, students face holds, registration blocks, or collections actions for balances they've already paid. Real-time posting is the difference between a trustworthy platform and a liability.

ERP / SSO

Student & Authorized Party Payments

Student One-Time Payment. Students must be able to make a one-time payment against their account balance via the Horizon consumer portal. Payment must be applicable to the full balance due or to specific charges (where institution configuration allows). Accepted methods: ACH/eCheck and credit/debit card. The student must receive a real-time confirmation screen with a payment reference number, a confirmation email/notification, and an immediate balance update in the portal.

Why: One-time payment is the highest-volume transaction type on the platform. Any friction in the flow — extra steps, unclear balance data, confusing confirmation — directly translates into abandonment, increased support contacts, and delayed collections.

Authorized Party (AP) Access & Payments. Authorized parties invited by a student must have their own Horizon portal credentials and their own dashboard showing the student's balance (per the student's visibility grant). APs must be able to make one-time payments on the student's behalf from their own account. Both the AP and the student must receive payment confirmation. The AP experience is distinct from the student's — APs do not see the student's full academic record, only the financial data the student has shared.

Why: A significant proportion of higher education payments are made by parents and families, not students. APs need their own authenticated access — sharing student credentials is a security and privacy risk, and it is not a workflow that works for most families.

Student Management of Authorized Parties. Students must be able to invite, view, and revoke Authorized Parties from their portal at any time. When inviting an AP, the student sets the level of access (view balance only, or view + pay). Each invitation is sent to the AP's email address. Students can revoke AP access at any time; revocation takes effect immediately and removes the AP's ability to view or pay on the account.

Why: FERPA places the student in control of who can see their financial information. The student-managed invite model ensures compliance while providing a self-service workflow that doesn't require institution admin involvement for every AP relationship.

AP Management of Student Relationship. Authorized Parties must be able to manage their own account settings (email, notification preferences, payment methods) independently of the student. An AP who manages payments for multiple students (e.g., a parent paying for two children at the same institution) must have a single AP account showing all student accounts they have access to, with clear switching between student contexts.

Why: An AP forced to create a separate account for each student they pay for is an AP who will call support. Multi-student AP access with a single login reduces friction for the most engaged payers on the platform.

Guest Payments

Guest Payment Invite (Student-Initiated). Students must be able to generate a one-time guest payment link from their portal and share it with a third party (e.g., an employer, a scholarship organization, a grandparent) who does not have or want a Horizon account. The guest link is tied to the student's account, is valid for a configurable period, and may be limited to a specific payment amount. The guest payer does not need to create an account.

Why: Not every third-party payer will create an account. A guest link provides a zero-friction path for ad-hoc payments from payers who have a specific need but will not become recurring users of the portal.

Guest Payer Experience. The guest payment flow accessed via the invite link must: clearly identify which student and institution the payment is for, display the amount requested (if specified) or allow the guest to enter a payment amount within institution-configured limits, accept card and ACH payment, send a confirmation receipt to the guest's email, and notify the student that the payment was made. The guest payment flow must not require account creation at any step.

Why: A guest payer who encounters a sign-up wall will abandon the payment and the student will have to seek another method. The no-account-required constraint is non-negotiable for this flow to serve its purpose.

Payment Processing

Card & Bank Payments. The platform must accept ACH/eCheck and credit/debit card payments (Visa, Mastercard, Discover, Amex) for all payment types: student one-time, AP one-time, guest, and plan installments. Payment method selection and entry must be available in a single step. Card numbers must be tokenized; no raw card data may be stored in Horizon systems. PCI DSS compliance is mandatory.

Why: Card and bank payments are the universal expectation for consumer financial transactions. Limiting payment methods is a direct cause of abandonment and is not acceptable for a product competing in the higher education fintech space.

Returned Payment Handling. When a payment is returned (ACH return, card chargeback, insufficient funds), the platform must: immediately reverse the balance credit in the portal, notify the student and any relevant APs via the appropriate communication channel, apply any returned payment fee configured by the institution, and surface the returned payment prominently in the student's account view. Multiple returned payments by the same payer must trigger a configurable restriction on future ACH payments.

Why: Returned payments that are not surfaced immediately create a window where the student believes their balance is paid but it is not — potentially leading to a registration hold that surprises them days later. Prompt, visible notification reduces that harm.

Statements & Communication History

On-Demand Statement. Students and authorized parties must be able to generate an on-demand account statement from the portal at any time. The statement must show the current account balance, all charges by type and date, all payments and credits applied, and the net amount due. The statement must be downloadable as a formatted PDF. On-demand statements are distinct from billed statements — they reflect the real-time account state at the moment of generation.

Why: Students frequently need statements for scholarship applications, employer reimbursements, FAFSA verification, and appeals. An on-demand statement eliminates the need to contact the bursar's office for a document they can self-serve in under a minute.

Communication History. The platform must maintain and surface a complete communication history for each student account, including: payment confirmation receipts, refund receipts, returned payment notices, courtesy notifications to students and APs regarding payment activity, guest payer invite messages, and any institution-generated balance notifications. All communications must be timestamped and accessible in the portal for a minimum of 24 months.

Why: Disputes ("I never received a notice," "I have a receipt") are the primary driver of compliance risk and bursar call volume. An immutable, accessible communication history is the platform's defense layer — both for the institution in an audit and for the student in a dispute.

Institution Admin & Servicing

Institution User Access & Assisted Payments. Institution staff with appropriate roles must be able to access any student's account, view their real-time balance and transaction history, and initiate payments on a student's behalf (assisted payment) when the student calls in or visits in person. Assisted payments must be logged with the acting staff member's identity. The institution admin portal must be distinct from the student portal but share the same underlying account data.

Why: A significant portion of payments in higher education are still assisted — a student hands a card to a bursar staff member who processes it. The platform must support this workflow natively rather than requiring staff to use a separate legacy system for in-person transactions.

Servicing Actions — Refunds, Chargebacks, Notes. Institution admins must be able to perform standard payment servicing actions from the admin portal: issue refunds against posted transactions (per role-based permission rules), manage chargeback responses by providing transaction documentation, and add internal notes to student account records. Servicing notes must be timestamped, attributed to the acting user, and retained in the audit log.

Why: Refunds and chargeback management are routine financial operations that must be handled within Horizon to maintain a complete transaction record. Forcing staff to use external systems for these actions creates reconciliation gaps.

Future Roadmap (Prioritized)

International Payments — Flywire. Integration with Flywire to enable international students to pay in their home currency via Flywire's international payment network. The payment is converted to USD and posted to the student's account as a standard transaction. Students must be able to initiate an international payment from their Horizon portal and receive a confirmation referencing both the Flywire transaction and the Horizon record.

Why: International students are a growing and high-value student population at most institutions. Without an integrated international payment path, these students face friction converting currency and lose confidence that their payments are being applied correctly.

International Payments — Convera. Integration with Convera as an alternative international payment provider, providing an additional international payment option alongside Flywire for institutions that have existing Convera relationships or prefer its routing.

Why: Institutional payment vendor relationships vary; offering two international payment integrations lets institutions work with their preferred provider without requiring platform switching.

Multiple Accounts per Student. Support for students who have multiple account balances at the same institution (e.g., undergraduate + continuing education, or housing account separate from tuition). Each account must be presentable independently with its own balance, charges, and payment history, while the student can switch between accounts in a single portal session.

Why: Larger institutions often have distinct billing systems for different programs or departments. Students enrolled in multiple programs need a unified payment experience without being forced to manage separate logins or portals.

Student Choice Refunds Integration. Integration to support student-directed refund disbursement — students select their preferred method (bank transfer, prepaid card, check) for receiving credit balance refunds from the institution. The integration must support at least one Student Choice provider and must surface refund status in the Horizon portal.

Why: Credit balance refunds (excess aid, overpayments) are a major student pain point when institutions default to check-by-mail. Student Choice integrations directly improve student financial wellness and satisfaction.

Additional Roadmap Items. The following capabilities are identified for future phases: Account Presentment & Authorized Party Enhancements · Customization of On-Demand Statement · Bulk Credit Card Refunds · NBS Service Fee Servicing · Banner ERP Integration · Tuition Insurance · System Maintenance Window Configuration · SSO to Direct Authentication Migration · Activity Card on Person Dashboard · Future-Dated Payments.

Why: Documenting roadmap items in the PRD ensures they are visible during architecture and API design decisions — building with future integrations in mind prevents costly refactoring when these features are scoped.

Solutions We Sell

Billing

Billing is the process institutions use to deliver amounts owed to account holders and their authorized parties at defined intervals — monthly, by academic term, or event-driven. Its primary purpose is to inform users that a balance exists and action is required. Horizon Billing reinvents this for modern higher education: shifting from static PDFs, batch jobs, and fragile audit trails to a real-time, event-driven, compliant, durable billing platform. Every notification is immutable, linked to who was notified and when — the first truly audit-ready billing system in higher education.

Statement Presentment

Digital Billing Statement Generation. The platform must generate a digital billing statement for each student each term. Each statement must include: all charges assessed by type and date, all credits and payments applied, net balance due, due date(s), available payment options (direct link to portal, payment plan enrollment), and the institution's billing contact information. Statements must be accessible in the consumer portal under account history and downloadable as formatted PDF. Statements are point-in-time snapshots — immutable once generated — and must be stored for the full retention period.

Why: An immutable, point-in-time statement snapshot is far more defensible in audit, dispute, and collections scenarios than a regenerated PDF. Institutions facing regulatory scrutiny need evidence of what was communicated and when — not a best-effort reconstruction.

On-Demand Statement. Students and authorized parties must be able to generate an on-demand account statement reflecting the real-time account state at the moment of generation. On-demand statements are distinct from billed statements: they reflect current balance, not a billing-cycle snapshot. Downloadable as PDF. Students use these for scholarship applications, employer reimbursements, FAFSA verification, and financial aid appeals.

Why: On-demand statements reduce billing office inquiries. Students who can self-serve their own statement documentation do not need to contact the bursar — a meaningful operational savings at scale across thousands of students.

Statement Delivery Notification. When a new billing statement is generated, the platform must notify the student and any authorized parties with balance visibility via their preferred channel (email, SMS, push). The notification must include: a direct link to the portal, the amount due, and the due date. Delivery must occur within 24 hours of statement generation. Delivery status and read receipt must be captured and stored as part of the communication history.

Why: Notification-at-bill-generation drives earlier payment than waiting for students to check the portal proactively. Read tracking and delivery confirmation eliminate the "I never received a bill" dispute — institutions can prove notification was sent and opened.

Billing Communications & Reminders

Configurable Due Date Reminders. The platform must send automated pre-due-date reminders to students with outstanding balances: configurable N days before the due date (options: 7, 14, 30 days), on the due date, and N days after if still unpaid. Reminder cadence, content, and channel must be configurable per institution. Reminders must be automatically suppressed for students enrolled in a payment plan that covers their outstanding balance — sending an overdue notice to a student making faithful plan payments is an error, not just an annoyance.

Why: Intelligent suppression of reminders for plan-enrolled students is as important as sending them for non-enrolled students. Getting this wrong erodes student trust and generates avoidable support contacts.

Communication History — Full Audit Record. Every billing communication — statement generation notifications, due date reminders, late notices, payment confirmations, refund receipts, returned payment notices — must be recorded in an immutable, timestamped communication history linked to the student's account. The history must record: communication type, delivery channel, delivery status, read status (where the channel supports it), and the content snapshot. This record must be accessible to institution admins and exportable for audit purposes.

Why: Communication history is the platform's defense layer. When a student claims "I never received a notice" or a regulator asks "what did you communicate and when," the communication history is the answer. Immutability means it cannot be altered after the fact — which is what makes it defensible.

Paperless Billing Enrollment. Students must be able to opt into paperless billing (digital-only) via the consumer portal. For institutions with paper statement delivery via a third-party mail house, Horizon must suppress paper delivery for opted-in students. Paperless status must be recorded and available in institution reporting.

Why: Paper statements are a significant cost center for large institutions and a friction point for students who expect digital-first communication. Driving paperless adoption is a direct cost reduction and a consumer experience improvement.

Billing Platform Architecture

Event-Driven Billing Architecture. The billing engine must be event-driven: billing statements are triggered by defined account events (charge posted, aid applied, due date set) rather than batch jobs on a fixed schedule. This enables support for any billing model — term-based, monthly, rolling, cohort-based — without architectural changes. The event model must be extensible so that new billing triggers can be added without rebuilding the notification service.

Why: Batch-based billing systems break in non-standard calendar scenarios (rolling programs, accelerated terms, cohort-based pricing). An event-driven architecture is the foundation that supports the full spectrum of higher education billing models without special-casing each one.

Customizable Statement Template. Institutions must be able to configure the visual presentation of their billing statements: institution logo, header/footer content, contact information, color scheme, and which charge categories are shown as distinct line items vs. grouped. Template changes must take effect on the next billing cycle without requiring NBS engineering involvement.

Why: Institutions have different branding requirements and different conventions for how they present charges. A configurable template eliminates institution-specific development work and lets the institution control how their students experience billing.

Solutions We Sell

Checkout

Horizon Checkout is a lightweight, embeddable payment and enrollment flow that institutions can deploy at the point of a specific transaction — continuing education registration, event fees, departmental charges — without requiring the full Horizon portal experience. It is the bridge to non-traditional student payment contexts.

Embedded Checkout Experience

Embeddable Checkout Widget. Horizon Checkout must be embeddable as a drop-in component (JavaScript embed or iFrame) in third-party institution web properties — continuing education portals, departmental registration systems, event ticketing, and other non-SIS transaction contexts. The checkout widget must accept a charge amount and description from the host page and must process payment using the institution's configured Horizon payment rails without the student needing to navigate to the full Horizon portal.

Why: Continuing education students often have no relationship with the main bursar portal. Requiring them to create a full Horizon account to pay a $150 workshop fee will result in abandonment. An embeddable checkout lowers the barrier to payment for transactional interactions while still processing through Horizon's payment infrastructure.

Payment Plan Option at Checkout. When checkout is configured for a charge type that has eligible payment plan templates (e.g., a semester-long certificate program fee), the checkout widget must offer the student the option to enroll in a payment plan rather than paying in full. Plan enrollment via checkout must follow the same disclosure and agreement process as portal-based plan enrollment. This feature was identified in the HE Market section as a first-mover opportunity with no current competitive equivalents.

Why: Continuing education programs are growing and are price-sensitive. Offering a payment plan at the point of CE registration converts students who would otherwise not register due to upfront cost. This is an incremental revenue opportunity for institutions and a differentiation point for Horizon against general-purpose checkout solutions like Stripe.

Checkout Configuration

As an institution admin

Checkout Configuration in Admin. Institution admins must be able to create and configure named Checkout instances within the Horizon admin experience. Each Checkout instance has: a charge type label, accepted payment methods, plan template eligibility (if any), success redirect URL, and optional appearance customization (logo, accent color). Checkout instances are identified by a unique API key/embed code that the institution deploys in their third-party system.

Why: An institution may have multiple Checkout use cases — CE registration, event payments, library fines, athletics fees. Separate named instances allow distinct configuration per use case and allow the institution to enable/disable specific Checkout deployments without affecting others.

Solutions We Sell

Notify

Horizon Notify is the outbound communication layer — proactive student outreach beyond the transaction-triggered emails in ePay and Billing. It enables institutions to reach students with balance alerts, enrollment reminders, and financial wellness messaging on a configurable cadence, including students who have not yet logged into the Horizon portal.

Proactive Outreach

ERP-Driven Proactive Outreach. Notify must be able to trigger outbound messages to students based on ERP data events — not just Horizon portal events. This means a student with an outstanding balance who has never visited the Horizon portal must still receive a notification that drives them to the portal. The trigger data comes from the institution's ERP sync (balance posted, charge added, due date approaching) rather than from student portal activity.

Why: Students who don't know the Horizon portal exists are a lost opportunity. Proactive ERP-driven outreach is the mechanism by which Horizon reaches the entire student population with an amount due — not just the self-service-oriented students who would find the portal on their own. This is specifically called out in the Institution Vision section as a key capability.

As an institution admin

Notify Campaign Builder. Institution admins must be able to create targeted notification campaigns: select a student segment (all students with balance above $X, students in a specific program, students who have not logged in within N days), compose a message, and schedule delivery. Campaign results (delivered, opened, clicked, action taken in portal) must be visible in the admin reporting interface.

Why: Institutions do their most effective collections work through targeted outreach to specific student populations at specific moments — financial aid disbursement time, registration holds approaching, end-of-term. A campaign builder puts this targeting capability in the hands of the institution without requiring NBS or IT involvement for each campaign.

Communication Channel Support

Multi-Channel Notify Delivery. Notify must support delivery via email (primary), SMS (TCPA-compliant, institution-configurable), and in-app notification (for students who are logged into the portal). Message content must be configurable per channel — an SMS notification must be a concise text version of the email, not a truncated copy. Links in SMS and email must be trackable for open/click analytics.

Why: Notify's value proposition is reaching students where they are. Email-only reach means missing the growing population of students who primarily communicate via SMS and rarely check non-institutional email. Multi-channel delivery with appropriate content optimization per channel is the difference between Notify being a notification system and being an actual collections tool.

Solutions We Sell

Batch Credit Card Refunds

Horizon Batch Credit Card Refunds enables institutions to process large volumes of credit balance refunds back to the original payment card — typically driven by financial aid disbursements, overpayments, or withdrawal credits — without manual one-by-one processing.

Batch Processing

As a finance admin

Batch Refund File Upload. The platform must accept an institution-generated batch file (CSV or institution ERP export) containing a list of students with credit balance amounts to be refunded. The batch must be validated before processing — identifying records with missing card tokens, amounts exceeding the original transaction, or students with no card on file — and produce a validation report that the admin must review and approve before any refunds are processed.

Why: Bursar offices process hundreds to thousands of refunds at financial aid disbursement time. Manual one-by-one refund processing at that volume is operationally infeasible and error-prone. Batch processing with a validation gate prevents the institution from accidentally over-refunding or refunding to incorrect accounts.

Card Network Compliance for Refunds. Refunds must be processed back to the original card used for the payment where card network rules require it. The platform must enforce the network-specific refund window (typically 180 days for Visa/MC) and must identify records where the refund window has expired and an alternative refund method (check, ACH) is required. Alternative method routing must be flagged in the validation report rather than silently processed via the original card.

Why: Card network rules prohibit refunding to a different card than the one used for the original transaction, and restrict refunds to the original transaction amount. Violations result in chargebacks and potential card network penalties. The platform must enforce these rules so that institutions cannot inadvertently create a compliance issue by submitting an invalid batch.

As a finance admin

Batch Refund Reporting. After batch processing, the platform must produce a results report showing: each record's processing status (success, failed, flagged), the refund amount and card network, the date processed, and any exception notes. Failed records must be exportable as a separate file for manual follow-up. The report must be available the same business day as processing and must feed into the institution's reconciliation workflow.

Why: Without a comprehensive results report, the finance team cannot identify which students' refunds failed and need to be re-processed through an alternative method. Failures not caught promptly result in students missing expected refunds — a high-sensitivity issue, especially when the refund is tied to financial aid.

Admin Bulk Refund Tool

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

In-Portal Multi-Student Refund Selection. Institution Finance Admins can initiate a bulk refund for up to 100 students at a time directly within the portal without uploading a file. Admins search and select students from a filtered list view that surfaces only students with credit balances. For each selected student, the admin sees: student name, student ID, credit balance amount, original payment method(s), and a suggested refund amount pre-populated from the credit balance.

Why: The file-upload batch workflow is appropriate for large-scale end-of-term refund runs but creates unnecessary overhead for routine smaller batches; an in-portal tool reduces processing time and eliminates file preparation errors for Finance Admins handling day-to-day credit balance resolution.

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

Per-Student Amount Override and Batch Confirmation. Before processing, the admin can override the suggested refund amount for any individual student in the batch. After all amounts are set, the admin must review and explicitly confirm the total batch refund amount before processing begins. Confirmation is a required step and cannot be bypassed.

Why: Suggested amounts may not account for partial credits, holds, or manual adjustments; per-student override capability ensures accuracy; a mandatory batch total confirmation step creates a deliberate checkpoint that prevents accidental processing of incorrect totals.

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

Real-Time Processing Status and ERP Integration. As the bulk refund processes, the admin sees real-time status for each student's refund. Failed refunds are highlighted with a human-readable failure reason. Bulk refund results — including both successful and failed items — are included in the ERP Transmission Report (URS-ERP-01) and are distinguishable from file-upload batch refunds by a source indicator ("admin-portal-bulk") in the audit trail.

Why: Real-time status allows the admin to act on failures immediately; ERP report inclusion ensures bulk portal refunds are part of the same reconciliation workflow as all other refund types; the source indicator preserves auditability of which tool originated each refund batch.

Solutions We Sell

In-Person Tuition Payments

Horizon In-Person Tuition Payments enables institutions to accept payments at a physical bursar window or cashier station, processing card and cash (where applicable) transactions through the Horizon payment infrastructure — unifying the in-person and self-service payment experience in a single platform.

Teller / Cashier Experience

As a bursar staff / teller

Student Account Lookup at Window. Bursar tellers must be able to look up a student account in the Horizon admin interface by student ID, name, or institutional email. The lookup must return the student's current balance, open charges, active payment plans, and payment history. The teller must be able to process a payment on behalf of the student from this view — entering the payment amount, method (card swipe/tap, cash, check), and confirming the transaction — without requiring the student to log into the portal.

Why: Not all students use the self-service portal, and some payment types (cash, in-person card) require staff involvement by definition. Bursar staff processing in-person payments must see the same balance data that the portal shows — not a separate view from a different system — so there is one source of truth and no discrepancy between what the student saw online and what the teller sees.

Card Terminal Integration. In-person card payments must be processed through an integrated PCI-compliant card terminal (e.g., Ingenico, Verifone) connected to the Horizon admin workstation. Card data must never pass through the admin workstation — the terminal handles EMV/NFC capture and tokenization. The Horizon admin application receives only the token and authorization response from the terminal. The system must support chip, tap/contactless, and swipe (fallback) card acceptance.

Why: If in-person card data passes through the admin workstation, the workstation and its network become PCI scope — requiring extensive security controls, audits, and ongoing compliance burden for the institution's IT team. Terminal-based tokenization eliminates this scope entirely while still allowing the admin application to record and reconcile the transaction.

As a bursar teller

Receipt Generation. Upon successful payment, the system must produce a transaction receipt that can be printed to a receipt printer or emailed to the student. The receipt must include: institution name, student name and ID, payment amount, payment method (masked card or cash), transaction date and time, transaction reference number, and the updated account balance. Students who prefer email receipt over printed receipt must be able to provide an email address at the window.

Why: Physical receipts are expected at bursar windows. Students paying in person at the end of a hold situation often need a receipt as proof of payment to present to another office (registrar, housing) immediately after the transaction. Inability to produce a receipt generates a secondary service interaction.

Solutions We Sell

Refunds (non-batch)

Horizon non-batch refunds covers individual, admin-initiated refund processing for credit balances resulting from overpayment, withdrawal credits, financial aid disbursements, or institutional adjustments — processed one at a time rather than in bulk.

Manual Refund Processing

As a bursar admin / finance admin

Admin-Initiated Refund. Institution admins with refund permission must be able to initiate a refund on a student account that has a credit balance. The admin must specify: refund amount (up to the credit balance), refund method (original card, ACH to saved bank account, or flag for check issuance), and a refund reason code for internal reconciliation. The system must validate that the refund amount does not exceed the credit balance and that the selected method is available (card on file is within refund window, bank account is saved).

Why: Individual refund situations — a student withdraws, a scholarship is applied retroactively, an admin makes a billing correction — cannot wait for the next batch refund cycle. Same-day or next-day refund capability for admin-initiated cases is a baseline expectation for bursar offices.

Student-Requested Refund (Configurable). Where institution configuration permits, students with a credit balance must be able to request a refund directly from the consumer portal. The request must specify the refund method (card, ACH to saved account) and must be subject to any institution-configured approval workflow before processing. An approval workflow allows a finance admin to review the request before it is processed — useful for institutions where credit balances require verification before disbursement.

Why: Allowing students to self-request refunds reduces the inbound volume to the bursar office for what is otherwise a routine action. Institutional control over whether self-service refunds require approval preserves the institution's ability to verify credit balance legitimacy before disbursing funds.

As a finance admin

Refund Status Tracking & Communication. Every refund — whether admin-initiated or student-requested — must have a visible status lifecycle: Pending → Processing → Sent → Completed (or Failed). Students must be notified at each status transition via the platform's correspondence system. The admin must have a real-time refund status view in the admin interface. Failed refunds must be immediately surfaced with the failure reason and a clear remediation path.

Why: "Where is my refund?" is one of the highest-volume student service inquiries at any institution. A visible status lifecycle with proactive student communication eliminates the majority of these inquiries without requiring any staff involvement — converting a high-touch support interaction into a self-service information lookup.

Solutions We Sell

PayPal & Venmo Payments

PayPal and Venmo as consumer payment methods for one-time balance payments. A contractual commitment to Big Ten and Big 12 member institutions and a meaningful revenue opportunity given the high adoption of these wallets among the 18–25 demographic.

Acceptance & Method Selection

Institution Admin

Institution-Configurable Wallet Enablement. Institution admins can independently enable or disable PayPal and Venmo as accepted payment methods. Each wallet can be toggled separately; enabling one does not require enabling the other.

Why: Not all institutions will have the same contractual or compliance posture toward each wallet; independent control avoids forcing institutions to accept both as a bundle.

Student / Consumer

Wallet Selection and Authorization Redirect. When one or both wallets are enabled, PayPal and Venmo appear as payment method options alongside ACH and card in the one-time payment flow. The consumer selects their preferred wallet and is redirected to the respective PayPal or Venmo authorization UI. After the consumer authorizes the payment, they are returned to the Horizon payment confirmation screen. The full payment amount and institution context are preserved through the redirect so the consumer is not required to re-enter any information upon return.

Why: The redirect-and-return pattern is the standard PayPal/Venmo integration model; preserving payment context through the redirect removes friction that would otherwise cause consumers to abandon the flow upon return.

Service Fee Handling

Institution Admin

Institution-Configured PayPal/Venmo Service Fee. Institution admins configure the service fee rate for PayPal and Venmo payments, typically set to the same rate as the credit card service fee. Institutions can also configure whether ACH-funded PayPal transactions qualify for a lower fee rate and, if so, what that rate is.

Why: PayPal transaction costs to the institution vary based on the funding source; allowing institutions to pass through a differentiated rate for ACH-funded PayPal transactions avoids charging consumers a card-equivalent fee for a lower-cost transaction.

Student / Consumer

Pre-Authorization Fee Disclosure and Receipt Line Item. The service fee is disclosed to the consumer before they authorize the payment in the PayPal or Venmo UI. On the payment receipt, the service fee is shown as a separate line item distinct from the balance payment amount.

Why: Pre-authorization disclosure is required for regulatory compliance and consumer trust; a separate receipt line item ensures consumers can distinguish the service fee from the payment applied to their balance.

Settlement & Reconciliation

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

PayPal Merchant Settlement API and ERP Trigger. PayPal and Venmo settlements are received via PayPal's merchant settlement API. ERP write-back triggers on settlement confirmation — not on consumer authorization — consistent with the platform's settlement-based posting model. Settlement timing for PayPal/Venmo is typically T+1 compared to T+2 for card; the platform handles both settlement cadences within the same ERP posting pipeline.

Why: Triggering ERP posting on authorization rather than settlement would result in postings for payments that may not ultimately fund; settlement-based posting ensures the ledger reflects confirmed funds.

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

ERP Transmission Report Inclusion. PayPal and Venmo settlements are included in the ERP Transmission Report (URS-ERP-01) with a payment method type value of "PayPal" or "Venmo" respectively, enabling institution finance teams to identify and reconcile wallet-funded payments distinctly from card and ACH settlements.

Why: Finance teams need to reconcile wallet settlements against PayPal's merchant settlement statements; a distinct payment method type in the ERP report provides the necessary identifier for that reconciliation.

Refunds via PayPal / Venmo

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

PayPal API Refund Processing. Refunds for PayPal and Venmo payments are processed back through the PayPal merchant API to the consumer's PayPal or Venmo balance. Institution admins initiate PayPal/Venmo refunds from the same refund workflow used for card refunds; no separate refund interface is required. The PayPal merchant refund window is 180 days from the original transaction date.

Why: Routing refunds back through PayPal ensures the consumer receives funds in the same wallet they used to pay; a unified refund workflow reduces training overhead for Finance Admins.

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

Out-of-Window Refund Handling. Refund requests for PayPal or Venmo payments more than 180 days after the original transaction date cannot be processed through the PayPal API. The platform surfaces a clear message to the admin identifying the out-of-window condition and indicating that the refund must be processed via a manual off-platform method.

Why: Attempting to submit an out-of-window refund through the API will fail; surfacing a clear message at initiation prevents failed API calls and ensures the admin knows immediately that a manual process is required.

Institutional Eligibility

Institution Admin / NBS Sales

Horizon Contract Requirement and Initial Cohort Rollout. PayPal and Venmo are available only to institutions on the Horizon payment platform contract that have enabled the feature. Initial rollout is limited to Big Ten and Big 12 member institutions pursuant to contractual commitment. General availability to other eligible institutions follows after the initial cohort has been validated in production.

Why: Contractual obligations to the Big Ten and Big 12 require that these institutions receive the capability at launch; limiting initial rollout to the committed cohort allows the platform to validate the integration at scale before broader release.

Institution Admin / Product

Pay Over Time Exclusion in Initial Release. PayPal and Venmo may not be used for Pay Over Time plan installment payments in the initial release. The wallets are available exclusively for one-time balance payments. Installment payment support via PayPal/Venmo is a deferred capability, not in scope for the initial contractual commitment.

Why: Pay Over Time installments involve recurring payment authorization patterns that require additional PayPal API capabilities beyond the one-time payment authorization model; deferring installment support scopes the initial release to a technically and contractually achievable scope.
