The imported data must include: student ID (resolved to Horizon account), charge type and code, charge amount, effective date, due date, and any existing credits or payments on the account. The sync must support delta updates (only changed records) to minimize processing overhead at scale.

Why: If Horizon shows a stale balance — especially when charges have been added or credits applied since the last sync — students lose confidence in the platform and call the bursar to verify, defeating the purpose of self-service. Real-time or near-real-time sync is a consumer experience requirement, not just a technical nicety.

Enrollment Status Feed. Horizon must receive enrollment status updates from the ERP to determine which students are currently enrolled, their enrollment level (full-time/part-time), and their enrollment period. This feed drives eligibility for payment plan enrollment, hold release logic, and communication suppression rules. Enrollment status changes (withdrawal, leave of absence, re-enrollment) must be reflected in Horizon within the configured sync window.

Why: Allowing a withdrawn student to enroll in a new payment plan for charges they are no longer incurring creates confusion and potential disputes. Enrollment status drives core plan eligibility logic and must be kept current.

Payment Write-Back. Every payment processed through Horizon must be written back to the institution's ERP as a payment transaction against the originating charge(s). Write-backs must occur within the configured settlement window and must include: payment amount, payment date, payment method type, Horizon transaction reference, and the charge codes being reduced. The write-back must be idempotent — duplicate write-back attempts for the same transaction must not result in double-credit.

Why: The original receivable remains on the institution's books (this is the fundamental difference between Horizon payment plans and a loan model). Accurate, timely write-backs keep the ERP balance current so that financial holds can be released, transcripts can be unlocked, and future-term registration can proceed — all of which are direct student outcomes tied to payment plan adoption.

Platform Requirements

3rd Party Integration

API standards, webhook architecture, and certified partner integrations beyond the core ERP/SIS ecosystem — covering analytics vendors, communication platforms, collections partners, and custom institution integrations.

API Standards & Architecture

RESTful API with OpenAPI Specification. All Horizon platform capabilities that are accessible externally must be exposed through a versioned RESTful API documented with an OpenAPI 3.x specification. The API must use OAuth 2.0 / OIDC for authentication, support JSON request and response bodies, and follow standard HTTP status code semantics. Breaking API changes must follow a deprecation policy with minimum 6-month notice before a version is retired.

Why: Institutions and integration partners need predictable, documented API contracts to build against. Undocumented or inconsistently versioned APIs create brittle integrations that break on platform updates — eroding trust and generating support tickets. An OpenAPI spec enables partner self-service integration and automated SDK generation.

Webhook Event System. The platform must support outbound webhooks for all significant platform events — payment processed, payment failed, plan enrolled, plan terminated, balance updated, student account created, hold applied/released. Webhooks must be configurable per institution, support HMAC signature verification, provide retry with exponential backoff on delivery failure, and include a delivery log accessible to NBS technical support.

Why: Push-based webhooks enable real-time integrations without polling. Institutions that build internal dashboards, alert systems, or custom workflows on top of Horizon events need reliable delivery guarantees. HMAC verification prevents spoofed webhook events from triggering financial actions.

Collections & Debt Management Partners

External Collections Agency Handoff. When a student account is referred to an external collection agency, Horizon must support a standardized data handoff including: student contact information, balance breakdown, history of payment plan activity and terminations, communication history, and any legal disclosures previously sent. The handoff format must be compatible with common collections agency intake systems. Horizon must also receive status updates back from the agency (payment received, settled, disputed) to keep the institution's ERP balance current.

Why: The collections escalation path is a defined phase in the institution process flow. A clean handoff reduces the manual data preparation burden on bursar staff and ensures the agency has the complete picture needed to pursue the account effectively. Bidirectional status updates prevent the ERP from showing a balance as outstanding after the collections agency has negotiated a settlement.

Integration Certification & Partner Program

Integration Certification Process. NBS must maintain a documented integration certification process for third-party partners (ERP vendors, communication platforms, analytics tools, collections agencies) who want to build certified integrations with Horizon. Certification must verify: correct API usage, appropriate data handling (FERPA, PCI, TCPA compliance), and consistent behavior on platform updates. Certified integrations must be listed in a publicly accessible partner directory to support institution evaluation and sales.

Why: As Horizon grows, NBS cannot build and maintain every integration internally. A certification program creates a scalable partner ecosystem that expands Horizon's integration breadth without proportional NBS engineering investment. The partner directory is also a sales tool — institutions frequently ask "does this integrate with X?" before making a purchasing decision.

Reporting Needs

Institution User Reporting Needs

What institution finance and student services teams need to see — operational, compliance, and strategic reporting that runs within the institution's Horizon admin experience.

Operational Reporting

As a bursar / finance admin

Daily Payment Activity Report. A report showing all payments processed in a given date range: student name, student ID, payment amount, payment method, plan name (if plan payment), transaction status, and settlement date. Must be filterable by date range, payment method, plan type, and campus. Must be exportable to CSV and PDF. Must be available by 8am on the next business day.

Why: This is the primary daily reconciliation tool for bursar staff. Without it, they cannot verify that Horizon settlements match their GL entries or confirm that student payments are being applied correctly.

As a bursar / finance admin

Payment Plan Enrollment Report. A report showing all active payment plans: student name, student ID, plan type, plan start/end date, original plan amount, amount paid to date, amount remaining, next payment date, and plan status (active, in jeopardy, defaulted). Must support filtering by term, plan type, enrollment status, and delinquency status. Must be exportable to CSV.

Why: Finance teams need to project cash flow from payment plans each month. The enrollment report feeds that projection and also surfaces at-risk plans before they default — enabling proactive outreach that recovers accounts before they reach collections.

As a bursar / finance admin

Outstanding Balance Report. A report showing all students with an outstanding balance above a configurable threshold: student ID, total balance, balance by charge type, enrollment status, whether they have an active payment plan, and days since last payment. Must support filtering by enrollment status, balance range, campus, and plan status. Intended for proactive outreach and collections referral workflow.

Why: Identifying accounts approaching the collections referral threshold before they cross it enables timely intervention — a phone call or targeted communication can recover an account that a collections referral would make significantly harder and more expensive to resolve.

As a finance admin

Term Reconciliation Report. At the close of each term, a report showing: total charges assessed, total paid via Horizon, total in active plans, total referred to collections, total written off, and net remaining. Comparable against prior term for trend analysis. Must include payment method breakdown (ACH vs. card) and plan type breakdown. Serves as the primary term-close financial reconciliation document.

Why: Term-end reconciliation is a required accounting process. Institutions that cannot reconcile Horizon activity against their ERP at term close will manually re-verify every transaction — a significant labor cost that erodes the platform's value proposition.

Compliance & Audit Reporting

As a compliance officer / finance admin

Audit Log Export. All admin actions within the institution's Horizon tenant must be logged with: action type, actor (user name + role), timestamp, affected student/account, before/after values for changed fields. The audit log must be exportable and must be retained for a minimum of 7 years. Institutions subject to external audit must be able to provide a clean export without NBS involvement.

Why: Higher education institutions are subject to federal financial aid audits, state attorney general inquiries, and internal audit processes. An institution that cannot produce a complete audit trail of financial transactions and admin actions is in a materially worse position in any regulatory investigation.

As a compliance / student services admin

Financial Responsibility Agreement Completion Report. A report showing which students have and have not completed the FRA for the current term, with completion date, version signed, and delivery method. Required for institutions that condition registration on FRA completion. Must be filterable by enrollment status and term.

Why: The FRA is a legal document that establishes the institution's right to collect and to impose the fees and practices described in this PRD. Institutions need to verify and document FRA completion for risk management and potential litigation contexts.

Reporting Needs

Unified Reporting Suite (URS)

The Unified Reporting Suite is Horizon's embedded reporting platform — eight named operational reports plus the technical architecture that powers them. URS is the primary data access layer for institution finance teams, NBS account managers, and compliance staff. Reports are delivered in-app with CSV/PDF export; the architecture is event-driven and audit-immutable.

Payments & Transactions

As a bursar / finance admin

Daily Payment Activity Report (URS-PAY-01). A real-time-updatable report of all payment transactions within a configurable date range. Required columns: student name, student ID, payment date, payment amount, payment method (ACH / card / check / cash), transaction status (settled / pending / returned / failed), plan name if plan payment, campus/school code, and GL account code mapping where configured. Filters: date range, payment method, transaction status, plan type, campus. Sort: date (default), amount, student name. Export: CSV and PDF. Availability SLA: all transactions from the prior business day must appear by 8am local institution time.

Why: This is the bursar's daily reconciliation instrument. Every day, accounts receivable staff compare Horizon settlements to their GL. A missing transaction or misclassified payment method creates a reconciliation gap that cascades into the month-end close. The 8am SLA aligns with the start of the bursar's workday — if the report isn't ready when staff arrive, they start their day behind.

As a bursar / finance admin

Failed & Returned Payments Report (URS-PAY-02). A targeted report covering all failed, returned (NSF), and reversed transactions within a configurable date range. Required columns: student name, student ID, original payment date, original amount, failure/return date, failure reason code (NSF, invalid account, card declined, stop payment, etc.), current account balance, whether the student is on an active plan, and next scheduled payment date if applicable. The report must support bulk re-notification — Finance Admins can select multiple records and trigger a communication to all selected students simultaneously. Filters: date range, failure reason, plan status. Recommended action column: "Schedule follow-up / Re-attempt / Refer to collections" based on failure count and account history.

Why: Returned payments are the primary leading indicator of plan default and collections escalation. Institutions that identify and act on NSF events within 24–48 hours recover more accounts than those who let them age. The bulk re-notification capability is what makes the report operational rather than just informational — staff shouldn't have to manually contact 50 students one at a time from the report view.

As a finance admin / NBS account manager

Settlement & Disbursement Summary Report (URS-PAY-03). A periodic (daily, weekly, monthly configurable) summary of net settlement activity: total payments collected, total refunds issued, total NSF reversals, net disbursement to institution, Horizon service fees withheld, and net amount remitted. For guarantee plan institutions: includes guarantee reserve balance and any guarantee claim amounts. Must reconcile to the institution's bank statement and to NBS revenue reporting. Exportable as CSV (for GL import) and PDF (for treasury/finance director review). Month-end version must include prior-period comparison column.

Why: Settlement reconciliation is a required accounting control. Institutions need to verify that the amount hitting their bank account matches what Horizon reports as remitted. The fee-withheld column is important for GL allocation — service fees are a separate expense line from collected tuition. Guarantee reserve visibility is a specific requirement for guarantee plan clients who carry contingent liability on their books for the reserve balance.

Agreements & Scheduled Activity

As a bursar / finance admin

Payment Plan Enrollment & Status Report (URS-AGR-01). A comprehensive view of all payment plans — active, completed, defaulted, and cancelled — within a configurable term and date range. Required columns: student name, student ID, plan type, plan start date, plan end date, original plan amount, total paid, total remaining, scheduled payment count, payments made, payments missed, next payment date, plan status, and campus. Status values: Active (current), In Jeopardy (1 missed payment), At Risk (2+ missed payments), Defaulted (plan terminated for non-payment), Cancelled (admin-cancelled), Completed (paid in full). Filters: term, plan type, status, campus, delinquency band. Export: CSV. Used for cash flow projection, proactive outreach, and term-end reconciliation.

Why: Cash flow projection from payment plans is a primary financial planning input for institutions — many institutions fund operations partially on the assumption that enrolled plan balances will be collected over the term. A plan enrollment report that surfaces the at-risk cohort before they default allows proactive intervention that improves the projection's accuracy. The status taxonomy (In Jeopardy / At Risk / Defaulted) is a specific request from NBS account managers who found that clients using only "active/defaulted" couldn't identify deteriorating plans early enough to act.

As a bursar / finance admin

Upcoming Scheduled Payments Report (URS-AGR-02). A forward-looking report of all scheduled payment plan payments due within a configurable future window (7, 14, 30, 60 days). Required columns: student name, student ID, plan type, scheduled payment date, scheduled payment amount, payment method on file (ACH / card / last 4), whether a prior payment was returned for this student, and account standing. The report must flag accounts where the payment method on file has expired or is about to expire (card expiration within 30 days). Filters: date range, payment method type, campus. Used for pre-payment outreach and payment method health monitoring.

Why: Expired payment methods are a preventable cause of returned payments and plan defaults. Institutions that proactively prompt students to update expiring cards 2–3 weeks before the scheduled payment have measurably lower NSF rates than those who only discover expired cards at time of charge. This report is the operational instrument for that proactive approach. It also supports staffing decisions — a bursar manager can see that a large cohort of payments is scheduled for a specific week and ensure adequate coverage.

As a finance admin / compliance officer

Financial Responsibility Agreement Completion Report (URS-AGR-03). A report of all students who have been presented with the institution's Financial Responsibility Agreement, their completion status, the FRA version they were presented, and the date/method of completion. Required columns: student name, student ID, enrollment term, FRA version, presentation date, completion date, completion method (digital signature / in-person / mail), and whether completion is required for registration. Students with outstanding FRA requirements who are also registered for upcoming classes must be flagged. Filters: term, FRA version, completion status, enrollment status. Export: CSV and PDF. Minimum retention: 7 years.

Why: The FRA is the institution's legal basis for the fees, collection practices, and hold policies described in this PRD. An institution that cannot produce signed FRA records for a specific student in a collections dispute or regulatory inquiry is in an extremely weak legal position. This report provides the operational monitoring layer (who hasn't signed yet, before the registration deadline) and the long-term documentation layer (signed copies tied to specific versions).

Billing & Outstanding Balances

As a bursar / finance admin

Outstanding Balance & Aging Report (URS-BILL-01). A report of all student accounts with an outstanding balance above a configurable threshold (default: $1), organized by aging bucket: current (0–30 days), 31–60 days, 61–90 days, 91–180 days, 180+ days. Required columns: student name, student ID, total balance, balance by charge type, enrollment status, whether the student has an active payment plan, days since last payment, date of last contact attempt, and whether the account has been referred to collections. Filters: balance range, aging bucket, enrollment status, plan status, campus. Sort: balance descending (default), aging bucket, enrollment status. Export: CSV. This report feeds the collections escalation workflow.

Why: Aging report visibility is the most requested reporting feature in every bursar conversation NBS has conducted. Without it, institutions are flying blind on their receivables position — they don't know whether their portfolio is getting better or worse until they do a manual GL extract, which is time-consuming and usually only happens at month-end. Real-time aging visibility enables daily prioritization of the accounts most at risk of aging past the collections referral threshold.

As a finance admin

Term Reconciliation & Closing Report (URS-BILL-02). A term-close summary report for finance directors and controllers. Required metrics: total charges assessed in the term, total payments collected via Horizon, total enrolled in active plans, total plan payments received vs. scheduled, total plan defaults, total referred to collections, total written off, net remaining outstanding. All metrics must include prior-term comparison and percent change. Charge type breakdown (tuition / housing / fees / other). Payment method breakdown (ACH / card / cash / other). Plan type breakdown. GL account mapping summary for institutions using Horizon GL codes. Available by the 3rd business day after the institution's configured term close date. Export: PDF (for executive review) and CSV (for GL reconciliation import).

Why: Term-close reconciliation is a required accounting process — auditors, controllers, and CFOs need a clean summary of the term's financial activity. Institutions that have to manually compile this from multiple Horizon report exports and ERP data are spending significant staff time on a report that Horizon should produce automatically. The GL mapping summary is specific to institutions that use Horizon's charge codes as a passthrough to their accounting system.

Technical Architecture

Event-Driven Report Data Pipeline. All URS report data must be powered by an event-driven data pipeline, not synchronous database queries against the operational database. Every financial event in Horizon — payment processed, plan enrolled, plan cancelled, NSF returned, refund issued, balance updated — must emit a structured event to the reporting pipeline with a full payload (event type, timestamp, actor, affected accounts, before/after state). The reporting layer materializes views from these events. This architecture ensures: (1) report generation does not impact operational system performance; (2) reports reflect the state of the system at any point in time (event replay); (3) the pipeline itself serves as the audit-immutable event log.

Why: Running complex aggregation queries against the operational database at scale — especially at term-end when hundreds of institutions may be generating reports simultaneously — causes performance degradation that affects real-time student transactions. Event-driven architecture decouples reporting load from operational load. Event replay capability means URS can regenerate any historical report from the event log even if reporting tables are corrupted or reset — a critical disaster recovery capability for financial reporting.

Immutable Audit Trail. The event log powering URS must be write-once, append-only, and cryptographically tamper-evident. Once an event is written, it cannot be modified or deleted — corrections must be recorded as new compensating events (e.g., a refund that reverses a payment is a new event referencing the original, not a modification of the original payment record). The tamper-evidence mechanism must be verifiable by an external auditor without NBS involvement. Retention: minimum 7 years for all financial event types, minimum 10 years for FRA completion events.

Why: Financial reporting integrity depends on the underlying event log being unalterable. A tamper-evident log is not just a security feature — it is the foundation of the institution's ability to defend its financial practices in litigation, regulatory inquiry, or audit. The distinction between immutable records and compensating events is the standard accounting principle of non-erasure: you don't erase a mistake, you record the correction. External verifiability means institutions can commission independent audits of Horizon data without waiting for NBS to produce certified exports.

Report Scheduling & Delivery. All URS reports must support scheduled delivery: Finance Admins can configure any report to run automatically on a daily, weekly, or monthly schedule and deliver the result to one or more email recipients (institution users only — external addresses not permitted). Scheduled reports must include a run timestamp and a record count in the delivery email so recipients can confirm completeness before opening the export. Failed scheduled deliveries must generate an alert to the Full Admin and retry up to 3 times within a 4-hour window before generating a support ticket. Scheduled delivery configuration must be logged in the audit trail.

Why: Many bursar workflows depend on having a fresh report at the start of each day or week — staff check their email for the daily payment activity report before opening Horizon. Without scheduled delivery, the report only provides value to staff who remember to generate it manually. Scheduled delivery converts URS from a passive lookup tool to an active part of the institution's daily financial operations workflow.

Cross-Institution Reporting for NBS (Portfolio View). NBS account managers and operations staff must have access to a cross-institution aggregated reporting layer that surfaces portfolio-level metrics without requiring access to individual institution tenants. Portfolio metrics must include: active plan count and enrolled amount by institution, payment success rate by institution (trailing 90 days), delinquency rate by institution, NSF rate by institution, plan default rate by institution, average plan enrollment amount by plan type, and institution-level trend data (current term vs. prior term). NBS-internal portfolio reporting must be completely isolated from institution-facing reporting — institution admins must never see data from other institutions.

Why: NBS account managers need portfolio-level visibility to identify at-risk clients, prepare for QBRs, and benchmark client performance. Without this layer, AMs either have to log into each institution tenant individually (operationally unsustainable at scale) or wait for a data warehouse export (too slow for operational decisions). Isolation from institution-facing reporting is a contractual and regulatory requirement — institutions have confidentiality expectations about their operational data.

Data Export API. All URS reports must be accessible via an authenticated REST API in addition to the in-app UI. The export API must support: parameterized queries (date range, filters matching the UI filters), pagination for large result sets, JSON and CSV response formats, and OAuth 2.0 authentication scoped to the institution's credentials. The API enables institutions to build their own downstream integrations — GL import automation, custom dashboards, BI tools (Tableau, Power BI). API access must be logged (which report, which date range, which credential, timestamp) in the audit trail. Rate limiting: 100 requests/minute per institution credential; burst allowance for term-end peaks configurable by NBS.

Why: Larger institutions have data engineering teams who want to pull Horizon data directly into their data warehouse or BI tools rather than manually downloading CSV exports. An export API is the path from URS being an isolated reporting tool to Horizon being a data platform integrated into the institution's broader analytics infrastructure. The rate limit with term-end burst allowance balances API availability against the risk of a runaway integration hammering the reporting layer during peak load.

Unified Transaction & Remittance Reports

As a bursar / finance admin

Unified Transaction Report (URS-TXN-01). A single consolidated view of all financial transactions across all payment types and methods — card, ACH, international, manual, scheduled, refunds, and returns. Required columns: Transaction ID, timestamp, transaction type, provider, status, amount, posting date and time, return code and message (where applicable), payer identity (Student / AP / Guest), payment method details, Agreement ID if the transaction is plan-related, institution, tenant, and term. Filters: date range, transaction type, status, institution, provider. UX flow: landing page → report → table → row click → detail view → export. This report supersedes the need to access multiple system-specific exports for daily reconciliation — all transactions appear in one place.

Why: Today institutions rely on disconnected system exports from Payment Platform, Enterprise, QuickPay, and Refunds — each with different formats. Daily reconciliation requires stitching these together manually. A single unified transaction report eliminates that workflow and is the highest-priority URS report for reducing reconciliation support tickets.

As a bursar / finance admin

Remittance Report (URS-REM-01). A reconciliation report that matches posted transactions to disbursements sent to the institution. Required columns: Transaction ID, Batch ID, amount processed, amount disbursed, settlement status (Matched / Variance / Pending), provider reference, and bank confirmation reference. Drilldown must show: the variance amount and reason when settlement status is Variance, and the source transactions contributing to the settlement batch. Filters: date range, settlement status, institution. The remittance report is the primary instrument for identifying cases where the amount hitting the institution's bank account does not match the sum of processed transactions.

Why: Remittance mismatches currently require engineering support to investigate — there is no self-service path for institutions to identify why their bank deposit differs from their transaction total. Every institution experiences occasional variances due to fee withholding timing, returned payment clawbacks, and batch processing cutoffs. A self-service remittance report eliminates the engineering escalation path and gives finance teams the tool to investigate and resolve mismatches independently.

Billing, Insurance & Refund Reports

As a billing administrator

Billing Generation Summary (URS-BILL-03). A report supporting institutions and NBS internal billing operations teams in verifying invoice generation and billing totals for each billing cycle. Required columns: Invoice ID, billing period, invoice amount, fees, tax, status (Generated / Sent / Paid), aging bucket, and institution. Filters: billing period, institution. The billing generation summary surfaces discrepancies between expected invoice totals and generated actuals before invoices are sent to students, giving billing operations a quality-check step in the workflow.

Why: Billing data is currently fragmented across systems, making it difficult for billing administrators to verify that the correct students received invoices for the correct amounts in any given billing cycle. Errors found after invoices are sent require corrections that erode student trust. The pre-send quality-check enabled by this report reduces billing errors and the volume of student inquiries about incorrect invoices.

As an institution admin / compliance officer

Tuition Insurance Report (URS-INS-01). A report providing institutions with visibility into which students are enrolled in tuition insurance and relevant policy and coverage details. Required columns: Student ID, student name, coverage amount, insurance fee or premium paid, enrollment status, and any refunds or cancellations processed on the insurance policy. The report supports compliance use cases (verifying insurance enrollment for students in coverage-required programs), refund validation (confirming insurance premiums were correctly reversed on withdrawal), and policy auditing (validating that coverage amounts align with tuition charges).

Why: Tuition insurance administration requires accurate enrollment records — an institution that cannot verify which students have coverage and at what amount cannot fulfill its disclosure obligations to students or its contractual obligations to the insurance carrier. Institutions have also requested this report specifically for refund audits, where they need to confirm that insurance premium reversals were processed correctly when students withdrew.

As a bursar / NBS operations

Bulk Refund Status Report (URS-REF-01). A report giving institutions and NBS operations teams visibility into the status of bulk refund file executions. Required columns: Refund Batch ID, total refund requests in the batch, successful count, failed count, pending count, failure reasons by count, and affected transaction IDs. Row-level drilldown must show individual refund detail within a batch — student ID, refund amount, status, and failure reason if failed. Filters: date range, batch status, institution. The report must be available immediately after a batch file is processed, not on a nightly delay.

Why: Bulk refund file execution currently lacks transparency — institutions submit a refund file and then wait for NBS support to tell them how many succeeded and why some failed. Failed refunds that go unaddressed result in student complaints, registration hold disputes, and potential regulatory exposure if refund obligations are not met within required timeframes. Real-time visibility into bulk refund status enables institutions to take immediate corrective action on failures.

Student & Authorized Party Relationship Report

As a bursar / institution admin

Student–AP Relationship Report (URS-AP-01). An exportable, authoritative record of all Student–Authorized Party relationships within the institution's tenant. Student columns: Student ID, student name, institution, term. Authorized Party columns: AP ID, name, email, phone, account status (Invited / Created / Logged In), last login timestamp. Relationship columns: creation date, access level granted, relationship initiator (student / AP / admin). Engagement indicator columns: whether the AP has a payment plan (yes/no and count), whether the AP has ever made a payment (yes/no and last payment date). Filters: student, AP, has-logged-in status, has-payment-plan status. Export: CSV for SIS/ERP sync. Primary use case: institutions that manage AP contact lists in their SIS need to sync this data without manual extraction.

Why: AP relationship data currently lives only inside the platform with no institutional export path. Institutions that want to verify AP contact information, audit relationship changes, or sync AP data to their SIS are forced to screen-scrape or contact NBS support. This report solves that data portability gap. The engagement indicators (has made a payment, last login) are specifically useful for identifying APs who were invited but never activated — a cohort institutions want to target with re-engagement outreach.

Power BI Delivery & Report UX

Power BI Embedded in Existing Framework. URS reports must be delivered as Power BI dashboards embedded within Horizon's existing reporting framework — not as separate external links or standalone tools. Each of the eight MVP reports must appear on a URS landing page organized into three categories: (A) Payments & Transactions — Unified Transaction Report, Remittance Report, Bulk Refund Status Report; (B) Agreements & Scheduled Activity — Payment Plan Agreement Report, Scheduled Payment Volume Report, Student & Authorized Party Relationship Report; (C) Billing, Insurance — Billing Generation Summary, Tuition Insurance Report. Clicking any report tile opens the dedicated Power BI page for that report.

Why: Embedding within the existing framework avoids sending users to a separate tool they need to authenticate into independently. The three-category landing page structure mirrors how bursar and finance teams mentally organize their work — transaction-level, agreement-level, and billing-level — which reduces cognitive load and time to the right report.

Report UX Standards. Every URS report must follow a consistent UX pattern: filters at the top (matching the filter options specified per-report), primary data table as the main view, optional summary metrics section (counts, totals, rates) above the table where applicable, row-level drillthrough to detail view for reports that support it (Payment Plan Agreement, Remittance, Bulk Refund, Student-AP Relationship), and Export to CSV on all reports. Column naming must be standardized and consistent across reports where the same field appears in multiple reports (e.g., "Student ID" must mean the same field in all reports). Breadcrumb navigation must allow users to return to the URS landing page from any report without using the browser back button.

Why: Inconsistent UX across reports — different filter placements, different column names for the same concept — creates retraining burden and erodes trust in the data. Bursar staff who use multiple URS reports daily will make fewer errors and find answers faster when the interaction model is predictable. The breadcrumb requirement addresses a common complaint with embedded BI tools: the browser back button navigates out of the Horizon app instead of back to the report landing page.

Performance Requirements. All URS reports must load within 3 seconds for result sets up to 50,000 rows. CSV export must complete within 15 seconds for any date range that returns data. Reports that commonly return large result sets (Unified Transaction Report, Plan Agreement Report) must use server-side pagination and must not require the full dataset to load before the first page of results is shown. Power BI dataset refresh cadence: hourly for MVP; near-real-time (under 5 minutes) is a future phase target and not required for MVP delivery.

Why: A report that takes 30+ seconds to load will not be used for daily reconciliation — bursar staff will revert to ERP exports or spreadsheets, defeating URS's purpose. The 3-second target is aggressive but achievable with proper dataset materialization and server-side pagination. Hourly refresh is an acceptable MVP tradeoff that enables launch while the near-real-time architecture is built out in subsequent phases.

Row-Level Security. Power BI row-level security must ensure that institution users can only see data from their own institution tenant. NBS-internal users accessing the cross-institution portfolio view must be on a separate report surface with a distinct permission scope. An institution finance admin must not be able to see data from any other institution — even accidentally, such as if an RLS misconfiguration allows cross-tenant filter manipulation. RLS configuration must be validated as part of every URS release deployment, not just at initial setup.

Why: Cross-tenant data leakage in a reporting tool would be a critical privacy and contractual violation. Institutions share sensitive student financial data with NBS with an expectation of strict confidentiality. Mandatory RLS validation at every release closes the gap where a passing release could introduce an RLS regression that goes undetected until a user accidentally sees another institution's data.

URS Scope, Non-Goals & Success Metrics

MVP Explicit Non-Goals. The following capabilities are explicitly NOT included in the URS MVP and must not be committed to clients or designed into initial architecture in ways that would need to be undone: dashboards requiring Notify or engagement data; cross-product analytics across Enterprise or QuickPay; fraud or exception dashboards; executive KPI summaries; custom report builder; real-time refresh under 5 minutes; forecasting, projections, or AI predictions; visual-heavy dashboards (MVP is table-forward with simple summary metrics only). These are future phase targets, not deferrals of MVP scope.

Why: Explicit non-goals prevent scope creep during implementation and prevent sales from over-committing to clients. Each item in the non-goals list was discussed and deliberately deferred — documenting them explicitly prevents them from being re-introduced as "quick adds" during development sprints. The table-forward approach for MVP is a deliberate choice: bursar operations require precise data, not dashboards; deliver accuracy first, visualization second.

URS Success Metrics. URS MVP success is measured against five quantitative targets: (1) 95% adoption of the Transaction, Agreement, and Remittance reports within the first 90 days post-launch for all institutions on URS; (2) 30% reduction in reconciliation-related support tickets compared to the 90-day pre-launch baseline; (3) 40% reduction in NBS internal billing operations manual data pulls; (4) 99% export success rate across all report types and date ranges; (5) average Power BI report load time under 3 seconds measured at p95. These metrics must be instrumented at launch — report usage, export attempts, and load time must be captured by the telemetry layer so actuals can be compared to targets at the 90-day mark.

Why: Success metrics without instrumentation are aspirational statements, not measurable targets. The 30% support ticket reduction is particularly important — it is the primary business case for URS investment. If support tickets do not decline, it suggests either that the reports are not being used, or that they are being used but not solving the reconciliation problems institutions are calling about. Either failure mode needs to be identified quickly so it can be addressed before renewal conversations.

URS Phased Delivery Sequencing. URS must be delivered in three sequential phases: Phase 1 (8–10 weeks) covers data lake ingestion for all MVP fields plus four reports — Unified Transaction Report, Payment Plan Agreement Report, Scheduled Payment Volume Report, and Student & Authorized Party Relationship Report. Phase 2 (6–8 weeks) adds the Remittance Report and Bulk Refund Status Report. Phase 3 (6–8 weeks) completes the MVP with the Billing Generation Summary and Tuition Insurance Report plus landing page category UI polish. Future phases address Notify and engagement analytics, fraud dashboards, executive KPIs, custom report builder, dashboard personalization, multi-product unified dashboards, and predictive insights. Phase sequencing is based on operational impact and data availability — the Phase 1 reports serve the highest daily-use cases for bursar teams.

Why: Phased delivery serves three purposes: it allows NBS to deliver immediate value while longer data ingestion pipelines are built; it allows institution users to adopt a smaller surface before the full suite launches (reducing training burden); and it creates defined checkpoints for NBS to validate that Phase 1 reports meet quality and performance standards before extending the architecture to additional report types. The Phase 1 prioritization reflects direct feedback from bursar users that transaction visibility and plan agreement status are the most urgent daily needs.

Plan Reports & ERP Transmission

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

Agreement Report (URS-AGREE-01). Institution users can generate a report of all Pay Over Time plan agreements for a specified term. Each row shows: student ID, plan type, enrolled date, covered balance, total installments, and enrollment status (active, cancelled, completed, defaulted). The report is available in CSV and PDF formats and is filterable by plan type, enrollment date range, and enrollment status.

Why: Institutions need a term-level reconciliation artifact for audits, accreditation reporting, and internal finance review; the agreement report is the authoritative record of plan commitments made in a given period.

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

Future Scheduled Payments Report (URS-SCHED-01). Institution users can generate a report of all upcoming installment payments not yet processed across all active plans for their institution. Each row shows: student ID, plan name, installment date, installment amount, and payment method type (card or ACH). The lookout window is configurable by the user at run time (7, 14, 30, 60, or 90 days).

Why: Cash-flow forecasting requires institutions to know the expected inflow from plan installments in a forward-looking window; this report gives treasury teams the inputs needed to manage daily and weekly cash positions.

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

ERP Transmission Report (URS-ERP-01). Institution users can access an audit log of all ERP write-back attempts, including: payment amount, charge type, student ID, ERP posting date and time, posting status (success, error, or pending), and ERP transaction reference. Failed postings are visually highlighted. Institution Finance Admins can initiate a retry of failed postings directly from the report UI without requiring NBS support intervention.

Why: ERP posting failures create student account discrepancies that directly impact collections and financial aid eligibility; a self-service retry capability reduces resolution time and removes NBS as a bottleneck for routine reconciliation.

Plan Reporting Technical Architecture

Platform / Engineering

Event-Driven Pipeline with 15-Minute Lag SLA. Plan reports (URS-AGREE-01, URS-SCHED-01, URS-ERP-01) are generated from the same event-driven, append-only data pipeline used for all other URS reports. Agreement and schedule reports must reflect a data state no older than 15 minutes from the operational system at the time of report generation.

Why: Architectural consistency with the existing URS pipeline avoids a parallel data infrastructure and ensures plan data is subject to the same data-quality controls as all other institutional reporting.

Platform / Engineering

Row-Level Security and Same-Day ERP Availability. All plan reports enforce row-level security so each institution can only access data for their own students. The ERP Transmission Report (URS-ERP-01) must be available and current on the same calendar day that payments process, ensuring it is usable as the primary reconciliation tool for institution finance teams on payment processing days.

Why: Multi-tenancy requires strict data isolation; same-day ERP report availability is required to support institution close-of-business reconciliation workflows that cannot wait until the following day.

Institution Admin / Finance Admin

Access via Power BI and Export API. All plan reports are accessible through the URS Power BI embedded interface and via the URS export API in both CSV and JSON formats, consistent with all other URS report delivery mechanisms.

Why: Institutions that have built downstream workflows against the URS export API expect plan data to be accessible through the same interface; requiring a separate access path would fragment the institutional data integration model.

Reporting Needs

NBS Reporting Needs

What NBS sales, implementation, account management, and operations teams need — client performance visibility, portfolio analytics, and operational health metrics.

Client Performance & Account Management

As an NBS account manager

Client Portfolio Dashboard. A cross-institution view accessible to NBS account managers showing: for each assigned client — active plans, total enrolled amount, payment success rate (last 90 days), delinquency rate, collections referral rate, and trend vs. prior term. Must support comparison between clients and benchmarking against portfolio average. Serves as the primary account health monitoring tool for AM quarterly business reviews.

Why: Account managers who can identify declining client performance before the client notices are in a fundamentally better renewal position than those reacting to client complaints. Early intervention on delinquency trends can also save NBS from guarantee-plan losses.

As an NBS sales / account manager

Adoption & Utilization Metrics. Per-institution metrics covering: payment plan adoption rate (plans enrolled / eligible students), self-service rate (payments made via consumer portal vs. admin-assisted), feature adoption (authorized parties set up, communications preferences configured, etc.), and comparison to peer institutions. This data supports renewal conversations and identifies upsell opportunities (e.g., an institution with zero hidden plan usage may not know the feature exists).

Why: Low adoption of Horizon self-service features translates directly into higher NBS support costs per institution. Identifying low-adoption patterns at the feature level gives account managers specific, actionable talking points for QBRs rather than generic "are you using the system?" conversations.

Operations & PAS Reporting

As an NBS PAS operations manager

PAS Processing Metrics. Daily and weekly reports on PAS-handled transactions: number of plans processed for re-enrollment, number of manual adjustments made, number of exception cases handled, processing time per institution, and error/exception rates. Must support comparison against SLA commitments and trend analysis week-over-week.

Why: PAS is a human-in-the-loop operation. Without visibility into processing volume and exception rates, NBS operations leadership cannot staff appropriately for term-end peaks or identify process failures before they generate client complaints.

As an NBS implementation manager

Implementation Progress Tracking. A view per institution in implementation: milestones completed vs. planned, current phase, blockers, days to go-live, and comparison against target timeline. Must be accessible to NBS implementation, account management, and executive team. Must generate alerts when an institution falls more than N days behind their go-live target.

Why: Implementation delays are the #1 source of client dissatisfaction during the onboarding period. Early visibility into slippage enables proactive escalation before a delay becomes a billing dispute or contract issue.

Financial & Revenue Reporting

As NBS finance

Revenue & Transaction Fee Reporting. Monthly reporting on transaction fees earned per institution, enrollment fees (where applicable), guarantee plan risk exposure, and projected revenue from active plan portfolios. Must reconcile against billing to institutions. Must include variance analysis for actuals vs. projected.

Why: NBS revenue from Horizon is driven by transaction volume and plan enrollment. Finance needs accurate, timely data to close the books, forecast future revenue, and identify clients where fee structure changes are needed at renewal.

Reporting Needs

IT & Product Success Metrics

How NBS IT and Product teams measure whether Horizon is working — user behavior analytics, infrastructure health, data platform monitoring, and delivery tracking. These are the instruments we use to know if the product is succeeding before clients tell us it isn't.

User Behavior & Feature Adoption — Pendo

Pendo Integration for Consumer Journeys. Horizon's consumer-facing experience must be instrumented with Pendo (or equivalent product analytics platform) to track: page-level engagement, feature interaction events (enrollment flow started, plan selected, payment method saved, authorized party added), funnel drop-off points, and session duration by user segment. Student cohorts should be tagged by institution, plan type, enrollment status, and returning vs. first-time user to support segmented analysis.

Why: Without behavioral analytics, the product team is flying blind on whether features are being used as designed. Pendo funnel data on the enrollment flow, for example, will reveal exactly where students abandon the plan enrollment process — enabling targeted UX improvements that increase completion rates without requiring a complete redesign guess.

Pendo for Institution Admin Adoption. The institution admin experience must also be instrumented to track: which admin features are used (and by which role), configuration completion rates (e.g., what percentage of institutions have fully completed plan template setup vs. leaving it partially configured), and guide/tooltip interaction rates. This data feeds directly into the NBS account management adoption metrics described above.

Why: Admin features that are technically available but behaviorally unused suggest either a UX problem or a training gap. Pendo data distinguishes between the two — if an admin visits a feature page but doesn't interact with it, that's a UX issue. If they never visit the page, that's a discoverability or training issue. Each has a different solution.

Pendo NPS & In-App Surveys. The platform should support periodic in-app NPS surveys to students (after plan enrollment, after first payment, at plan completion) and to admin users (after completing a key workflow). Survey data must be segmentable by institution, plan type, and user role. Target: NPS baseline established within 6 months of GA launch, with monthly tracking thereafter.

Why: NPS at key moments of truth (plan enrollment completion, payment success) directly measures whether Horizon is delivering the consumer experience quality that the product vision promises. Declining NPS in a specific segment is an early warning signal that a release degraded the experience for that group — before it shows up in support ticket volume or renewal risk.

Infrastructure & Application Health — Datadog

Datadog APM for Core Transactions. All critical transaction paths — payment processing, plan enrollment, ERP write-back, SSO authentication, webhook delivery — must be instrumented with Datadog APM traces. P50, P95, and P99 latency must be tracked per endpoint. Error rates must generate alerts at configurable thresholds. Traces must be retained for minimum 15 days for post-incident analysis.

Why: Payment processing failures are silent to the product team unless instrumented. A 3% payment failure rate may look like normal noise until you correlate it with a specific institution's ERP sync job timing. APM traces provide the correlation layer that turns noise into actionable signal.

Datadog Monitors for SLA-Critical Paths. Datadog monitors must be configured for: (1) Payment processing uptime <99.9% per rolling 30 days; (2) ERP sync lag > configured threshold per institution; (3) Webhook delivery failure rate >2% in any 1-hour window; (4) Consumer portal load time P95 >3 seconds; (5) Authentication failure rate spike (>3× baseline). Alerts must route to the on-call engineer via PagerDuty with severity classification and runbook links.

Why: These are the five most common failure modes in higher education payment platforms. Pre-configured monitors with runbooks mean that when a term-end payment surge degrades performance, the on-call engineer has a clear remediation path rather than starting diagnosis from scratch at 11pm during enrollment peak.

Datadog Log Management for Audit & Compliance. Application logs covering all payment transactions, ERP sync events, admin user actions, and security events (auth failures, permission escalations) must be shipped to Datadog Log Management with appropriate retention (90 days hot, 2 years cold via archive). Log ingestion must be structured (JSON) to support automated alerting and compliance query. PII must be masked in logs at the point of ingestion — student IDs may appear but full SSNs, card numbers, and bank account numbers must be redacted before log storage.

Why: Structured log management is the foundation of incident response, compliance audit support, and security investigation. Unstructured or incomplete logs turn a 2-hour incident investigation into a 2-day one. PII masking in logs is a data security requirement — log aggregation systems are a high-value exfiltration target and should not contain raw sensitive data.

Data Platform Health — MongoDB Atlas

Atlas Performance Advisor Monitoring. MongoDB Atlas Performance Advisor recommendations must be reviewed on a weekly cadence by the platform engineering team. Slow query alerts (queries exceeding configurable thresholds) must be routed to the engineering team via Datadog or direct Atlas alerting. Index utilization reports must inform quarterly index optimization reviews. Collection-level document count and storage growth must be tracked to anticipate capacity needs ahead of term-end peaks.

Why: Term-end enrollment creates predictable but dramatic spikes in read and write load on the data layer. Without proactive query and index optimization, these spikes manifest as application latency that students experience as a slow or failing enrollment flow — exactly when volume is highest. Performance Advisor turns reactive firefighting into proactive engineering.

Atlas Data Access Pattern Reporting. The product and data teams must have visibility into: which collections are accessed most frequently, which queries have the highest document scan counts (potential index gaps), and how data access patterns shift across the academic calendar. This data should feed into capacity planning for Atlas cluster tier selection and regional deployment decisions.

Why: Higher education has a highly seasonal access pattern — enrollment spikes in August/September and January are 5–10× off-peak load. Cluster tiering decisions made in the off-season without access pattern data result in either over-provisioning (wasted cost) or under-provisioning (degraded student experience at the worst possible time).

Delivery & Velocity Tracking — Azure DevOps

ADO Sprint Velocity & Throughput. The product and engineering teams must track sprint velocity (story points delivered per sprint), cycle time (time from work item active to closed), and lead time (time from work item created to closed) via ADO Analytics. These metrics must be reviewed in sprint retrospectives and trended over rolling quarters. Feature area breakdown (which product area is consuming most engineering capacity) should be visible at the portfolio level.

Why: Without velocity data, roadmap commitments to NBS leadership and to institutions are educated guesses. Trending velocity across sprints makes capacity planning a data-driven exercise and provides early signal when a team is overloaded before the overload becomes a missed delivery date.

ADO Feature Delivery Tracking vs. PRD. Each requirement section in this PRD should map to one or more ADO Epics/Features. The product team must maintain a living ADO query that shows: total PRD requirements, requirements with linked ADO work items, requirements in-sprint, requirements delivered, and requirements not yet scheduled. This PRD-to-delivery linkage is the primary tool for communicating product progress to NBS leadership.

Why: PRDs that are not linked to delivery artifacts become shelfware. Explicitly mapping this document's requirements to ADO work items creates accountability — every requirement is either in the backlog, scheduled, or explicitly deprioritized. It also enables the "N changes to review" experience documented elsewhere in this PRD to eventually drive from delivery data rather than manual changelog entries.

Bug Escape Rate & Defect Density. Engineering must track: bugs found in production vs. bugs found in QA (escape rate), defect density per feature area (bugs / story points delivered), and mean time to resolve production incidents by severity. These metrics must be visible to product and engineering leadership and reviewed monthly. A rising escape rate in a specific feature area is a signal to increase test coverage or review testing practices for that area.

Why: Payment and financial aid software has near-zero tolerance for production defects — a calculation error or incorrect payment application is not a UX annoyance, it's a financial harm to a student or institution. Tracking escape rate and defect density by feature area makes quality a first-class metric alongside velocity, rather than an afterthought discovered through client complaints.

Key Success Metrics — Product Outcomes

North Star Metric: Self-Service Resolution Rate. The product team should define and track a North Star metric for Horizon: the percentage of student financial obligations that are resolved (paid in full, enrolled in a plan, or otherwise actioned) via self-service in the consumer portal without institution staff or NBS intervention. Target: 75%+ self-service resolution rate within 12 months of institution go-live. This metric aggregates enrollment funnel completion, payment success rates, and authorized party setup to produce a single outcome measure.

Why: This is the metric that translates Horizon's consumer experience quality into institutional value (fewer support calls, faster collections) and NBS value (lower PAS cost per institution). All of the feature-level analytics described above are in service of moving this number.

Horizon Health Score. Product and account management should collaborate to define a composite Horizon Health Score per institution — a weighted combination of: self-service resolution rate (40%), payment plan enrollment rate (25%), payment success rate (20%), and admin login frequency/feature adoption (15%). The Health Score should be calculated monthly and integrated into the NBS Account Management dashboard described in the NBS Reporting section. Institutions with Health Score below a threshold should trigger an automatic AM review.

Why: Individual metrics can be gamed or can look fine in isolation while the overall client relationship is declining. A composite Health Score surfaces systemic issues — for example, an institution with a great payment success rate but terrible self-service rate is likely doing most of their processing manually, meaning Horizon is not delivering its core value proposition and the account is at renewal risk.
